Śrīnivāsa, a scholar of hardly twenty years of age could not grasp the true implications of the dream and hence consulted his *ācārya* Ghaṭikāśatam Varadācārya who asked him to obey the mandate. So, in the prime of his life, he wended his way to Ahobilam with a few followers. Bathing in the holy river Bhavanāśinī and after performing his *nityānuṣṭhāna*, the young Śrīnivāsa started meditating on Lord Nṛsiṁha. Then the Lord

[^80]: Ghaṭikāśatam Varadācārya - great grandson of Naḍādūr Ammāḷ (Vātsya Varadācārya) was known to be a prolific composer capable of composing a hundred verses in a *ghaṭikā* (Nāḻigai - 24 minutes). He was in charge of a *ghaṭikā* (centre of learning) in Kāñcī after his Ācārya, Brahma Tantra Svatantra Jīyar - I. The Ghaṭikā drew many illustrious learners. (*History of Śrīvaiṣṇavism in the Tamil Country - [Post-Rāmānuja]*, p.134.)
[]
appeared before him in the guise of an ascetic and Himself bestowed the robes of a *saṁnyāsin* on Śrīnivāsa,[^81] administered in his ears the *preṣamantra*, ordained him into the ascetic order, offered him the *tridaṇḍa* and called him Śrī Śaṭhakopa Jīyar. The Lord revealed to him His real Self and nominated him to be His Ārādhaka, thenceforth bestowed the *Śaṅkha* and *Cakra* from His Divine hands and made this clear command: "Worshipping me, go to villages and towns, grant aspirants the sacred symbols, *mantras* and their significance. Accept their surrender and proceed to sustain the way of Viśiṣṭādvaita as expounded by Āḻvārs, Rāmānuja and Vedāntadeśika."[^82] The Jīyar thus received the charter of Śrī Ahobila Maṭha from its progenitor Lord Nṛsiṁha Himself. This happened on the fifth day of the bright fortnight (*Śuklapakṣapañcamī*) *Puraṭṭāci* month, *Bahudhānya* year (in the *Śaka* year 1301), exactly on his twentieth birthday (*tīrunakṣatra*) – September 18, 1379 A.D. He stayed on in Ahobilam and started an organisation with a band of people possessing missionary zeal, called Ahobila Dāsaris who worked for the uplift of the hill tribes (*ceñcus*) living in and around Ahobilam.[^83] An idol of Lord

[^81]: *Śrī Sannidhiguruparamparā*, p. 21: अहॊबिलॆ श्रीनृसिंहः प्रॆषमन्त्रं स्वयं ददौ।
[^82]: *Śrī Sat Sampradāya Prakāśikā*, v. 8. ग्रामॆ ग्रामॆ च गत्वा पदकमलनतान् मां गृहीत्वाश्रियश्च।
[^83]: "Historical Evolution of Śrīvaiṣṇavism in South India" in *Cultural Heritage of India*, IV, p.182.
[]
Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha came into his hands through His grace.[^84] The nucleus of Śrī Ahobila Maṭha may be said to have been laid with his becoming the custodian of worship and ritual in the temple at Ahobilam.

Dream seems to have been the medium through which Lord Nṛsiṁha communicated with the Jīyar. He was asked to proceed to Āḻvār Tirunagari, the birth place of Nammāḻvār, on the banks of the Tāmraparṇi and pay obeisance to the Lord there. So, the Jīyar started his *divyadeśayātrā*, reached Āḻvār Tirunagari where, to his dismay, he found that it was named *Ekādaśarudra-kṣetra* (housing eleven *liṅgas*). The idol of Nammāḻvār was retrieved from a nearby tank[^85] by reciting the *Kaṇṇinuṇ Śiṟuttāmpu* (the *prabandha* by Madhurakavi Āḻvār). The local Śaivite Pāṇḍya king seems to have been converted to Śrīvaiṣṇavism and with his patronage, the idol of Nammāḻvār was consecrated and installed in the temple with due pomp and glory.[^86] Thereupon it is said that the presiding deity of Āḻvār Tirunagari

[^84]: Purisai Naḍādūr Krishnamacarya, *Ācārya Vaibhavam*, p. 232, Sri Viśiṣṭādvaita Research Centre.
[^85]: *Śrī Sannidhi Guru Paramparā - Satsampradāya Muktāvali*, p. 23 by Śrī Sathakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika, 33rd Jīyar of Sri Ahobila Maṭha. The idol of Nammāḻvār is said to have come up from the waters to answer the call of the Jīyar even as the idol of Selvapillai came towards Rāmānuja and sat on his lap in the palace of the Mohammedan King at Delhi.
[^86]: No dates are given in the *Śrī Sannidhi Guru Paramparā*, p.24. and also no name is given to the Pāṇḍya King. In 1400 A.D. or so, when this event happened the Pāṇḍya chiefs held sway over these parts of Tirunelveli district. From Robert Sewell's list of South Indian dynasties, we can cull out one Kulasekhara Pāṇḍya as the reigning chief.
[]
conferred on him the title Vaṇ (powerful) Śaṭhakopa and Nammāḻvār added the epithet Ādi (first). Henceforth the Jīyars have always had the prefix - "*Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa*". The Jīyar also built a shrine for Vedāntadeśika there. He received the *haṁsamudrā* from Nammāḻvār himself as a *pāritoṣika* (gift) for the services rendered by him. The *haṁsamudrā* remains even to this day, the official seal of the Ahobila Maṭha and is affixed in all correspondences of the Pontiffs. The Jīyars sign as "Śrī Śaṭhakopa Śrī" and the following are some of their titles: Śrīmad Vedamārga Pratiṣṭhāpanācārya Paramahaṁsa Parivrājakācārya, Sarvatantra Svatantra, Ubhayavedāntācārya, Śrī Bhagavad Rāmānuja Siddhāntanirdhāraṇa Sārvabhauma,[^87] etc. Even to this day the air resounds with this sound of these titles chanted aloud by the *śiṣyas* of Śrī Ahobila Maṭha wherever and whenever the Jīyar goes out in processions.

The Jīyar's services were commemorated by the local chief by the installation of the Jīyar's idol in a shrine built to the west of Nammāḻvār's shrine within the temple. The Jīyars of Śrī Ahobila Maṭha are entitled to the "*Mudal* (first) *Tīrtham*", "*Śrī Śaṭhāri*" and other respects due in the temple.

[^87]: Reference is made in a work entitled the *Padyaprāthamyavāda* (cf. p.241 of *Ācārya Vaibhavam*) to a dialogue through the medium of an *arcaka* that took place between Nammāḻvār and the Jīyar wherein the former is said to have cleared certain doubts of the latter. To cite a couple of doubts: (a) If *parokṣaśruti* and *pratyakṣarūpa bhagavadājñā* are opposed to each other, what has to be followed? (b) What is to be done if an individual has to perform an *aṅgin* opposed to the *aṅga* of his *varṇāśrama dharma*?
[]
The Jīyar then returned to Ahobilam and placed the *haṁsa-mudrā* at the feet of Lord Nṛsiṁha who blessed him and is said to have ordained him to be the tutelary head of the 74 *siṁhāsanādhipatis* nominated by Rāmānuja.[^88]

The incident in the Pāṇḍya king's life finds a parallel in the life of the King of Orissa, Mukunda Devarāya by name, who was driven out of his kingdom by the Mohammedans. He resorted to the feet of the Jīyar and with the latter's help was able to regain his lost kingdom. As a mark of gratitude and respect, King Mukunda Devarāya made a grant of *chattra, cāmara, bherī, mṛdaṅga*, elephants, horses and retinue to the Jīyar. He also ordered an artistic palanquin of ivory to be made for the Jīyar, in which he was taken out in procession. (This ivory palanquin is in vogue even today and after the *paṭṭābhiṣekam* of a new Jīyar, he is given the honour of being carried in this palanquin, in a procession.) Reference is made to this incident by the seventh

[^88]: These events are testified by the term "ஆழ்வார் தம் கிருபையாலான அறுபத்து நான்கு முத்திரை வாழ்வே" and the following *śloka* recited by the ancestors:
`श्रीरामानुजसम्प्रदायपदवीभाजं चतुस्सप्ततिः`
`श्रीमद्देश्यभवभृतां गुणभृतां सिंहासनस्वायिनाम्।`
`अध्यक्षत्वमुपेयिवांसमतुलं श्रीमन्नृसिंहाज्ञया`
`प्राज्ञं वण्शठकोपाख्यमुनिराजधुरीयमीडीमहि॥`
(*Śrī Sannidhi Guru Paramparā*, pp. 34-35).
[]
Jīyar of Śrī Ahobila Maṭha in his Sanskrit play, the *Vāsantikā Pariṇayam*, thus : [^89]

`पूर्वं यस्तु मुकुन्ददेवविभुनारून्धे धृतान्दोलिकः`
`प्राप्तः श्रीपुरुषोत्तमं रचितवान् भक्तप्रतिष्ठापनम्।`
`लब्ध्वा दन्ति तुरङ्ग छत्रचामरन्द्रादीनि यमौ पुनश्च विजयी कर्णाटसिंहासनम्॥`

The Jīyar then proceeded to Puruṣottamapurī (modern Pūrī) where he gave discourses on Rāmānuja-siddhānta and defeated many Advaita pandits in debates.[^90] Thus he was able to secure a large number of followers and ordered the installation of the images of Nammāḻvār and Rāmānuja in the temple at Pūrī.

[^89]: By Śaṭhakopa III, 7th Jīyar, ed. by Narasimha Sastri, pub. Vidyatarangini Press, Mysore, 1912 (Telugu characters).
[^90]: The Ahobilam Inscription of Śrīraṅga Rāya dated 1584-85 says that Śrī Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa Svāmi III, the 7th Jīyar of Śrī Ahobila Maṭha who had installed the idol of Śrīvaiṣṇava Āḻvār at Jagannath approached King Śrīraṅga Rāya and asked for the restoration of the District to its original condition by recovering it from Muslims. From the Inscription it seems that one Mukunda Harichandra of Orissa was a contemporary of this Jīyar. The idea of the installation of Āḻvār idols at Pūrī is corroborated by the play *Vāsantikā Pariṇayam* (see S. Krishnaswamy Iyengar, *Sources of Vijayanagar History*, pp. 233-234). This takes the 7th Jīyar to the end of the 16th century A.D. B.V. Rāmānujam believes in the contemporaneity of Ṣaṣṭha Parāṅkuśa (6th Jīyar) and Aliya Rāma Rāya and Sadāśiva Rāya on the strength of the *Satsampradāya Muktāvali*. As these arguments are fairly conclusive, the traditional dates assigned to some of the Jīyars may have to be post-dated. But S.N. Venkatesa Iyer has "thought it best to stick to the *Sri Sannidhi Guru Paramparā* as the safest course with our present imperfect knowledge of the times" (*History of Ahobila Maṭha*, p.19).
[]
The *Guruparamparā* then takes us from Orrisa to the capital of the Karnataka kingdom, presumably Vijayanagar, where the Jīyar stayed for sometime enjoying the patronage of the local king.[^91] It states that the Jīyar met one *Maṇalpākkam* Toḷappar who learnt all the *Śāstras* from the Jīyar. Impressed by Toḷappar's quick mastery of all *Śāstras*, the Jīyar asked him to write *dharma śāstra* digests for Śrīvaiṣṇavas. In accordance with the Jīyar's wish he wrote eight works - *Gṛhyaratnam, Kaṇṭhabhūṣaṇam, Smṛtiratnākara, Pitṛmedhasāra*, and its commentary *Sudhīvilocanam, Daśanirṇaya, Āśaucaśatakam*, and *Āśaucanirṇaya*. He was conferred the title of Vaidika Sārvabhauma by the Jīyar.

The Jīyar then toured Kumbhakoṇam, Śrīraṅgam and Āḻvār Tirunagarī doing *maṅgalāśāsana* to the deities in the *divyadeśas*, administering *pañcasaṁskāra* and accepting *śaraṇāgati* of the devotees, and finally he reached his birth-place, Tirunārāyaṇapuram (Melkote). There, two important events are said to have taken place: (a) The presence of a five-hooded serpent as one of the audience during *Śrībhāṣya-pravacana* of the Jīyar, and (b) the

[^91]: We are not given any details regarding the date or name of the King.
[]
installation of Vedāntadeśika's image in the temple precincts[^92] and the renovation of the temple Gopuram. The holy trinity of Śrīvaiṣṇavite worship and pilgrim centres: (a) the Periya Kovil at Śrīraṅgam, (b) Perumāḷ Kovil at Kāñcī and (c) Tiruvenkaṭam - Tirumala, must have demanded the Jīyar's attention. He ordered the construction of the *Sopāna* (steps) leading to Tirumalai Hill. Several rest houses and maṭhas were constructed on the wayside and arrangements were made for their maintenance. Evidence of the Jīyar's influence and of these permanent arrangements can be seen in the Tirumala Tirupati Inscriptions of 1516, 1546 and 1556 A.D. These Inscriptions along with the Ahobilam Inscriptions go to prove the Jīyar's organisational capabilities. Enough to say that the influence of the Maṭha at Tirumala abides to this day; such is the strength of the foundation laid by this Jīyar.

Then came the divine call from Kāñcī, the place of the Jīyar's early education. Here, he ordered the construction of a massive hundred-pillared *maṇṭapa* and a *kalyāṇamaṇṭapam* for seating the Lord Varadarāja and Perundevi Tāyār during *utsava* days. Evidence of this contribution can be

[^92]: Refer *Commemoration Volume* published on the occasion of the Silver Jubilee of the coronation of H.H. the 44th Aḻagiya Siṅgar. Śrī Rāmānuja is believed to have been the incarnation of Ādiśeṣa who appeared as a five-hooded serpent and nodded approval during the Jīyar's exposition of Śrī Rāmānuja's *Śrībhāṣya*. This led to the second event namely, the *punarnirmāṇa* of the gopuram at Tirunārāyaṇapuram and installation of Vedānta at Āḻvār Tirunagari.
[]
seen in a pillar of the *maṇṭapam*, wherein is sculptured Lord Nṛsiṁha and facing the Lord is sculptured Śrī Ādivaṇ Śaṭhakopa Svāmī in another pillar. He stayed for sometime here and gave discourses on *Grantha-catuṣṭayam* viz. the *Śrībhāṣya*, the *Gītābhāṣya*, the *Bhagavad-viṣayam* and the *Śrīmad Rahasyatrayasāra*. Here he chanced to meet Udayabhānumiśra, a rich Advaitin from Bengal. This meeting resulted in a challenge to the superiority of the rival systems. The discussions started as usual with the preliminary wager of the loser embracing the religion of the winner. The Jīyar took recourse to the *Śatadūṣaṇī* of Vedāntadeśika and defeated his opponent. Udayabhānumiśra surrendered at the Jīyar's feet and embraced Śrīvaiṣṇavism, had his *pañca-saṁskāra* at the Jīyar's hands and offered all his wealth at the Jīyar's feet. This wealth was utilised for the construction of buildings at Kāñ-ci and a separate temple for Vedāntadeśika, *maṇṭapas* etc. However, nothing more is heard of this Udayabhānumiśra.

The Jīyar then proceeded to Sholinghur expounding the philosophy of Rāmānuja. He met the grandfather of Doḍḍayācārya[^93] who learnt his lessons at the feet of this Jīyar. Pleased by the sincerity of his devotion, the Jīyar ordained him to take charge of the temple affairs at Sholinghur. It is a well

[^93]: Doḍḍayācārya alias Doḍḍa Aiyaṅgār Appan alias Śrīnivāsa alias Mahācārya lived perhaps in the 15th century A.D. Vide N. Jagadeesan, *History of Śrīvaiṣṇavism in the Tamil Country*, p. 26.
[]
known fact that the Doḍḍayācārya family, in keeping with the Jīyar's orders is entitled for "*mudal tīrtham*" and other temple honours till this day.

After worshipping Rāmānuja at Śrīperumbūdūr, the Jīyar proceeded to Śrīraṅgam. He was accorded a royal welcome with full temple honours, as a fitting climax, to half a century of strenuous toil of propagating the *sampradāya*. Here too, the Jīyar took upon himself the task of building the temple *prākāra*-walls (as was done in the past by Tirumaṅgai Āḻvār). In the northern entrance of Śrīraṅgam temple, he built a Maṭha and installed an image of Śrī Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha (and later the Jīyar's image was also installed). He also built a frontal *maṇṭapa* for the Daśāvatārasannidhi at the northern suburb of Śrīraṅgam beyond the temple walls and installed the image of Tirumaṅgai Āḻvār. The idol of Vedāntadeśika was also duly consecrated in front of the Śrīraṅganācciyār *sannidhi* inside the temple precincts, and arrangements were made for the daily worship there. In fact, the Jīyar himself stayed for sometime there and carried on the activities of the Maṭha. In the *Uttara* street at Śrīraṅgam, a big Maṭha was constructed (near the eastern gate of the temple) and Lord Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha was installed. Having thus given fixity and method to the Maṭha activities and arranged for its continuance, the Jīyar felt himself called upon to proceed to Melkote and perform worship of Lord Tirunārāyaṇa.
[]
Here at his birth place, he consecrated the image of Vedāntadeśika, built a Maṭha and personally attended to the rituals of worship. The Jīyar was at this time, advanced in age and felt that his end was approaching.

With his usual great care and foresight, he selected Nampākkam Kṛṣṇamācārya Svāmī, the 'Abhinava Vedāntadeśika' as his successor. He bequeathed the *saṁnyāsin*'s robes and performed *preṣamantropadeśa* to him and named him Śrī Nārāyaṇa Jīyar and installed him as the second pontiff of Śrī Ahobila Maṭha. When we recapitulate the achievements of the Jīyar who had founded a great Śrīvaiṣṇava Maṭha and who, through his ceaseless peregrinations spread Rāmānuja-darśana far and wide, taking innumerable *śiṣyas* within his solacing fold, one cannot but marvel at the intensity of his devotion, determination of purpose, and his great organisational capability, next only to Rāmānuja himself.

The first Jīyar breathed his last at Melkote on Saturday, 11th day (*Ekādaśī*) of dark fortnight (*kṛṣṇapakṣa*) of Caitra month, Bahudhānya year, Kaliyuga 4560 equating to April 1458 A.D. His Bṛndāvan is at Melkote on the banks of Kalyāṇī Puṣkariṇī, an object of reverential worship for his numerous followers. His praises are being duly sung in beautiful verses (*Aḻagiyasiṅgar Pugaḻ Mālai*).
[]
His Taniyans (composed by the second Jīyar) are read as under:

`प्रपद्ये निरवद्यानां निष्ठां गुणपदाम्पदाम्।`
`शरणं भवभीतानां शठकोपाख्यनीश्वरम्॥`
`केशवार्यकृपापात्रं श्रीशमादिगुणार्णवम्।`
`श्रीशठारियतीशानं देशिकेन्द्रमहं भजे॥`

#### The First Jīyar in Contemporary Literature and Epigraphical Records

The accounts gleaned from the *Guruparamparās* do not furnish us with any reliable chronological or historical data. But we have satisfactory evidence in contemporary liter- ature and epigraphs which help us fix the times of the Jīyars.

Ādivaṇ Śaṭhakopa Jīyar was the most revered scholar of his times. Many resorted to his feet for spiritual guidance. Maṇavāḷa Māmuṉi (1370-1443 A.D.) who is said to be an incarnation of Śrī Rāmānuja resorted to his feet and obtained *preṣamantropadeśa* and *saṁnyāsāśrama* from the first Jīyar. His other students were Yatirāja Jīyar, Śrīman Nārāyaṇa Jīyar, and Ācci Tiruveṅkaṭācārya.[^94]

The famous Telugu poet who adorned the court of King Kṛṣṇadevarāya of Vijayanagar, Allasāni Peddanna (1509-1530 A.D.) is said to

[^94]: Piṉbaḻagiya Perumāḷ Jīyar, *Āṟāyirappaṭi Guruparamparā-prabhāvam*, p. 597.
[]
have had his literary training under one Śaṭhakopa Yati.[^95] He refers to this in his works like the *Harikathāsāra* and the *Manucaritamu*. Of these the first is not extant now and only a few verses from it are quoted in the *Ānandaraṅgacampū*.[^96] He mentions in his *Manucaritamu* that Śaṭhakopa Yati was his *guru* and discribes him as an asylum of learning and dispeller of the darkness of ignorance through the moonlight of his kind looks.[^97] However, since Ādivaṇ Śaṭhakopa flourished between 1379-1458 A.D. and also since the period of Peddanna is accepted by many scholars to be between 1480-1533 A.D. it appears that the Śaṭhakopa he refers to could not have been the first Jīyar of Ahobila Maṭha. He is in all probability the seventh pontiff of the Maṭha whose pontificate is fixed approximately between 1513 and 1522 A.D.

The T.T.D. Epigraphical Report says that the famous music composer, *Tāḷlapākaṁ Annamācārya* (1424-1503 A. D.) was a contemporary of the first

[^95]: K.A. Nilakanta Sastri, *History of South India*, p. 412.
[^96]: Śaiva Krishnamurthy, *Peddanna's Concept of Poetry*, Introduction, p.8. शठकोपयतिकण्ठ ...
[^97]: Cf. Suryanarayana Sastri's edition of *Manucharitramu*, pp. 7-8 for a tribute to Śaṭhakopayati: कोल्लनुन् मद्गुरु विभव, निलमुन् करुणाकटक्ष निबिडज्योत्स्ना-दलितताश्रितजनदुरितच्छन्नगाढध्वान्तसमिति शठकोपयतिन्॥ He is also said to have obtained a village Kokaṭa (in Cuddapah District) as a gift from Emperor Kṛṣṇadevarāya. Critics say that he renamed it Śaṭhakopapura in honour of his *guru* and gave it away to Srivaiṣṇavas. Cf. *Peddanna's Concept of Poetry*, p. 8.
[]

Jīyar. The songs of this famous composer inscribed on copper plates were found hidden in the underground cellars of the upper Ahobilam temple.[^98] One song reads as follows:[^99]

`चुट्टिदि रकु सुलभमुड हरि तोडु नीड यगु दोरमुनि यितडु`
`केवल्यमुनकु गनक्य दापल म्रोवै द्रुतलकु दुदिपदमे`
`पावन म्रुक रूपमे विरजकु नावै युन्नाडिदे यितडु`
`कापाडग लोकमुल्लकु सुज्ञान दीपमे जगतिकि देजमे`
`पापालडपन भवपयोधिुलकु तेपै युन्नाडिदे वीतडु`
`कृपानिधिकि रंगापतिकि गाञ्चीवल्ल्कु वेकटगिरिपतिकि`
`निरतिनहोबल नृकेसरिकि तत्परुडगु शठकोपमुनि यितडु`

The Jīyar was a disciple of Nainārācārya the apostolic head from 1371 - 1410 A.D. Maṇavāḷa Māmuṉi (1370 - 1442 A.D.), Kaṇḍāḍai Rāmānuja Aiyaṅgār and the first, second and third Brahma Tantra Svatantra Jīyars of Parakāla Maṭha are said to have been the other contemporaries of the Jīyar.

Kaṇḍāḍai Rāmānuja Aiyaṅgār, a disciple of Aḻagiya Maṇavāḷa Jīyar and super- intendent of the free feeding house (Rāmānuja Kūṭam) at Tirumala

[^98]: S.K. Sarasvathi, "Art and Architecture in Vijayanagar", *Epigraphical Report*, p. 280.
[^99]: "Behold! this is our revered Śaṭhakopa Muni who is easily accessible to all and to whom Lord Hari Himself is the guide and refuge! He is our golden path for final beatitude, the last word in scriptures, the soul pure and free from sin and the boat with which to cross the Virajā river. He is the divine lamp of wisdom illuminating all the worlds, the redeemer of sins and the raft which enables us to cross this ocean of *saṁsāra*. He is an ardent devotee of the presiding deities of Śrīraṅgam, Kāñcī, Veṅkaṭādri and Ahobilam and is a prince among ascetics!"
[]
is mentioned in some Inscriptions.[^100] This enables us to fix the date of the Jīyar in the second half of the 15th century A.D. Two other Inscriptions mentioning this Kaṇḍāḍai Rāmānuja Aiyaṅgār are found at Śrī Raṅganātha temple, Śrīraṅgam.[^101] They mention one Kaṇḍāḍai Mādhava Aiyaṅgār as his disciple.

The first three Brahmatantra Svatantra Jīyars had been the heads of the Parakāla Maṭha. The date of the *āsthāna* of the first Jīyar is from 1364 - 1386 A.D.[^102] As per the Kāñcī Inscription dated in Śaka 1282 (29th March 1360 A.D.) he was the pontiff of the Maṭha.[^103] He was a direct disciple of Vedāntadeśika and Nainārācārya along with the first Jīyar of Ahobila Maṭha.

Sāḷuva Narasiṁha was a feudal king of Chandragiri who later extended his control over North Arcot, South Arcot and Chingleput districts, and finally usurped the throne of Vijayanagar.[^104] He is said to have installed the

[^100]: T. T. D. *Inscriptions* Vol. I Serial No. 4 of Śaka 1378 (corresponding to 12th September 1456 A.D.) and No. 23 dated Śaka 1387 (corresponding to 14th April 1465 A.D.) of Sāḷuva Narasiṁha's regime.
[^101]: A.R. 92 - 1936 - 37 (South Indian Inscription XXIV, No: 357, 355) and A.R. 41 1938 - 39 p. 363 and dated Śaka 1422 (1500 A.D.).
[^102]: See the succession list of the pontiffs of Śrī Brahma Tantra Svatantra Prakāla Maṭha - "The origin and History of Parakāla Maṭha" by K. Desikachary, p. 23.
[^103]: A.R. 318 / 1909.
[^104]: T.T.D. *Inscriptions*, Vol II, s.no.82 (G.T. No. 272), p. 151.
[]
image of Lord Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha on the pathway to Śeṣādri. A few other Inscriptions are found to relate to the period of the first Jīyar.

An Inscription[^105] on a slab set up in a garden near Āḻvār Cheruvu (tank) in Tirupati, Chittoor District, refers to the building of Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha Maṇṭapa and laying out of a flower garden. It is dated in Śaka 1326 (1404 A.D.). It may be the Vaṇ Śaṭhakopan Nandavanam mentioned in a T.T.D. Inscription.

The second Inscription[^106] in Tamil on the western wall of the second *prākāra* in the Tirumala temple is the record of a *śilāśāsana* which contains among other things a provision that the balance of offerings be made to Aḻagiya Śiṅgar, his Ācārya, Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa Jīyar. This is dated Śaka 1415 (15th June 1493 A.D.) when Sāḷuva Narasiṁha was ruling Vijayanagar. The above Inscription is particularly important for two things: The Jīyar was called Aḻagiya Śiṅgar and a disciple had endowed to perpetuate the memory of his Ācārya.

The third Inscription dated Śaka 1407 (6th June 1485 A.D.) records the execution of a *śilāśāsana*. It gives the information that Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa Jīyar constructed the entrance of the Vasanta Maṇṭapa with stone through the

[^105]: T.T.D. *Inscriptions*, Vol I, p. 457 and A.R. 258 - 1904.
[^106]: Ibid. Vol. II, No. 70.
[]
utilisation of the income of Tiruviḍaiyāṭṭam (village) Pūṅgōḍu but left the stone roof over the *maṇṭapa* unfinished. The *narpaṇam* of 2000 *panams* which the donor paid was to cover the value of verandah work. It also details the festivals when the processional deities shall be taken to this *maṇṭapa*. As S.K. Iyengar observes, this Inscription proves the first Jīyar's activity in Tirupati, the construction of a *maṇṭapa*, the establishment of his reputation as an Ācārya and the building up of a devoted following in the temple town.

We also hear of Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa Maṇṭapa in two other Inscriptions, one occuring at Tirumala[^107] dated Śaka 1427 (1.3.1505 A.D.) and one dated Śaka 1429 (4th October 1508 A.D.).[^108] K.V. Raman refers to an Inscription in Kāñcī Varadarāja temple dated Śaka 1431 (1509 A.D.) mentioning the gift of a land in a village Vaṇ Śaṭhakopapuram, named evidently after the first Jīyar.[^109]

An Inscription in Kāñcī Varadarāja Temple dated 14.1.1517 A.D. mentions that King Kṛṣṇadevarāya visited Kāñcī in the course of his conquests, worshipped Lord Varadarāja and donated 1000 *varāhas* and granted certain villages for provisions of offerrings to the deity with the stipulation that the balance of offerings be utilised for distribution among the disciples of Śaṭhakopa Jīyar. This shows that the first Jīyar had established a

[^107]: T.T.D. *Inscriptions*. Vol II, No: 276.
[^108]: Ibid Vol II, No. 11.
[^109]: Ibid. 411.(1919)
[]
Maṭha at Kāñcī and that his name was held in high esteem by King Kṛṣṇadevarāya. The Inscription[^110] in the Govindarāja temple in Tirupati dated Śaka 1450 (November 1528 A.D.) mentions a *nandavana* (flower garden) called Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa Nandavanam.

Two Inscriptions are found in Śrī Raṅganāthasvāmī temple, Śrīraṅgam. They mention King Kṛṣṇadevarāya's visit to Śrīraṅgam and a provision for the distribution of a share of offerings to the disciples of Śaṭhakopa Jīyar Maṭha at Śrīraṅgam. All these are unmistakable attestations to the fame and popularity of the first Jīyar of Ahobila Maṭha.

The history of the Ācāryas of the Ahobila Maṭha who succeeded Śrī Ādi Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa Svāmī is dealt with in the following pages. Lord Nṛsiṁha is referred to in Tamil as "Aḻagiya Śiṅgam" or "the Beautiful Lion". As a natural corollary, the Ācāryas of Śrī Ahobila Maṭha who propogated the worship of Lord Nṛsiṁha are referred to as "Aḻagiya Śiṅgars".

**2. Śrī Nārāyaṇa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

Tirumalai Nampākkam Kṛṣṇamācārya, one of the disciples of the first Jīyar, succeeded him in the pontificate on the fifth lunar day of the bright half of Caitra in the year Bahudhānya in Kaliyuga 4560 (corresponding to Friday,

[^110]: T.T.D. *Inscriptions*, Vol III, G.T. No. 275.
[]
9th April 1458 A.D.). He was born in the Tamil month Āvaṇi under star Jyeṣṭhā. He was an erudite scholar and was the author of several works in his *pūrvāśrama*. He is well known as the "author of sixty works" (*Ṣaṣṭi-prabandhanirmātā*).[^111] Chief among his works are the *Īśāvāsyopaniṣad vyākhyā, Puruṣārthasudhānidhi, Rahasyatrayajīvāttu, Rahasyatrayavicāra, Tiruvārādhanakrama, Nyāsadaśakavyākhyā, Yajus-sandhyāvandana-bhāṣya* and *Nyāsaviṁśativyākhyā*. He is also known as "Abhinava Vedāntadeśika." The *Śrī Sannidhi Guruparamparā* ascribes the *Puruṣakāra-mīmāṁsā*, to this Jīyar.[^112]

This Jīyar presided over the Maṭha for a period of fourteen years. He established an *agrahāram* at Madhuramaṅgalam. He installed an image of his Ācārya Śrī Ādi Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa Jīyar in the temple at Melkote (Tirunārāyaṇapuram) and another in the Svāmī's Bṛndāvanam at Melkote.

[^111]: V.K.S.N. Raghavan, *History of Viśiṣṭādvaita Literature*, Ajanta Publications, 1979. pp. 54-55.
[^112]: *Śrī Sannidhi Guruparamparā*, pp. 49-50. It is a treatise on the principles of mediation required for salvation. It was in two parts viz. *pūrvapakṣa* and *siddhānta*. It is said that some scholars, for reasons not disclosed, took away the *siddhānta* portion and kept it out of circulation. Further, it is stated that the elder Vedānta Rāmānuja Svāmi learnt the *siddhānta* portion of it from his Ācārya and later wrote works like *Śrītatvasiddhāñjana* based on this treatise. But recent researches have identified the author of this work as the fourteenth Jīyar.
[]
During his pontificate, the Jīyar travelled throughout South India. He visited Śrīraṅgam, Śrīmuṣṇam, Tiruvahīndrapuram, Tirukkōvalūr, Kāñcī and its eighteen satellite *divyadeśas*, and proceeded *via* Colasiṁhapuram and Tirumala, to Ahobilam. He spent the rest of his life giving discourses to his devotees on the Śrīvaiṣṇava religion and philosophy.

He attained Ācāryan Tiruvaḍi (liberation) at Tirunārāyaṇapuram in the year Nandana, in the Tamil month of Panguni, on Kṛṣṇapakṣa Dvitīyā tithi (March 1473). His Bṛndāvanam is located at Kalyāṇī Tīrtha at Melkote, beside that of his Ācārya.

His Taniyan reads as follows:-

`श्रीशठारियतीशानपदपङ्कजषट्पदम्।`
`श्रीमन्नारायणमुनिं श्रये श्रीभाष्यदेशिकम्॥`

#### The Second Jīyar in Epigraphical Records

The second Jīyar appears in a few Inscriptions and these help us to fix his chronology. Two Tirupati Inscriptions[^113] falling within the reign of Kṛṣṇadevarāya give him a specific date. One of these occurring in the Govindarāja shrine in Lower Tirupati is a benefaction for the first Jīyar on his birthday (*Puraṭṭāsi-Keṭṭai*) the donor being Nārāyaṇa Jīyar himself. It is in both Tamil and Grantha. Therein, provision was made for five food services

[^113]: T.T.D. *Inscriptions*, Vol. III No. 110 (60 of G.T.) and 114 (160 of G.T.) p. 240.
[]
during the *adhyayana utsava*, performed for the Lord of Seven Hills and for thirteen other services on the monthly star of his Ācārya.[^114]

The other Inscription[^115] dated Śaka 1438 (7th November 1516 A.D.) refers to the deposit of 3800 *panams* to be invested for the improvement of irrigation sources and the interest income thereof to be utilised for daily services in the Govindarāja temple. These Inscriptions show that the second Jīyar took certain steps to perpetuate the memory of his illustrious Ācārya by instituting services in his memory in the famous shrines at Tirupathi and Śrīraṅgam and popularising his Maṭha and carrying forward the work of propagation of Rāmānuja-darśana.

A third Inscription[^116] pertaining to this Jīyar is found in the South wall of the central shrine of Periyāḻvār temple at Alipiri. It records the execution of a *Śilāśāsana* in favour of the disciples of Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa Jīyar for providing a certain offering in the Jīyar's *nandavana* (flower garden).

Regarding the date 1516 A.D., S.K Aiyangar[^117] observes: "It is not given by way of a mere indirect reference but is the date of an actual record

[^114]: A similar provision for taking out the deity at Śrīraṅgam on Jyeṣṭhā asterism day was made by Kṛṣṇadevarāya during his visit to Śrīraṅgam in 1517 A.D.
[^115]: T.T.D. *Inscriptions*, Vol. III. No. 114, p. 240.
[^116]: Ibid. No. 178, pp. 364-65.
[^117]: *History of Tirupati*, Vol. II, p. 175.
[]
made by the Svāmī himself and must have been put on record necessarily under his orders and it may even be under his supervision and hence could not be brushed aside." K.V. Raman[^118] says that Nārāyaṇa Jīyar lived almost to the end of Kṛṣṇadevarāya's reign (1500-1529 A.D.).

If we are to accept these dates occuring in the Inscription as falling within the pontificate of Nārāyaṇa Jīyar, it is necessary to make an adjustment by putting up the dates of the Jīyars by about sixty years.[^119] The dates assigned to the Jīyars of Ahobila Maṭha are based on dates provided by the *Śrī Sannidhi Guruparamparā*. These dates, though disputed, are still given so that there may be a general chronological background for an account of the Jīyars.

**3. Śrī Parāṅkuśa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Jīyar was born in Malayāṅkuḷam agrahāram in the Kāñcīpuram District in the Tamil month of Thai under the asterism of Śravaṇa. His *pūrvāśrama* name was Kaṇḍāḍai Kṛṣṇayajvā, indicating that the Svāmī performed many *yāgas*. He assumed the office of pontificate on a full-moon day in Nandana year in the Tamil month of Paṅguni, corresponding to March 1473.

[^118]: *Varadarājasvāmī Temple at Kāñcī*, p.70
[^119]: V.S. Seshadri, *History of Vaiṣṇavism from Vedic Times to the end of 16th century A.D.*, p. 263.
[]
He ably carried forward the work of his two illustrious predecessors. He proceeded from Tirunārāyaṇapuram to Kāñcī where he performed *maṅgalāśāsana* to Lord Varadarāja and Perundevi Tāyār. He gave religious and philosophic discourses to learned scholars on the *Śrībhāṣya* and other texts.

He established *agrahārams* at Nīrvalūr, Uragadam, Nimmili, Kāḍaṅgarai and Kaḷattūr. Then he proceeded to Tirukkōvalūr, Tiruvahin-drapuram, Śrīmuṣṇam and Śrīraṅgam. He stayed for sometime at Śrīraṅgam giving discourses on *Grantha-catuṣṭayam*. At the divine command of Rāmānuja he proceeded to Śrīmuṣṇam to worship the Lord Bhūvarāha. Having spent a worthwhile life, full of service to his *pūrvācāryas* and Lord Nṛsiṁha, the Svāmī attained Ācāryan Tiruvaḍi in the Tamil Month of Thai, Krodhi year (January 1485) on Kṛṣṇapakṣa caturdaśī. His Bṛndāvanam is at Śrīmuṣṇam. He occupied the pontificate for eleven years and ten months.

His Taniyan reads as follows:

`श्रीमन्नाराणमुनेः पदपङ्कजषट्पदम्।`
`पराङ्कुशमुनिं सम्यग् पराङ्कुशमुनिं भजे॥`

**4. Śrī Śrīnivāsa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Jīyar was born in the Tamil Month of Mārgaḻi under the star Citrā. He assumed office in the Tamil Month of Thai in the Krodhi year corresponding to January 1485 at Śrīmuṣṇam.
[]
This svāmī proceeded on his religous tours (*sañcāra*) from Śrīmuṣṇam to Śiṅgarkoil where he gave discourses on Ubhayavedānta texts. He then left for North India via Ahobila to Dvārakā, Gokulam, Mathurā, Avantī(Ujjain) and Ayodhyā and returned to Śiṅgarkoil via Kāñcī. Due to his failing health this Svāmī prayed to Lord Nṛsiṁha to relieve him of his mortal frame, after appointing a suitable successor. Complying to the Svāmī's fervent prayer, Lord Nṛsiṁha appeared in the dream of a certain scholar (who was called "*Sarvatantrasvatantra*" in due recognition of his knowledge of all *śāstras*) and commanded him to proceed to Śiṅgarkoil to don the ochre robes. Accordingly, he proceeded to the Ahobila Maṭha at Śiṅgarkoil where the divine command was intimated to the Jīyar. It was thus that the fifth Jīyar[^120] was initiated into asceticism with the title of "*Sarvatantra svatantra Śaṭhakopa Jīyar*". Subsequently, the elder Svāmī attained *paramapada* in the Tamil month of Citra in the year Pramādica on Kṛṣṇapakṣa caturthī (April

[^120]: V.S. Seshadri, *History of Vaiṣṇavism from Vedic Times to the end of 16th Century A.D.*, p. 264: "When the Jiyar found that the Śrīvaiṣṇavasvāmī was of Teṅgalai sect he wanted to admit him into the Vaḍakalai fold, but the latter was not willing for a second initiation. The Jiyar having no other option, admitted him into the ascetic order and nominated him as the next pontiff, with the stipulation that the practices pertaining to both the traditions be followed in the Maṭha". However, no such reference is found in the *Śrī Sannidhi Guruparamparā*. According to T.A. Swaminatha Aiyar (*Ācārya Carittira Mālā* - Appendix), the first eleven chiefs of the Maṭha (Parakāla Maṭha) were subject to Śrī Ahobila Maṭha because the Parakāla Maṭha tradition includes the recitation of certain Taniyans peculiar to the Ahobila Maṭha. See N. Jagadeesan, *History of Śrīvaiṣṇavism in the Tamil Country (Post-Rāmānuja)*, p.159.
[]
1493). His Bṛndāvanam is at Śiṅgarkoil and he was in the pontificate for eight years and three months (1485-1493 A.D.).

His Taniyan reads as follows:-

`श्रीपराङ्कुशयोगीन्द्रचरणाम्बुजषट्पदम्।`
`श्रीनिवासमुनिं वन्दे श्रीभाष्यमृतसागरम्॥`

**5. *Kaṇḍalūr* Śrī Sarvatantrasvatantra Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Jīyar was born in the Tamil month of Kārtigai under the star Kṛttikā in Ātreya Gotra. He assumed the pontificate in the year Pramādica in Citra month (April 1493) on Kṛṣṇapakṣa dvitīyā tithi.

An erudite scholar, well-borne out by his title "*Sarvatantrasvatantra*", his discourses on religion and philosophy were most sought after by the Śrīvaiṣṇava community. He visited Śrīraṅgam and Tirumala, propagating *Rāmānuja-darśana* and proceeded to the North. He attained Ācāryan Tiruvaḍi in the year Kālayukti in the month of Thai (January 1499) on Kṛṣṇapakṣa navamī Tithi, on the banks of river Kṛṣṇā. His Bṛndāvanam is also situated there. He ruled over the pontificate for five years and nine months (1493 - 1499).[^121]

[^121]: The *Śrī Sannidhi Guruparamparā* mentions that upto the period of this Jīyar there was cordial inter-mingling between the *Vaḍakalai* and *Teṅgalai* sects of the Śrīvaiṣṇava community. P.B. Aṇṇaṅgarācāryar, in his *History of Rāmānuja Darśanam*, p. 34 holds that the Ahobila Maṭha originally followed the *Teṅgalai* tradition but was later on converted to *Vaḍakalai* tradition.
[]
His Taniyan reads as follows:

`श्रीनृसिंहदयापात्रं परवादिगजाह्वयम्।`
`सर्वतन्त्रस्वतन्त्रायं शठकोपमुनिं भजे॥`

***Epigraphical Records***

The T.T.D. Epigraphical Report mentions one Vedānta Śaṭhakopa Jīyar as the fifth pontiff who presided over the Ahobila Maṭha during the reign of Sadāśivarāya.

From the two Inscriptions in Lower Tirupati[^122] we understand that the Jīyar was the spiritual *guru* of the Nandyala royal family. This information is also contained in two other Inscriptions[^123] wherein it is stipulated that the donor's share of the offering (*prasāda*), be made over to their Ācārya.

The T.T.D. Epigraphical Report also states, "this is the same Vedānta Śaṭhakopa Jīyar who regained for Gajapati king, Mukunda Devarāya, his lost kingdom."

**6. Śrī Ṣaṣṭha Parāṅkuśa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Jīyar was born in the Tamil month of Thai under star Pūraṭṭādi in Karalappākkam village near Tiruvaḷḷūr in Bharadvāja Gotra. In his *pūrvāśrama* days, he was well-known in literary circles as Vidvān Vaṅgīpuram Veṅkaṭācārya Svāmī.

[^122]: T.T.D. *Inscriptions*, Vol. VII, p. 278.
[^123]: Ibid. No. 65 and No. 122.
[]
Pañcamatabhañjanam Tātācārya[^124] of Kāñcī was his cousin. He received the Pañca- saṁskāra at the hands of Ṣaṣṭha Parāṅkuśa Jīyar. He was appointed as the Śrīkāryam (Secretary) of the Ahobila Maṭha to look after administrative and financial matters of the Maṭha.

This Jīyar was a famous personage of his times. Being well grounded in Jñāna and Anuṣṭhāna, he had a large number of followers and many resorted to His Holy Feet for *pañcasaṁskāra* and *prapatti*.

Ṣaṣṭha Parāṅkuśa was a contemporary of King Sadāśiva Rāya according to the *Śrī Sannidhi Guruparamparā*. It is stated that the Jīyar with his superhuman[^125] powers was able to cure the daughter of the King from the evil effects of certain spirits. As a mark of respect, the King visited Ahobilam and paid obeisance to the Lord and the Jīyar. He also gifted the village of Śrī Bhāṣyapuram on the banks of river Pinākinī. The royal patronage was one of the causes for the Ahobila Maṭha gaining in prominence and prosperity during this period.

[^124]: He later became famous as the royal preceptor of Sadāśiva. His son is the more famous Koṭikanyakādānam Tātācārya. The Tātācāryas trace their origin to Periya Nambi who administered *pañcasaṁskāra* to Rāmānuja. They belong to the Śāṭamarṣaṇa Gotra. According to S.K. Iyengar, they belonged to Toḷappar family (*History of Tirupati*, Vol II, p. 277).
[^125]: *Ācārya Vaibhavam*, p. 274, Śrī Viśiṣṭādvaita Research Centre, 1992. See also "The Hindu" 13th November, 1966.
[]
The Jīyar proceeded in his religious tour to North India. He visited Badarī[^126] and then returned via Tirumala to South India. He visited Madhuramaṅgalam, Nīrvalūr, Iñjimeḍu, Kaḷathūr, Uragaḍam and Kāñcī and then proceeded to Ahobilam. During his pontificate, the Maṭha became a wealthy and powerful institution. The Jīyar himself enjoyed the status of a *rājasaṁnyāsī* and was provided with a paraphernalia consisting of elephants, horses, guards, etc., The Jīyar was assisted in his pontifical duties by one Rāmānuja Aiyaṅgār, who was his *Mudrādhikārī*. The *Śrī Sannidhi Guruparamparā* states that this Jīyar had a divine call from Jvālā Nṛsiṁha to worship the Lord permanently in His cave. Hence at the Lord's command he initiated Iḷaṅkāḍu Kavisārvabhauma Śikhāmaṇi into asceticism and appointed him as his successor and entered the Holy cave in Aṅgirasa year, Māsi month, Kṛṣṇapakṣa pañcamī tithi (February 1513).[^127] It is stated that the Jīyar has authored the following works - *Siddhānta Maṇi Dīpa, Pañcakāla Dīpikā, Prapatti Prayoga*, and *Nṛsiṁha Stava*. He ruled the pontificate for fourteen years and one month from January 1499 to February 1513.

[^126]: Ibid. p. 275.
[^127]: *Śrī Sannidhi Guruparamparā*, p. 58, states that the Śrī Kāryam Svāmī, who came to know of this later, came to Ahobilam and tearfully prayed for a final *darśan* of the Svāmi. The Svāmī appeared outside the cave, consoled the Śrīkāryam Svāmī, blessed him and then entered the cave, never to return. (Cf. *Ācārya Vaibhavam*, p. 276).
[]
His Taniyan reads as follows:

`श्रीमच्छठारिमुनिपादसरोरुहंसं श्रीमत्पराङ्कुशपयोधनलब्धबोधम्।`
`श्रीमन्नृसिंहवरदं पदमावदान्तं श्रीमत्पराङ्कुशमुनिं प्रणतोऽस्मि नित्यम्॥`

***Epigraphical Records***

Fortunately, Parāṅkuśa II is mentioned in many Inscriptions, which help us to fix his chronology.

Of the twenty-three Inscriptions[^128] at Lower Ahobilam, thirteen fall within the period of King Acyuta Rāya and King Sadāśiva Rāya (1513-1564 A.D.). Six Inscriptions[^129] at Upper Ahobilam belong to King Sadāśiva Rāya's era (1548-1564 A.D.). Parāṅkuśa Jīyar is specifically referred to in three Inscriptions at Lower Ahobilam[^130] and two at Upper Ahobilam.[^131] Mention is made of him in two Inscriptions[^132] as the Trustee of the Ahobilam Temple. The Inscriptions at Lower Ahobilam bear the dates in Śaka 1472 (1550 A.D.) and Śaka 1477 (1555 A.D.). Those at Upper Ahobilam are dated in Śaka 1480 (1558 A.D.) and Śaka 1476 (1564 A.D.). Thus we find that the pontificate of Parāṅkuśa Jīyar II falls between 1550 A.D. and 1564 A.D. and entirely within the reign of King Sadāśiva Rāya. K.V. Raman refers to two

[^128]: A.R. No: 55, 56, 58, 59, 60, 61, 63, 65, 66, 69, 72, 73 and 75, all of 1915 A.D.
[^129]: Ibid. 78-81 and 87 of 1915.
[^130]: Ibid. 65, 73-75 of 1915.
[^131]: Ibid. 79 and 82 of 1915.
[^132]: Ibid. 65 and 75 of 1915.
[]
inscriptions[^133] at Kāñcī which speak of the association of Parāṅkuśa Jīyar II, with the Varadarāja Temple.

Śrī Vāhinipati, the poet-laureate, has praised this Jīyar in his *Guruparamparā Pāramārśa* wherein he refers to the Jīyar as the foremost among Saṁnyāsins, second only to Ādiśeṣa, third behind Bṛhaspati and Śukra, and fourth behind the Holy Trinity, viz. Śiva, Viṣṇu and Brahmā.[^134] Ātreya Ahobila Guru praises the Jīyar as a *Sarvatantrasvatantra* in his work, *Periya Vāccāṉ Piḷḷai's Rāmāyaṇa Pratyeka Śloka Vistaraṇam*. He also eulogises the Jīyar for installing the images of Āḻvārs in many places.

**7. Śrī Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Jīyar was born in Iḷaṅgāḍu (*agrahāram*) village in Kāñcī District in Bhāradvāja Gotra in the Tamil month of Vaikāśi under star Viśākhā. He assumed the office of pontificate in the Tamil month of Māsi in Āṅgirasa year ( February, 1513) in his twenty-fifth year. He visited many holy shrines from Ahobilam to Rāmeśvaram. Because of his erudition, he was honoured with the titles of "*Śatalekhinī lekhānuguṇa kavitā dhuranthara, kavitārkika kaṇṭhīrava*". He wrote a five-act drama in Sanskrit titled "*Vāsantikā-

[^133]: K.V. Raman, *Varadarāja Svāmī Temple at Kāñcī*, p. 80.
[^134]: *Vedānta Dīpikā*, 1923 October issue, p. 17. Article titled *Gurparampard Paramarśam*. Cf. V.S. Seshadri, *History of Vaiṣṇavism from Vedic Times to the End of 16th Century A.D.* p. 268.
[]
*Pariṇayam*".[^135] He installed the images of Āḻvārs and Ācāryas in the Pūrī temple which he visited. The Inscription at Lower Ahobilam mentions the restoration of the temple-custody to the Jīyar of Ahobila Maṭha after the invaders were driven away by King Śrīraṅgarāya.

The Jīyar visited many *divyadeśas* including Tirumala, Kāñcī, Śrīraṅgam, Tirunārāyaṇapuram, Kumbhakoṇam, Āḻvār Tirunagari and stayed at Śrīraṅgam giving religious discourses. He attained Ācāryan Tiruvaḍi in the year Viṣu, in the Tamil month of Paṅguni on a pūrṇimā day at Śrīraṅgam (April, 1522). He ruled the pontificate for nine years and two months (1513-1522). His Bṛndāvanam is at Śrīraṅgam.

His Taniyan reads as follows:

`श्रीपराङ्कुशयोगीन्द्रचरणाम्बुजसेखरम्।`
`समस्तशास्त्रपारीणं शठकोपमुनिं भजे॥`

**8. Śrī Parāṅkuśa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Jīyar was born in the Tamil month of Mārgaḻi under star Aśvinī. He was initiated into the ascetic order by his *pūrvācārya* and he took charge as the spiritual head of the Ahobila Maṭha in the Viṣu year, in the month of Paṅguni (April 1522) on a Śukla ekādaśī day. He stayed at Śrīraṅgam for the rest of his life, giving discourses on religious and the philosophical texts like

[^135]: The theme of the drama is the marriage of Lord Nṛsiṁha with Ceñcu Lakṣmī daughter of the chieftain of the hill tribes.
[]
the *Śrībhāṣya, Bhagavad Viṣayam* and *Śrutaprakāśikā*, and worshipping Lord Raṅganātha. He attained *paramapada* in the year Heviḷambi in the month of Mārgaḻi (January, 1538) on a Kṛṣṇapakṣa pañcamī tithi. He ruled over the pontificate for fifteen years and nine months (1522-1538).

His Taniyan reads as follows:

`शठकोपयतिनेत्रद्वयपदपङ्कजषट्पदम्।`
`सर्वशास्त्रार्थतत्त्वज्ञं पराङ्कुशमुनिं भजे॥`

**9. Śrīman Nārāyaṇa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in the month of Āni under star Tiruvādirai. He became the pontifical head in the year Heviḷambi, in Mārgaḻi month, on a pūrṇimā day (January 1538) at Śrīraṅgam.

This Jīyar stayed at Śrīraṅgam for sometime and then proceeded to Kumbhakoṇam to offer worship to Lord Ārāvamudan. He stayed there for sometime and is said to have developed the temple premises by constructing *maṇṭapas*. Then he proceeded to Śrīmuṣṇam, Tirukkōvalūr, Kāñcī, Tirumala and then to Ahobilam where he is said to have offered worship at all the nine Nṛsiṁha shrines. He took up the task of constructing *maṇṭapas*, buildings steps leading to the shrines at Ahobilam, and dedicating his life to Lord Nṛsiṁha's worship. He attained *paramapada* in the month of Āni in the year Subhakṛt (July 1542) on Kṛṣṇa caturthī. His Bṛndāvanam is at Ahobilam. He ruled the pontificate for four years and six months (1538 - 1542).
[]
His Taniyan reads as follows:

`श्रीमन्नृसिंहवरदपराङ्कुशकृपात्रम्।`
`श्रीमन्नारायणमुनिं वन्दे श्रीभाष्यदेशिकम्॥`

**10. Śrī Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Jīyar was born in the month of Vaikāsi under star Viśākā. He assumed the office of pontificate in the year Subhakṛt, Āni month (July 1542) on Kṛṣṇa pakṣa tṛtīyā tithi.

He set out on his religious tours (*divyadeśasañcāra*) visiting Tirumala, Kāñcī, Śrīperumbūdūr, Tiruvallikkeṇi, Tiruviṇḍantai, Tirunirmalai, Tirucci-ttirakūṭam totalling nearly forty-two holy shrines. He then left for Tirunārāyaṇapuram at the instance of the Lord, and stayed there till the end of his life. He left for his heavenly abode in the year Siddhārthi, in the month of Āni on Kṛṣṇadvādaśī (July 1559). He ruled over the pontificate for seventeen years (1542 - 1559).

His Taniyan reads as under:

`वरदार्यगुरुस्तंबवणाब्जषट्पदम्।`
`शठकोपमुनिं वन्दे शठारिप्रवणं सदा॥`

**11. Śrī Śrīnivāsa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in Vaṅgīpuram village in Tiruvaḷḷūr in Bhāradvāja Gotra in the month of Aippaśi under star Mūlam. He assumed
[]
the office of pontificate in Āni month, Siddhārthi year (July 1559) at Tirunārāyaṇapuram.

He visited the holy shrines at Tirumala, Tiruvaḷḷūr, Kāñcī and Śrīraṅgam. He stayed for sometime at Śrīraṅgam,[^136] enlightening the people about Śrīvaiṣṇava religion and philosophy. After revisiting Tirunārāyaṇapuram, the Jīyar came to Śrīraṅgam where he spent the rest of his life in the service of the Lord and the propagation of Śrī Rāmānuja Darśana. This Jīyar occupies the pride of place among the Jīyars to have ruled the pontificate for a long period of 38 years and 9 months.[^137] He attained *paramapada* on Kṛṣṇapakṣa Caturdaśī tithi in the month of Citra in Viḷambi year (April 1598). His Bṛndāvanam is at Śrīraṅgam.

His Taniyan reads as follows:

`पराङ्कुशकृपाऽऽसिध्पदाम्भोजैकधारकम्।`
`श्रीनिवासमुनिं वन्दे मङ्गलानि तनोतु नः॥`

**12. Śrīman Nārāyaṇa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in Bhāradvāja Gotra under star Pūraraṭṭh, in the month of Puraṭṭāci at Vaṅgīpuram. He became the pontifical head in the month of Citra in the year Viḷambi on Kṛṣṇa Pakṣa daśamī tithi (April 1598) at Śrīraṅgam. He then proceeded in his *sañcāra* to Tirunārāyaṇapuram. He

[^136]: *Ācārya Vaibhavam*.
[^137]: Ibid, p. 282.
[]
stayed for sometime there, worshipping the Lord and paying obeisance to his *pūrvācārya* Śrī Ādivaṇ Śaṭhakopa Svāmī at his Bṛndāvanam there. He has the distinction of having discoursed on the *Śrībhāṣya* twelve times (*dvādaśā vṛtti*) there.

Then he proceeded to Ahobilam, Tirumala, Tiruvaḷḷūr, Kāñcī and returned to Tirunārāyaṇapuram. He attained Ācāryan Tiruvaḍi in the month of Puraṭṭāci, in Āṅgirasa year on Kṛṣṇapakṣa ṣaṣṭī tithi (September, 1632 ). He ruled over the pontificate for 34 years and 5 months. His Bṛndāvanam is at Tirunārāyaṇapuram.

His Taniyan reads as follows:

`श्रीपराङ्कुशयोगीन्द्र श्रीनिवासपदाश्रयम्।`
`श्रीमन्नारायणमुनिं वन्दे वेदान्तदेशिकम्॥`

**13. Śrī Vīrarāghava Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This svāmī was born in Tiruvaḷḷūr (Vaṅgīpuram agrahāram) in Bhāradvāja Gotra in the month of Āni under star Uttarāṣāḍhā. He became the pontifical head in the year Āṅgirasa in the month of Puraṭṭāci on Kṛṣṇapakṣa pañcamī tithi (September 1632) at Tirunārāyaṇapuram.

He started his *divyadeśa sañcāra* visiting Śrīraṅgam, Tirumāliruñjōlai, and Āḻvār Tirunagari. He stayed for sometime there worshipping the Lord and paying his obeisance at the shrines of Nammāḻvār and Ādi Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa
[]
Svāmī.[^138] Following the instructions given by Nammāḻvār in his dream, the Jīyar gave discourses on *Bhagavad viṣaya* for more than a year, there. Then he proceeded to Śrīvilliputtūr, and after visiting Tiruppullāṇi, proceeded to Ahobilam and then decided to spend the rest of his life at Śrīraṅgam, enlightening his disciples in Śrīvaiṣṇava religion and philosophy through his discourses.

He attained *paramapada* in the year Naḷa, in the month of Aippaśi on Kṛṣṇapakṣa ṣaṣṭhī tithi (October 1676). He ruled over the pontificate for 44 years and one month. He has the credit of having ruled over the Maṭha for a very large number of years next only to Ādi Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa. Hence he is referred to the *Śrī Sannidhi* cirlces respectfully as the Elder Śrī Vīrarāghava Śaṭhakopa Svāmī. His Bṛndāvanam is at Śrīraṅgam.

His Taniyan reads as under:-

`श्रीमन्नारायणमुनेः पदपङ्कजहंसकम्।`
`वीरराघवयोगीन्द्रं वन्दे वरगुणार्णवम्॥`

**14. Śrīman Nārāyaṇa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in the month of Āḍi under star Uttarāṣāḍham. He became the pontifical head on Kṛṣṇapakṣa pañcamī tithi in the year Naḷa in the month of Aippaśi corresponding to the month of October 1676. He stayed at

[^138]: *Ācārya Vaibhavam*, p. 284.
[]
Śrīraṅgam for sometime giving religious and philosphical discourses and performing *pañcasaṁskāra* and *prapatti* for those who so desired.

This Jīyar wrote the *Ācārya Guṇādarśa*[^139] in compliance with the request of his disciples who wanted their *guru* to expound on *Guru Paramparāprabhāva*. The *Puruṣakāra Mīmāṁsā*[^140] (ascribed by the *Śrī Sannidhi Guruparamparā* to the second Jīyar) is said to be authored by this Jīyar. He has also written the *Gītārthasaṅgrahavibhāga, Gītārtha-saṅgrahasāra* and *Jijñāsāsūtrabhāṣya-Bhāvaprakāśikā*.

He then proceeded to Kumbhakoṇam and then to his native place Pullambūtanguḍi, where he paid his obeisance to Lord Valvilli Rāma and Hemāmbhujavalli Tāyār. He visited many *divyadeśas* in and around Tanjore. Later the Jīyar attained *Paramapada* at Tirukkaṇḍiyūr on the banks of river Kāverī on an *amāvāsyā* day in the year Akṣaya in the month of Āḍi (August 1686). He ruled over the pontificate for 9 years and 10 months. His Bṛndāvanam is a Tirukkaṇḍiyūr.

[^139]: D. No: 16566 - GOML - This Manuscript is complete. It describes the qualities of a Preceptor in the light of Viśiṣṭādvaita Vedānta. Reference is made to Rāmānuja and Vedāntadeśika.
[^140]: See G. Sakuntala's Ph.D. Thesis, "*Concept of Śrī as Puruṣkāra according to Nārāyaṇamuni's Puruṣakāra Mīmāṁsā*".
[]
His Taniyan reads as under:

`श्रीवीरराघवमुनेर्निखिलस्यैकजीवनम्।`
`समाश्रयेमहि श्रीमन्नारायणमुनीश्वरम्॥`

**15. Śrī Vīrarāghava Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born at Eśānūr near Kāñcī in Thaṭṭai in Vādhūla Gotra in the month of Thai under star Citrā. He assumed the office of the pontificate in the year Akṣaya in the month of Āḍi (August 1686) on pūrṇimā tithi.

He travelled from Tirukkaṇḍiyūr visiting many *divyadeśas* enroute, like Tirukkōvalūr and then reached Kāñcī. He settled down at Kāñcī and discoursed on the *Śrībhāṣya* and other texts in accordance to the wishes of his disciples who resorted to his holy feet from far and wide. In the year Bhava, in the month of Puraṭṭāci (October 1694), this Jīyar attained *paramapada* on Kṛṣṇapakṣa ekādaśī tithi at Kāñcī. He ruled over the pontificate for 8 years and 2 months. His Bṛndāvanam is at Kāñcī.

His Taniyan reads as follows:-

`श्रीनारायणयोगीन्द्रपदांभोजैकजीवनम्।`
`भजे श्रीहृत्कल्पाणवीरराघवयोगिनम्॥`
[]
**16. Śrī Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in Sōkatūr agrahāram (near Kāñcī) in the month of Mārgaḻi under star Mṛgaśīrṣa. He became the pontifical head in the year Bhava, in the month of Puraṭṭāci (October 1694) on Kṛṣṇapakṣa daśamī tithi.

After paying his obeisance to the Lord at Kāñcī, this Svāmī proceeded on his *divyadeśa* tour of the Southern districts. He reached Tiruvahindrapuram where he performed *maṅgalāśāsana* to Lord Devanātha and Lord Hayagrīva. It was at that time, that a scholar, named Tirunārāyaṇapuram Devanāthācār Svāmī resorted to the holy feet of the Jīyar. He gave discourse on the *Grantha-catuṣṭaya* before the Jīyar Svāmī and had his *prapatti* done by the Jīyar. Then he fervently prayed to the Jīyar to grant him the ochre robes and take him into the ascetic fold. Accordingly, he was initiated into the *tūrīyāśrama* (asceticism) and the Jīyar handed the Tridaṇḍa to him and named him Keśava Śaṭhakopa Jīyar and ordained him to write a *Vyākhyāna* for *Tiruvāymoḻi*. Obeying his Ācārya's command, he wrote the *Padinenāyirappaḍi* and placed it at the holy feet of his guru. The Jīyar blessed his work and asked him to give discourses on *darśana granthas*.

Śrī Śaṭhakopa Jīyar then proceeded on tours to Tirukkōvalūr, Śrīmuṣṇam, Citrakūṭam, Teralundūr, Kumbhakoṇam and Tiruvindalūr. He stayed for sometime at Kumbhakoṇam during which time Kiḍāmbi Śrī Veṅkaṭācārya Svāmī paid obeisance to the Jīyar and gave philosophical discourses in his presence.
[]
The Jīyar attained *paramapada* in the year Bahudhānya, in the month of Vaikāśi (June 1698) on Śuklapakṣa aṣṭamī tithi at Kumbhakoṇam. He ruled over the pontificate for 3 years and 8 months. His Bṛndāvanam is at Kumbhakoṇam.

His Taniyan reads as under:

`कल्याणराजवमुनेः कृपापात्रं दयानिधिम्।`
`सर्वशास्त्रार्थतत्त्वज्ञं शठकोपमुनिं भजे॥`

**17. Śrī Vīrarāghava Vedānta Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in the month of Puraṭṭāci in Tiruveḷḷiyaṅguḍi under the Śatabhiṣak star. He became the pontifical head in the year Bahudhānya, in the month Vaikāśi, on Śuklapakṣa pañcamī tithi (June 1698).

He proceeded in his *divyadeśa sañcāra* from Kumbhakonam to Śrīraṅgam and then to Tiruveḷḷiyaṅguḍi. He stayed for sometime there, doing *maṅgalāśāsana* to Śrī Kolavilli Rāma and Marakatavallī Tāyār. Later he proceeded to Śrīraṅgam and stayed there for sometime giving religious discourses at Rāmānuja's *sannidhi* inside the temple premises. He gave discourses for twelve times on the *Śrībhāṣya*, fifteen times on the *Bhagavad Viṣaya*, ten times on the *Gītā Bhāṣya* and ten times on *Śrīmad*
[]
*Rahasyatrayasāra*.[^141] He was instrumental in providing the Lord with many *divyābharaṇas*.

The Svāmī then proceeded to Tirunārāyaṇapuram and paid his obeisance to the Lord there. He stayed for sometime at the Bṛndāvanam of Śrī Ādivaṇ Śaṭhakopa Svāmī, then he returned to Śrīraṅgam and proceeded on a tour of the southern districts of Tirukkaṇḍiyūr, Kūḍalūr, Pullambūdaṅguḍi and Kumbhakoṇam. He also ordered many *divya* ornaments to be made for adorning Lord Valvilli Rāma and Lord Ārāvamudan. After worshipping at Tirumala, he proceeded to Śrī Ahobilam, the abode of nine Narasiṁhas. Then he went to Tiruvaḷḷūr to pay obeisance to Lord Vīrarāghava and Goddess Kanakavallī. Next in his itinerary were Śrīperumbūdūr, Tiruvallikkeṇi, Tirunirmalai and Kāñcī. Then he proceeded to Tirupputkuḻi, the abode of Lord Vijayarāghava.

This Svāmī fell ill there and attained *paramapada* in the year Pramādica in the month of Thai on Kṛṣṇapakṣa prathamā tithi (January 1734). He ruled over the pontificate for 35 years and 7 months. His Bṛndāvanam is at Tirupputkuḻi.

His Taniyan is as under:

`श्रीमन्नारायणमुनिं श्रीशठारिपदाश्रयम्।`
`श्रीवीरराघवमुनिं वन्दे वेदान्तदेशिकम्॥`

[^141]: *Ācārya Vaibhavam*, p. 291.
[]
**18. Śrīman Nārāyaṇa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in the month of Puraṭṭāci under star Āyilyam in the family of Vīravalli at Tiruvaḷḷūr. He became the pontifical head in Pramādica year in the month of Thai (January 1734) on śuklapakṣa ekādaśī tithi. He proceeded from Tirupputkuḻi to Kāñcī and then to Śrīraṅgam where he stayed for sometime, giving discourses on *Grantha catuṣṭaya*. At that time, one Koil Kaṇḍāḍai Appan Svāmī resorted to the holy feet of the Jīyar and learnt the philosophical truths expounded in the *Śrībhāṣya* from him. Appan Svāmī was in charge of the Daśāvatāra *sannidhi* at Śrīraṅgam which was handed over to the ancestors of Appan Svāmī by Śrī Ādi Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa Svāmī. Obeying the divine command, Appan Svāmī handed over the Daśāvatāra *sannidhi* along with its property, landed and monetary, to the Jīyar. It is also interesting to note that the silver *vigraha* of Lord Raṅganātha which is one of the many idols carried by the Jīyar in the silver *maṇṭapa*, in all his *sañcāras* (tours) and to which special *pūjās* and offerings are made day and night by the Jīyar, is the *vigraha* which had once adorned the house of Appan Svāmī and was handed over by his ancestor to the Ahobila Maṭha.

This Svāmī attained *paramapada* in the year Rākṣasa in the month of Āḍi (July 1735) in Kṛṣṇapakṣa ekādaśī tithi. He ruled over the pontificate for 18 months. His Bṛndāvanam is at Śrīraṅgam.
[]
His Taniyan reads as follows:

`श्रीमद्रराघववेदान्तमुनिवर्यपदाश्रयम्।`
`श्रीमन्नारायणमुनिं श्रये श्रीभाष्यदेशिकम्॥`

**19. Śrī Śrīnivāsa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in Tiruvallikeṇi in the Naḍādūr family in the month of Māsi under star Maghā. He became the pontifical head in Rākṣasa year on the month of Āḍi on Kṛṣṇapakṣa navamī tithi (July, 1735). He proceeded from Śrīraṅgam and visited many *divyadeśas* like Kumbhakoṇam, Tiruvahindrapuram, Tirukkōvalūr, Madhurāntakam, Kāñcī, Tirumala and Ahobilam, then returned via Ghaṭikācala, Tirumala, Tiruvaḷḷūr, Tiruvallikkeṇi, Tirunirmalai, Tiruviṇanthai, Tirukkōvalūr, Śrīmuṣṇam and then to Pullambūtaṅguḍi. There, he stayed for sometime, performing *maṅgalāśāsana* to Lord Valvilli Rāma. He attained *paramapada* in the year Krodhana in the month of Māsi (February, 1746 ) on Śuklapakṣa caturthī tithi. He ruled over the pontificate for 10 years and 7 months. His Bṛndāvanam is at Pullambūtaṅguḍi.

His Taniyan reads as under:-

`श्रीमन्नारायणमुनेः पदपद्ममधुव्रतम्।`
`श्रीनिवासमुनिं वन्दे वेदान्तद्वयदेशिकम्॥`
[]
**20. Śrī Vīrarāghava Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in Piḷḷaippākkam village near Śrīperumbūdūr (the birthplace of Rāmānuja) in the month of Puraṭṭāci under star Mūla. He became the pontifical head in Krodhana year in the month of Māśi (February, 1746) on Śukla pakṣa tṛthiyā tithi.

This Svāmī proceeded from Pullambūtaṅguḍi to Śrīraṅgam and then to Tirunārāyaṇapuram and from there to Tirumala and then to Ahobilam. On his way to Ahobilam the Svāmī got the divine call and left for his heavenly abode, in the year Prabhava, in the month of Paṅguni (March, 1748) on Kṛṣṇapakṣa saptamī tithi. He ruled over the pontificate for two years and one month.

It is not known for sure as to where exactly this Svāmī's Bṛndāvanam is situated. The *Śrī Sannidhi Guruparamparā* simply states that it is in the northern region (*Vada deśa*).[^142]

His Taniyan reads as under:

`श्रीनिवासमुनिहृत्पङ्कजवेदान्तसम्भवम्।`
`श्रीवीरराघवमुनिं कल्याणगुणमाश्रये॥`

[^142]: See p. 77.
[]
**21. Śrī Parāṅkuśa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in Thaiyār agrahāram in Vaṅgīpuram (in Kāñcī district) in Bhāradvāja Gotra in the month of Paṅguni under star Hastā. He became the pontifical head in the year Prabhava in the month of Paṅguni (March 1748) on Kṛṣṇapakṣa ṣaṣṭhī tithi.

This Svāmī proceeded to Ahobilam and then to Tirumala and from there to Tiruvaḷḷūr. He visited Śrīperumbūdūr, Kāñcī, Tiruvahindrapuram, Kumbhakoṇam and Śrīraṅgam. During his stay at Śrīraṅgam the Svāmī gave discourses on the *Śrībhāṣya* before Vedāntadeśika's *sannidhi* inside the temple precincts. Later, he visited Tirunārāyaṇapuram and the Bṛndāvanam of Śrī Ādivaṇ Śaṭhakopa Svāmī, where he developed an intense desire to write a *prabandha* about his Ācārya. This gained divine approval instantly, by Garuda circling in the sky above. Accordingly, the Svāmī wrote *Śrī Ādivaṇ Śaṭhakopa Svāmī's Aḍaikkalappathu* comprising of eleven verses. This beautiful string of verses beginning with *Ādimuraiyām* extolling Śrī Ādivaṇ Śaṭhakopa Svāmī's greatness is included in the daily *Nityānusandhāna* in Ahobila Maṭha till this day. He also wrote *Satsampradāyasāra* which gives concisely the *Ācāryavaibhava* of all the preceeding Jīyars of Ahobila Maṭha. He also wrote *maṅgala* verses on Lord
[]
Nṛsiṁha, Lord Kṛṣṇa and also a few songs to be sung during the cradle ceremony of Lord Kṛṣṇa (*dolotsavam*).

For sometime, the Svāmī stayed at Tirunārāyaṇapuram and then left for Śrīraṅgam. But on his way, the Svāmī fell ill and passed away. He attained *paramapada* in the year Īśvara, in the month of Kārthigai (November, 1757) on Kṛṣṇapakṣa caturthī tithi at Pāḷameḍu. He ruled over the pontificate for 9 years and 8 months. His Bṛndāvanam is at Pāḷameḍu.

His Taniyan reads as under:

`वेदान्तोदारवीरराघवमुनेर्नारायणश्रीनृधि-`
`श्रीमद्घोरष्टदृष्टहास्ययमिनां कारुण्यवीक्षास्पदम्।`
`विज्ञातोभयवेदमीलिहृदयं विद्वच्छिरोभूषणं`
`वन्देयामुनदिनं पराङ्कुशमुनिं वैराग्यभक्त्यान्वितम्॥`

**22. Śrīman Nārāyaṇa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in Gadādharapuram agrahāram in the month of Āḍi under star Rohiṇī. He became the pontifical head in the year Īśvara, in the month of Mārgaḻi (January, 1758) on Śuklapakṣa pañcamī tithi in Pāḷameḍu.

This Svāmī proceeded to Tirunārāyaṇapuram and paid obeisance to the Lord there. Then he visited the Bṛndāvanam of Śrī Ādivaṇ Śaṭhakopa Svāmī and stayed for six months there. Responding to the divine call, he proceeded to Śrīraṅgam but fell ill on the way. He attained *paramapada* in Pāḷameḍu in the
[]
year Bahudhānya in the month of Āḍi (August, 1758) on Kṛṣṇapakṣa ṣaṣṭhī tithi. He ruled over the pontificate for only 7 months, the shortest period of pontificate for any Jīyar of Ahobila Maṭha. His Bṛndāvanam is at Pāḷameḍu.

His Taniyan reads as under:

`विद्याम्भोधिरपारकृत्स्नमुनिराट्छिद्रेक्षदग्धाश्रितं`
`व्रत्यन्तामृतवर्षिणं तनुभृतां त्राणाय जातोदयम्।`
`क्षौण्यां ख्यातसमस्ततन्त्रकुशलव्याख्यातृताशालिनं`
`श्रीनारायणयोगिवर्यमनिशं कारुण्यपूर्णं भजे॥`

**23. Śrī Vīrarāghava Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in Tiruveḷḷiyaṅguḍi in the month of Āni, under star Uttaraṭṭādi. He became the pontifical head in Bahudhānya year, in the month of Āḍi (August, 1758) on Kṛṣṇapakṣa pañcamī tithi. He proceeded from Pāḷameḍu to Tirunārāyaṇapuram and then to the Bṛndāvanam of Śrī Ādi Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa Svāmī where he stayed for some time. He then proceeded to Ahobilam and after worshipping the nine Nṛsiṁhas, he started his *divyadeśa sañcāra* (tour) visiting Tirumala, Tiruvaḷḷūr, Tirunindravūr, Tiruvallikkeṇi, Śrīperumbūdūr, Kāñcī, Tirukkōvalūr, Kumbhakoṇam and Śrīraṅgam. He then proceeded to Tirunārāyaṇapuram and then to Śrīraṅgapaṭṭiṇam and settled down there. He attained Ācāryan Tiruvaḍi in the year Svabhānu, in the month of Thai (Februrary, 1763) on Śuklapakṣa daśamī tithi. He ruled over the pontificate for 5 years and 6 months. His Bṛndāvanam is at Śrīraṅgapaṭṭiṇam.
[]
His Taniyan reads as follows:

`वीरराघववेदान्तनारायणपदाश्रयम्।`
`श्रीवीरराघवमुनिं श्रये श्रितवत्सलम्॥`

**24. Śrī Parāṅkuśa Rāmānuja Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in the Kalyāṇapuram Cakravartī family in the month of Citra under star Punarvasu. He became the pontifical head in the year Svabhānu in the month of Thai (February, 1763) on Śukla pañcamī in Śrīraṅgapaṭṭiṇam. He proceeded to Tirunārāyaṇapuram and then to Śrīraṅgam and from there went to Ahobilam. The King of Gadvāl samasthān, Somabhūpāla, who came to know that the Jīyar was camping at Ahobilam, paid his obeisance to the Jīyar and invited him to visit his Kingdom. Complying to his invitation, the Jīyar visited Gadvāl and did *pañcasaṁskāra* to the King and his family. The king in return made generous endowments in the form of cash, lands and gold ornaments for the Lord.[^143] The Jīyar later proceeded to Tirumala and then to Tirunārāyaṇapuram where he gave religious and philosophical discourses. Then he wrote *Śrīprapatti, Śrī Nṛsiṁha maṅgalāśāsana, Śrīstava* and *Śrīpañcāśat*.

On his way to Śrīraṅgam, near Kokkarāyanpeṭṭai, the Svāmī fell ill and attained *puramapada* in the year Manmatha, in the month of Māsi (March,

[^143]: *Ācārya Vaibhavam*, p. 303 and *Śrī Nṛsiṁha Priyā*, Special issue, p. 30, June 1992.
[]
1776) on Kṛṣṇapakṣa Tṛtīyā tithi. He ruled over the pontificate for 13 years and one month. His Bṛndāvanam is at Kokkarāyanpeṭṭai.

His Taniyan reads as follows:-

`श्रीवीरराघवमुनिवृतिमोनिभूरि-श्रीमत्पदाब्जसममाश्रयलब्धबोधम्।`
`श्रीवीरराघवमुनीन्द्रकृपावलम्बं श्रीमत्पराङ्कुशयतीन्द्रगुरुं भजामः॥`

**25. Śrī Śrīnivāsa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in the month of Āḍi under Svāti star. He assumed the office of the pontificate in the year Manmatha in the month of Paṅguni (1776, March) in Śuklapakṣa pañcamī tithi.

The Svāmī was well-versed in *Tarka, Mīmāṁsā* and other *śāstras* and was a *Pañcakālaparāyaṇa* in his *pūrvāśrama*. He gave religious and philosophical discourses on *Śrībhāṣya, Śatadūṣaṇi, Nyāyapariśuddhi* and *Nyāyasiddhāñjana* after becoming the pontifical head. He was well-grounded in *jñāna* and *anuṣṭhāna* and adorned the pontifical seat like a *Yatisārvabhauma*.

Jealous of the Jīyar's erudition and scholastic achievements, one of his disciples dared to poison him.[^144] But the Svāmī's benedictory glance was enough to make the disciple accept his crime and beg for the Svāmī's

[^144]: *Ācārya Vaibhavam*, p. 313.
[]
forgiveness which was granted instantly. This incident was actually instrumental in attracting innumerable devotees into the Jīyar's fold.

This Svāmī then proceeded to Śrīraṅgam and did *maṅgalāśāsana* to Lord Raṅganātha. He is said to have recited the following *śloka* while praying to the Lord[^145] —

`श्रीरङ्गेशयः फणिपतिशयने दक्षिणां वीक्षमाणः`
`ख्यातं श्रीताश्रुतीये प्रणवपरिणतं तद्विमानं च दिव्यम्।`
`आद्यं व्यक्तं स्वयं च स्थलमतिशुभदं नायिकारङ्गपूर्वीं`
`भूमेर्वैकुण्ठमेतत् जगति विजयते सहाजेन्द्रपुसितम्॥`

The Jīyar proceeded on a tour of Southern districts visiting Kumbhakoṇam, Tiruvahindrapuram, Kāñcī and other places. Wishing to visit Badarikāśrama, the Jīyar proceeded northwards. He was confronted on the way by an evil sorcerer who threatened the Jīyar and his entourage. By invoking the Lord through *Nṛsiṁha anuṣṭup-mantra*, the Jīyar made the sorcerer ineffective. He fell at the Jīyar's feet asking for his pardon.[^146]

Unnerved by these threats the Svāmī proceeded to Gadvāl, where at a village named Sūrāpuram (Cuddapa district) he met a great scholar Kirīṭi Veṅkaṭācārya who challenged the Jīyar to a literary debate on Viśiṣṭādvaita philosophy. The Jīyar argued that a knowledge of the *kāraṇavastu* was

[^145]: *Ācārya Vaibhavam*, p. 313.
[^146]: *Śrī Nṛsiṁha Priyā*, Special issue, p. 31, June 1992. *Satsampradāya Muktāvali*, p. 87
[]
enough as *kāryavastu* became self-evident through this knowledge, Veṅkaṭācārya Svāmī took the opposite stand. The debate continued for fifteen days and on the night before the concluding date, Lord Nṛsiṁha appeared in the Jīyar's dream and advised him to argue his point after referring to the *Śrutaprakāśikā* and *Śatadūṣaṇī*. Obeying the Lord's command. The Jīyar emerged victorious in the debate whereupon the Sūrāpuram King became his disciple and granted many endowments in cash and kind to Ahobila Maṭha and honoured the Jīyar by carrying him in a palanquin on his shoulders. After staying for sometime at Sūrāpuram, accepting the hospitality of Veṅkaṭācārya Svāmī, the Jīyar proceeded on his tour.

The king of Gadvāl, Somabhūpāla received the Jīyar with full state honours on his arrival at the capital. He stayed for sometime there and the king donated many ornaments to the Lord and gave a generous grant in kind to the Maṭha. Later the Jīyar proceeded to Ahobilam and after worshipping the nine Nṛsiṁhas, he went on a tour of Tirumala, Tiruvaḷḷūr, Tirunindravūr, Tiruallikkeṇi, Śrīperumbūdūr, Kāñcī, Tiruvahīndrapuram, Tiruccitrakūṭam, Śrīmuṣṇam and Kumbhakoṇam. There he stayed for sometime and wrote *Saccaritrartnāvali, Śrī Nṛsiṁhastava* and *Śrī Nṛsiṁhamaṅgala*. He then proceeded to Śrīraṅgam and then to Tirunārāyaṇapuram and then came down to Pullambūtaṅguḍi and settled there. At that time, Tanjore was ruled by King Serfoji (1796-1833). Lord Nṛsiṁha appeared in the king's dream and directed
[]
him to make endowments in kind to Ahobila Maṭha. Whereupon, the king invited the Jīyar to his royal abode and paid obeisance to him relating his dream to the Jīyar. The Jīyar was pleasantly surprised by the king's donation of a village near Pullambūtaṅguḍi to Ahobila Maṭha for the daily worship of the Lord. Therefore the village came to be called Śrī Nṛsiṁhapuram. The Jīyar in turn, gave his holy sandals to the king who accepted and worshipped them with great veneration.[^147]

The Jīyar then returned to Pullambūtaṅguḍi and ordered a Maṭha to be constructed at Nṛsiṁhapuram. He stayed there giving religious and philosophical discourses on Vedānta texts. Later due to old age, the Jīyar passed away. He attained *paramapada* in the year Prajotpatti, in the month of Kārtigai (30.11.1811) on pūrṇimā tithi. His Bṛndāvanam is at Nṛsiṁhapuram. He ruled over the pontificate for 35years and 8 months. This Jīyar is said to be an *aṁśa* of Vainateya (Garuḍa).[^148] Even today devotees are miraculously cured of their illness by praying at his Bṛndāvanam. It was also during his pontifical period that the largest amount of landed property was acquired by Ahobila Maṭha.[^149]

[^147]: *Ācārya Vaibhavam*, p. 313.
[^148]: See "The Hindu", November 13, 1966.
[^149]: *Ācārya Vaibhavam*, p. 313.
[]
His Taniyan reads as under:-

`श्रीवासवीरराघववर्यपराङ्कुशादि-रामानुजार्यमुनिभिश्चिरसेवनीयः।`
`संप्रेक्षितं करुणया परिपूर्णबोधं श्रीश्रीनिवासयतिशेखरमाश्रयामः॥`

**26. Śrī Raṅganātha Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in the month of Āḍi under star Pūram at Gadādharapuram in Śrīvatsa Gotra. He became the pontifical head in the year Prajotpatti, in the month of Kārtikai, on Śuklapakṣa pañcamī tithi (21.11.1811).

This Jīyar proceeded from Nṛsiṁhapuram to Tiruādanūr, Kumbhakoṇam and then to Śrīraṅgam. From there he went to Tirunārāyaṇapuram and stayed there for sometime. The ruler of Mysore Śrī Kṛṣṇarāja Kaṇṭhīrava Sārvabhauma, sent his emissary to meet the Jīyar and to invite the Jīyar to Mysore. Complying to his request, the Jīyar proceeded to Mysore where he was received with full royal honours. Lord Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha was placed on a golden swing (*dolā*) inside a silver *maṇṭapa* and many ornaments were donated by the King. A *vajra* vessel was also made for the Lord's Tiruvārādhana. After enjoying royal hospitality for sometime the Jīyar started on his prerignations.
[]
The Jīyar went to Ahobilam and then to Tirumala, Tiruvaḷḷūr, Kāñcī, Tirukkōvalūr, Tiruvahindrapuram, and then to Kumbhakoṇam. From there he proceeded via Śrīraṅgam to Śrīvilliputtūr. There the Jīyar was instrumental in building a Maṭha in the *sannidhi* street and also performing many renovations in the Āṇḍāḷ *sannidhi*. Then he visited the nine Tirupathis in South India, doing *maṅgalāśāsana* to the deities there and then returned to Nṛsiṁhapuram. Here, he arranged for the construction of a Bṛndāvanam for his predecessor, the 25th Jīyar and installed his image there. He also established an *agrahāra* (Brahmin settlement) nearby called Śrīraṅganāthapuram. Complying to the request of his disciplies the Jīyar wrote a manual on the daily rites to be followed by the Ahobila Maṭha titled *Śrī Sannidhi Āhnika*. He also wrote a few verses on Lord Nṛsiṁha. Due to his old age, the Jīyar left for his heavenly abode in the year Sarvadhārī, in the month of Mārgaḻi (20.12.1828) on Śuklapakṣa caturdaśī tithi. He ruled over the pontificate for 17 years and one month. His Bṛndāvanam is at Śrī Nṛsiṁhapuram. This Jīyar was the son of the 25th Jīyar in his *pūrvāśrama*.

His Taniyan reads as under:

`श्रीवीरराघवयतीन्द्रपराङ्कुशादि-रामानुजार्यकमलाब्धिरविप्रसिध्वर्यैः।`
`संप्रेक्षितं करुणया परिपूर्णबोधं श्रीरङ्गनाथयतिशेखरमाश्रयामः॥`
[]
**27. Śrī Vīrarāghava Vedānta Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in the month of Vaikāśi, under star Aviṭṭam in Gadādharapuram in Ilanagar (Kāñcī). He became the pontifical head in the year Sarvadhārī in the month of Mārgaḻi on Śuklapakṣa pañcamī tithi (10.1.1829).

He toured Pillambūtaṅguḍi, Ādanūr, Kumbhakoṇam, Tiruccitrakūṭam, Tiruvahindrapuram, Kāñcī, Tiruvaḷḷūr, Tirumala and then proceeded to Ahobilam. After worshipping the nine Nṛsiṁhas, he stayed for sometime at Lower Ahobilam and paid his obeisance to Lord Prahlādavarada. The reigning King of Gadvāl, a *Śrī Sannidhiśiṣya*, paid his respects to the Jīyar and invited him to visit Gadvāl. Responding to his invitation the Jīyar visited Gadvāl and stayed there for sometime.

This Jīyar has many works to his credit. He has written the *Vaikuṇṭha Vijaya Campū*[^150] (a retaliation to *Nīlakaṇṭha Vijaya Campū*), *Caṇḍamāruta Vyākhyāna, Tātparya Ratnāvalī, Brahmasabdavādārtha, Viśeṣa Tarka Vāda, Vṛttisūtra in Vyākaraṇa, Vyākaraṇaśloka for Mahābhāṣya, Saṁkramaṇa-nirṇaya, Jayantinirṇaya, Strīsaṁskāraviṣayanirṇaya, Mūlamantrajapa-nirṇaya, Nyāsollāsa, Kṛpāsāgarastava, Daśāvarādirghagāyatrī-japanirṇayaśloka, Yativiṣaye sudarśanahomābhāvanirṇaya, Kṣiraṇa-

[^150]: See *Viśiṣṭādvaitakośa*, preface - p. xv: वैकुण्ठविजयः शैवकतॄनीलकण्ठविजयचम्पुप्रतिभटः।
[]
*distavam, Nandādhīpastava, Vihageśvarastava, Śrī Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁhastava Śrīvaṇśaṭharīstava, Śrī Vīrarāghavastavam, Śrī Ghaṭisūtranirṇayam, Śrī Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha maṅgalam*, and *Śrī Śrīnivāsa Yatīndra Mahādeśika Daśakam*.

This Jīyar was a famous personage during his pontifical term. The rapport between this Jīyar and the King of Gadvāl can be understood from the fact when the Jīyar fell ill, he left the Ahobila Maṭha in charge of the King of Gadvāl and authorised him to find a suitable successor to the pontificate.[^151]

This Jīyar attained *paramapada* in the year Khara, in the month of Āvaṇi, in Śuklapakṣa aṣṭamī tithi (17.8.1831). His Bṛndāvanam is on the banks of river Kṛṣṇā in Gadvāl district. He ruled over the pontificate for a short period of 2 years and 7 months. This Jīyar was the grandson of the 25th Jīyar and the son of the 26th Jīyar in their *pūrvāśrama*.

His Taniyan reads as under:

`श्री श्रीनिवासयतिशेखरलब्धबोधं श्रीरङ्गनाथयतिपुर्यपदाब्जभृङ्गम्।`
`श्रीवीरराघवमुनिस्फुरितम्लिभृङ्गैः श्रीनाथभक्तिभरिताश्रयमाश्रयामः॥`

**28. Śrī Raṅganātha Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in the month of Āvaṇi under star Mūlam in the Naḍādūr family in Śrīvatsa Gotra in Tirukkuruṅguḍi. His *pūrvāśrama* name

[^151]: There was a gap of about two years before a worthy successor could be found by the king of Gadvāl.
[]
was Śrī Vānamāmālācārī. This Svāmī and his younger brother Śrī Veṅkaṭanārāyaṇācār Svāmī were well known scholars in their village. So excellent were their memory skills, that they could discourse on the *Śrībhāṣya, Śrutaprakāśikā* and *Īḍu Muppattāṟāyirappaṭi* without referring to the concerned books. Both of them were well-grounded in *jñāna* and *anuṣṭhāna*.

There was an interregnum for a period of one year and eleven months after the passing away of the 27th Jīyar. The King of Gadvāl, who was given the charge of nominating a suitable successor to the pontifical throne, called for a *vidvatsadas* (a meeting of eminent scholars) to make his selection. The choice naturally fell on Tirukuruṅguḍi Svāmī who was well-qualified, with excellent communication skills to elucidate on the subtleties of the Viśiṣṭādvaita system of philosophy. He was able to establish his superiority in literary debates too, by winning over his adversaries with the greatest ease. In response to the King's request, this Svāmī donned the ochre robes and became the pontifical head in the year Vijaya, in the month of Āni, on Kṛṣṇapakṣa pañcamī tithi (7.7.1833).

In the hierarchy of Ahobilam Maṭha Jīyars, this Svāmī is placed on par with Śrī Ādi Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa Svāmī, Śrī Ṣaṣṭha Parāṅkuśa Svāmī and Śrī
[]
Śrīnivāsa Yatīndra Mahādeśika. He is also said to have granted succour to his afflicted devotees through his mantric powers.[^152]

This Svāmī proceeded from Gadvāl to Ahobilam, Tirumala, Tiruvaḷḷūr, Śrī Perumbūdūr, Kāñcī and Madhurāntakam where he stayed for sometime performing *maṅgalāśāsana* to Lord Kodaṇḍa Rāma and Goddess Janakavallī. He also gave religious and philosophical discourses to his devotees.

An incident is related in the Jīyar's life, when a rich devotee who was proud of his wealth, offered many pomegranate fruits and gold coins to the Jīyar. In order to humble his pride, the Jīyar ordered that both be offered to the Lord and then distributed equally among the devotees who had gathered there. The rich devotee realised his mistake and fell at the Jīyar's feet asking for his forgiveness.

Even when the Jīyar was at Madhurāntakam, he felt that his health was failing, and promptly appointed Lālāpeṭṭai Vajram Svāmī to look after the *nityārādhana* of the Lord who later appointed Ilanagar Gadādharapuram Śrī Cakravarti Svāmī to succeed him. The Jīyar attained *paramapada* in the year Durmukhi, in the month of Mārgaḻi on Kṛṣṇapakṣa saptamī tithi (29.12.1836). He ruled over the pontificate for three years and five months. It is to be noted

[^152]: *Ācārya Vaibhavam*, p. 320.
[]
here that the 33rd and 34th Jīyars who were to follow had great respect for this Jīyar's erudition and resorted to his holy feet for guidance, many a time.

The Jīyar's Bṛndāvanam is at Madhurāntakam.

His Taniyan reads as under:-

`श्रीवासहृत्पतिवीरराघवहादिवेदान्तसंयमिमौलिस्त्सायकमौलिभाजः।`
`संप्रेक्षितं करुणया परिपूर्णबोधं श्रीरङ्गनाथशठकोपमुनिं भजामः॥`

**29. Śrī Parāṅkuśa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in Lālāpeṭṭai in Vajram family in the month of Caitra under the star Citrā. He became the pontifical head in the year Durmukhi in the month of Kārthigai, on Śuklapakṣa navamī tithi (17.11.1836).

This Svāmī proceeded from Madhurāntakam to Kāñcī, Tirupputkuḻi, and then to Tiruppāṟkaḍal on the banks of the river Pālār. Finding his health to be deteriorating, he decided to stay there permanently. He called upon Ilanagar Gadādharapuram Cakravartiyācāriār Svāmī to become the pontifical head. Obeying the Ācārya's command, he took to *saṁnyāsāśrama* under the name of *Śrīnivāsa Vedānta Mahādeśika*.

The 29th Jīyar wrote the *Śrī Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁhasuprabhātam*. When he was at Tiruppāṟkaḍal, the Svāmī fell ill and passed away. He attained *paramapada* in the year Heviḷambi in the month of Mārgaḻi on Kṛṣṇapakṣa
[]
