caturdaśī tithi (10.12.1837). He ruled over the pontificate for one year and one month. His Bṛndāvanam is at Tiruppāṟkaḍal.

His Taniyan reads as follows:-

`विप्राम्भोधिसुधद्युतिव्रतिभिराट् श्रीवासरङ्गाधिप-`
`श्रीमद्घोरष्टदृष्टद्युतिविरयोद्योगीश्वरैरेन्दहम्।`
`रक्षाशिक्षणठारिसेप्यमिरक्षालोकितं सादरं`
`विद्यावारिनिधिं पराङ्कुशयतीन्द्राख्यं मुनीन्द्रं भजे॥`

**30. Śrī Śrīnivāsa Vedānta Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in Ilanagar Gadādharapuram in Śrīvatsa Gotra in the month of Mārgaḻi, under star Viśākhā. His *pūrvāśrama* name was Vidvān Cakravartiyācārya. He became the pontifical head in the year Durmukhi in the month of Paṅguni on Śuklapakṣa navamī tithi (15.3.1837).

This Svāmī proceeded from Tiruppāṟkaḍal to Kāñcī, Śrīperumbūdūr, Tiruvaḷḷūr, Tirunindravūr, Tiruvallikkeṇi, Tirunirmalai, Tiruvidavendai, Madhurāntakam, Tirvahindrapuram, and then to Kumbhakoṇam. There, he presented a golden *kavaca* to Lord Ārāvamudan.

Then he visited Pullambūtaṅguḍi and Ādanūr and stayed for sometime at Nṛsiṁhapuram. He was instrumental in constructing the *bṛndāvanams* for his *pūrvācāryas* who were enshrined there.

This Svāmī has ten compositions to his credit. He wrote *Śrī Nṛsiṁhamaṅgalāśāsana, Śrī Nṛsiṁhamaṅgalam, Śrī Raṅganāthamaṅgalam*,
[]
*Śrī Śrīnivāsamaṅgalam, Śrī Gītācāryan maṅgalam, Śrī Śārṅgapāṇi maṅgalam*[^153] *Śrī Lakṣmīnṛsiṁha Suprabhātam, Śrī Raṅganātha Suprabhātam, Śrī Śrīnivāsa Suprabhātam*, and *Śrī Lakṣmīnṛsiṁha Prapatti*. This Svāmī's *Śrī Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha Suprabhātam* is included in the *Nityānusandhānam* of the Ahobila Maṭha till this day.

This Jīyar then visited the *divyadeśas* in the Southern districts and returned to Śrī Nṛsiṁhapuram and settled down there. He attained *paramapada* in the year Subhakṛt in the month of Puraṭṭāci on Kṛṣṇapakṣa caturthī tithi (27.9.1842). He ruled over the pontificate for five years and six months. His Bṛndāvanam is at Nṛsiṁhapuram.

His Taniyan reads as follows:-

`श्रीवासकृत्पतिवीरराघवहादिवेदान्तदेशिकपराङ्कुशलक्ष्मणार्यः।`
`संप्रेक्षितं करुणया परिपूर्णबोधं श्रीश्रीनिवासनिगमान्तगुरुं भजामः॥`

**31. Śrīman Nārāyaṇa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in Śrīraṅgam in the Viñjimūr family, in the month of Kārtigai under star Makhā. He became the pontifical head in the year Subhakṛt in the month of Kārtigai on Śuklapakṣa pañcamī tithi (7.12.1842).

[^153]: See *Satsampradāya muktāvali*, p. 162.
[]
He proceeded from Nṛsiṁhapuram to Ādanūr, Pullambūtaṅguḍi, Kumbhakoṇam, Kāñcī and Tiruvaḷḷūr. There he ordered for a silver elephant vehicle to be made for the Lord Vīrarāghava, which could be taken out during the Lord's procession on festival days. Then, the Svāmī proceeded to Tirumala, Colasiṁhapuram, Śrīperumbūdūr, Tirunindravūr, Tiruvallikkeṇi, and via Tiruvahindrapuram he came to Śrī Nṛsiṁhapuram. There he gave discourses on *ubhaya vedānta* texts to his disciples. It was then that he wrote two works - *Śrī Nṛsiṁha maṅgalam* and *Śāṅgaprapatti niṣṭhā*.

Desirous of solitude, the Svāmī proceeded to a small hamlet on the banks of river Kāverī called Tyāgarājapuram and settled down there, worshipping Lord Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha. The Svāmī attained *paramapada* in the year Parābhava, in the month of Paṅguni on Śuklapakṣa caturdaśī tithi (30.3.1847). He ruled over the pontificate for four years and four months. His Bṛndāvanam is at Tyāgarājapuram.

His Taniyan reads as under:

`श्रीरङ्गनाथयतिवर्यकृपाब्धिसौधं श्रीवासवेदशिखरायदयावलम्बम्।`
`वैराग्यभक्तिसुभृशद्गुणसागरं श्रीनारायणश्रितशिरोयतिगुरुमाश्रयामः॥`

**32. Śrī Vīrarāghava Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in Śrīvilliputtūr, in the month of Caitra under star Pūraṭṭādi. Since his native place was Ādanūr, this Svāmī was popularly
[]
known as Ādanūr Aḻiyasiṅgar. He became the pontifical head in the year Parābhava in the month of Paṅguni on Śukalapakṣa pañcamī tithi (30.3.1847).

This Svāmī proceeded from Tyāgarājapuram to Kumbhakoṇam and then to Pullambūtaṅguḍi, Ādanūr and then to Śrīraṅgam, Āḻvār Tirunagari and the nine southern Tirupatis, Vānamāmalai, Tirukkuruṅguḍi, Madurai, Madhurāntakam and Kāñcī. Here, he visited the eighteen satellite *divyadeśas* around Kāñcī and then proceeded to Tirunārāyaṇapuram via Tirupputkuḻi. He stayed for sometime there doing *maṅgalāśāsana* to Lord and Śrī. The local king Śrī Kṛṣṇarāja Kaṇṭhīrava Sārvabhauma sent an invitation to the Jīyar to visit Mysore. The Jīyar complied with his request and stayed for sometime at Mysore accepting royal patronage. Later, he proceeded to Colasiṁhapuram and Tirumala and then decided to settle down at Tiruvaḷḷūr, because of his age.[^154]

The Svāmī chose as his successor a learned paṇḍit well-versed in the *Bhāṣya* and *Rahasya Granthas* called Parandūr Vaṅgīpuram Vedānta Tātācārya Svāmī, who was hardly 26 years of age. He was initiated into the *saṁnyāsāśrama* and was named Śrī Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika. The elder Jīyar attained *paramapada* in the year Pramādica in the month of

[^154]: This Svāmī was quite old (*vayo-vṛddha*) when he became the pontifical head and was affectionately called 'Tātā-Svāmī' or grandfather because of his age. See *Ācārya vaibhavam*, p. 329.
[]
Puraṭṭāci on Śuklapakṣa caturthī tithi (30.10.1853). He ruled over the pontificate for 6 years and 7 months. His Bṛndāvanam is at Tiruvaḷḷūr.

His Taniyan reads as under:

`श्रीवासहृत्पतिवीरराघवहादिवेदान्तमानिलयवेदशिरोयतीन्द्रेः।`
`संप्रेक्षितं करुणया परिपूर्णबोधं श्रीवीरराघवयतीन्द्रगुरुं भजामः॥`

**33. Śrī Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in Parandūr village in Vaṅgīpuram family in the month of Puraṭṭāci, under star Viśākhā. He was popularly known as Vaṅgīpuram Vidvān Śrī Vedāntācārya Svāmī in his *pūrvāśrama*. He was initated into asceticism and became the pontifical head in the year Pramādica in the month of Āvaṇi on the 10th day of the Śuklapakṣa (12.9.1853).

After assuming the office of the pontificate, he proceeded from Tiruvaḷḷūr to Śrīperumbūdūr, Madhurāntakam, Tirukkōvalūr, Tiruvahin-drapuram, Tiruccitrakūṭam, Śrīmuṣṇam, Kumbhakoṇam, Tiruvinnagar, Pullambūtaṅguḍi, Ādanūr, and Śrī Nṛsiṁhapuram. He stayed there for sometime worshipping at the Bṛndāvanam of his *pūrvācāryas*.[^155]

He then proceeded on a tour of South India, going up to Rāmeśvaram and then to Śrīraṅgam. Later, he proceeded to Tirunārāyaṇapuram and visited the Bṛndāvanam of Śrī Ādi Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa Svāmī . He then visited

[^155]: The Bṛndāvanams of his three *pūrvācāryas* 25th, 26th & 30th Jīyars are at Śrī Nṛsiṁhapuram.
[]
Colasiṁhapuram and returned to Tiruvaḷḷūr. This Jīyar seemed to have followed this itinerary thrice in his lifetime. He is said to have blessed thousands of devotees, performing *samāśrayaṇa* and accepting *bharanyāsa* for those who resorted to his holy feet. He is also said to have given discourses on *Śrībhāṣya* and *Rahasya-granthas*.

It goes to the credit of this Svāmī for having built a *sannidhi* for Svāmī Deśika and installing his idol at Nāgapaṭṭiṇam. In his scholastic erudition, he was placed on par with Rāmānuja, Deśika, Ādi Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa Svāmī, Ṣaṣṭha Parāṅkuśa and Śrīnivāsa Yatīndra Mahādeśika. He was instrumental in adorning the Lord and Śrī at Tiruvaḷḷūr with new ornaments, and acquiring landed property for the temple there. He ordered the construction of a big building for Ahobila Maṭha there. His style of delivering lectures and the comparative ease with which he outclassed and won over his opponents in literary and philosophical debates, attracted the masses to him.

An incident[^156] is related in his pontifical rule which makes interesting reading and bears testimony to the Svāmī's divine charisma. While on a tour of the modern Karnataka State, the Svāmī and his entourage were confronted by a group of dacoits in the thick jungle. The Svāmī is said to have informed the dacoit leader that he could take whatever valuables he wished, but only

[^156]: *Ācārya vaibhavam*, p. 333.
[]
after the Jīyar performed the *dolotsava* to Lord Kṛṣṇa. To this, the dacoit leader agreed and even while the *maṅgalārati* was being performed to the Lord, the dacoit leader and his gang shouted and wailed as if in great pain. The Svāmī then ordered the holy water to be sprinkled on the dacoits. Only after this, they were pacified and it came to be known through the dacoits leader that during the *pūjā* they seemed to be attacked by hordes of lions and the holy water drove them away. The dacoits then fell at the Jīyar's feet begging for forgiveness.

The Jīyar seems to have enjoyed the royal patronage of the Mahārāja of Mysore. The Āsthāna Vidvān of the Mysore Kingdom was one Rāma Śāstrī who underrating the Jīyar's erudition by his youth, invited him to a literary debate[^157], without paying due respect to the Jīyar. But, the *Āsthāna vidvān* was easily defeated and he fell at the Jīyar's feet requesting his pardon for misjudging his scholastic achievements.

The Jīyar wrote the *Guruparamparā* of the Ahobila Maṭha titled *Satsampradāya Muktāvali*, based on the *Ācārya Guṇādarśa* and *Sat Sampradāyasāra* by the earlier Jīyars. He had also written almost half of his autobiography in that book. One of his disciples Tiruvaḷḷūr Thaṭṭai Kṛṣṇamācārya was instrumental in publishing that work.

[^157]: *Ācārya vaibhavam*, p. 335.
[]
He was very popular among the literary cliches of his era because of his interesting philosophical discourses. He was visited often by one Vidvān Tirupputkuḻi Svāmī who used to discuss matters of current interest with him. He donated a sum of Rupees ten thousand for making a golden chariot for Lord Devarāja at Kāñcī which was finished during his life-time.

The Svāmī attained *paramapada* in the year Pramādi in the month of Āvaṇi on Kṛṣṇapakṣa daśamī tithi (10.9.1879). He ruled over the pontificate for 26 years. His Bṛndāvanam is at Tiruvaḷḷūr.

His Taniyan reads as under:

`श्रीरङ्गनाथशठकोपयतीन्द्रपादु-पद्मप्रवणचित्तमुदारबोधम्।`
`श्रीवीरराघवयतीन्द्रकृपावलम्बं श्रीमच्छठारियतिशेखरमाश्रयामः॥`

**34. Śrī Śaṭhakopa Rāmānuja Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in the village of Attipaṭṭu in his uncle's house in the year Śrīmukha in the month of Kārthigai under star Uttarāḍam (November, 1813).

His paternal grandfather belonged to Iñjimeḍu village and had the title of Māḍabhūṣi. This Svāmī was brought up at his maternal grandparents' place at Attipaṭṭu and hence he became known as Attipaṭṭu Jīyar. Reference is made to this Svāmī in the book *Sārabodhinī*, a commentary on *Śrīmad Rahasyatrayasāra* by the 42nd Jīyar. The relevant *maṅgalaśloka* reads as under:
[]
`स्तुतिपुलकाङ्कितगात्रं नृहरेर्बोधाब्धुना लसन्नेत्रम्।`
`वन्दे शठरिपुग्रामावरजसुनीन्द्रं मदीयकुलनाथम्॥`

The Svāmī's *pūrvāśrama* name was Vidvān Māḍabūṣi Śrīnivāsa-rāghavācārya Svāmī. In accordance to the wish of his Ācārya Śrī Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra he donned the ochre robes and became the pontifical head in the year Pramādica in the month of Āvaṇi in Kṛṣṇapakṣa ekādaśī tithi (12.9.1879) on his 61st birthday.

This Svāmī is described as *Vayovṛddha* (old in age) *Jñānavṛddha* (ripe in knowledge) and *Śīlavṛddha* (perfect in conduct) by his disciples.[^158] He was a *pañcakāla-parāyaṇa* and an epitome of a *paramaikāntin*. He was popularly called Ṛṣi Svāmī because he had learnt all the four Vedas. He has many works to his credit. They are as follows:

*Śrī Nṛsiṁhaṣaṣṭipādavārṇanam, Adhikaraṇa Sārāvalī Vyākhyāna, Nyāsaviṁśati Vyākhyāna, Sāmānyaviśeṣādinyāyasaṅgraha, Kavihṛdaya-rañjanī, Ākāśāśrayasamarthana, Ānantya- nirṇaya, Brahmasūtrārtha- mañjarī, Maṇipravāḷa Gītāvyākhyānam, Sāradīpikāhṛdayam, Vikṣāraṇya māhātmyam, Maṇipravāḷa Vyākhyāna* on *Nālāyirappadi, Tiruevvuḷ vaimaḻi* in Tamil, *Aḍaikalappattu* for *Śrī Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha, Kiṅgrheśa stuti*, and *Vedagiri Varṇanam*.

[^158]: *Ācārya vaibhavam*, p. 338.
[]
The *Aḍaikalapattu* on Śrī Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha is being recited daily in the worship of the Lord in the Ahobila Maṭha as also in the houses of Śrīsannidhi disciples. Interesting anecdotes are related extolling the Svāmī's *prabhāva* and *sākṣātkāra* of Lord Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha.[^159] The following *śloka* was also prevalent in the Jīyar's time regarding his *saulabhya* (easy accessibility).

`न चलति निजवर्णधर्मतो यः सम्मतिरात्मसुहृद्विपक्षपक्षे।`
`न हरति न च हन्ति किञ्चिदुच्चैः सितमनसस्तमवेहि विष्णुभक्तम्॥`

The Jīyar stayed at Tiruvaḷḷūr for sometime. Because of his failing health he could not go on religious tours, though he wished to visit many *divyadeśas*. During his stay at Tiruvaḷḷūr he decked the Lord Vīrarāghava with many ornaments and also ordered a golden chariot to be made for the Lord which could be used during festival times. The Jīyar Svāmī used to call Lord Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha as Mahāsvāmī and Lord Vīrarāghava as Māsvāmī (*Mā* meaning 'mine or my' in Telugu, *Mā* also means Lakṣmī and *Mā* meaning the offering of sweet flour to the Lord on (*amāvasyā*) the new moon day). It is to be noted that the rituals of worship (*pūjākrama*) as devised by this Svāmī (viz., *kaṭṭiyam, eccharika* and *anugraha*) are still being adhered to, for Lord Vīrarāghava.

[^159]: Śrī Purisai Naḍādūr Kṛṣṇamācārya Svāmī has recalled two instances from the Svāmī's life which he had heard from his *pūrvācāryas*. *Ācārya vaibhavam*, pp. 340-346.
[]
The 37th Jīyar Śrī Piḷḷaipākkam Svāmī and the 41st Jīyar resorted to this Svāmī's holy feet for refuge. The former wrote the *Ācārya Saptati* and the latter *Mahāsvāmigadyam*, in praise of this Jīyar.

Having adorned the pontifical throne with great prowess, the Svāmī attained *paramapada* in the year Citrabhānu, in the month of Puraṭṭāci on Kṛṣṇapakṣa daśamī tithi (5.10.1882). He ruled over the pontificate for three years and one month. His Bṛndāvanam is at Tiruvaḷḷūr.

His Taniyan reads as under:

`श्रीमद्वीरराघवदुहानिलिशोरवेङ्ककार्यात्मज-`
`श्रीवासश्रुतिसीमयोगिकुलजिद्ब्रोगीन्द्रवीक्षास्पदम्।`
`विख्यातं सपदिमादिगुरुराट्तर्ष्यं विपाञ्चित्तं`
`वन्दे श्रीशठकोपलक्ष्मणमुनिं वैराग्यवाराकरम्॥`

**35. Śrī Raṅganātha Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in Poṉvilainda Kaḷathūr in Chingleput district in Bhāradvāja Gotra of Vaṅgīpuram family in the month of Vaikāśi under star Keṭṭai. His *pūrvāśrama* name was Vidvān Nṛsiṁhācārya. He was entrusted with the job of looking after the daily rituals in Śrī Sannidhi in the time of Attippaṭṭu Jīyar.

Obeying his Ācārya's command, this Svāmī took to *saṁnyāsāśrama* in the year Citrabhānu in the month of Puraṭṭāci (3.10.1982). He was well
[]
versed in *Tarka śāstra* and was an expert in delivering lectures on *Śrībhāṣya* and other Vedāntic texts.

After staying for sometime in Tiruvaḷḷūr, the Jīyar started on his religious tour, proceeding to Tirumala, Tirupati, Tirunindravūr, Tiruvallikkeṇi, Śrīperumbūdūr, Kāñcī and then to Tūppul. He also visited all the *agrahāras* in and around Kāñcī and then returned to Tiruvaḷḷūr. It was during this Jīyar's time that *saṁprokṣaṇa* was done to the Lord Vīrarāghava temple at Tiruvaḷḷūr.

The Jīyar was of a generous disposition and no one who came to visit him and pay his respects went empty handed.[^160] The Jīyar is said to have done *samāśrayaṇa* to the 42nd Jīyar (of Iñjimeḍu) Vidvān Tirukkoṭṭiyūr Svāmī. It is also said that Piḷḷaippākkam Jīyar (37th Jīyar) looked after the affairs of the Maṭha during the Jīyar's pontifical period.

He attained *paramapada* in the year Sarvadhārī in the month of Āḍi on Śuklapakṣa caturthī tithi (10.8.1888). He ruled over the pontificate for 5 years and 10 months. His Bṛndāvanam is at Tiruvaḷḷūr.

[^160]: Śrī Purisai Naḍādūr Kṛṣṇamācārya Svāmī relates a couple of incidents in the Jīyar's pontifical period illustrating his generosity. See *Ācārya vaibhavam*, pp. 349-350.
[]
His Taniyan reads as under:

`श्रीमच्छ्रीवीरराघवद्रुतिभकुद्गुरुसद्वपादाब्जभृङ्गं`
`श्रीमच्छ्रीरघुङ्गवमनगुरुशेर्खलधवेदान्तयुग्मम्।`
`श्रीमन्नारायणाब्धुतिशिखरतारारातिरामानुजार्य-`
`प्रेक्षापात्रं भजामो गुरुवरमनघं रङ्गनाथं यतीन्द्रम्॥`

**36. Śrī Śrīnivāsa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in Kāñcī district at Parandūr in the month of Āḍi under star Pūṣya. His *pūrvāśrama* name was Vidvān Vaṅgīpuram Raṅgācārya Svāmī. He became the pontifical head in the month of Āḍi in the year Sarvadhārī under star Svāti (13.8.1888).[^161]

He stayed for sometime at Tiruvaḷḷūr, worshipping the Lord there and giving discourses on the Śrīvaiṣṇava religion and philosophy to his disciples. He was the brother of the 33rd Jīyar in his *pūrvāśrama* and was a famous exponent of *Śrībhāṣya* during his times.[^162] The Jīyar visited the following

[^161]: There was a legal controversy in the appointment of this Jīyar. His predecessor, the 35th Jīyar (Kaḷathūr Svāmi) attained *paramapada* without appointing a successor. The 36th Jīyar was appointed by the disciples of the Ahobila Maṭha who were gathered at Tiruvaḷḷūr. Some of the disciples who were located outside Tiruvaḷḷūr desired to install the well-known pandit of Coladeśa, Śrī Saṭṭarka Vācaspati Kurucci Raṅgācārya Svāmī and hence filed a case in the High Court. However the judgement was in favour of Parandūr Svāmī and the problem was legally resolved. The related case and the ensuing judgement are recorded in the corresponding *Law Journal*. See *Ācārya vaibhavam*, p. 353.
[^162]: It is stated that when this Jīyar attained *paramapada* Śrīmuṣṇam Śrī Svarṇam Kṛṣṇamācārya Svāmī is believed to have said that *Śrībhāṣyam* itself is 'dead and gone'. See *Ācārya vaibhavam*, p. 353.
[]
*divyadeśas* Śrīperumbūdūr, Kāñcī, Madurāntakam, Tiruahindrapuram, Kumbhakoṇam, Pullambūtaṅguḍi, Ādanūr, and Śrīraṅgam. He was respected for his depth of knowledge in *Tarka śāstra, Vedānta śāstra* and *Śrībhāṣya*.

The Jīyar proceeded to Pādūr at the request of his disciples and stayed for sometime there lecturing on Vedānta Philosophy. He attained *paramapada* in the year Viḷambi in the month of Mārgaḻi, on pūrṇimā tithi (27.12.1898). The Jīyar's Bṛndāvanam is in the western *prākāra* of the Pādūr temple. His idol has been installed there by the 40th Jīyar later. He ruled over the pontificate for 10 years and 4 months.

His Taniyan reads as under:

`श्रीनारायणवेदमीलिपतिराट्पादारविन्दाश्रयं`
`ख्यातश्रीशठकोपदेशिकमणेर्लब्धागमान्तद्वयम्।`
`श्रीमद्रघुवरीणयोगिवरण्यस्यात्मरक्षाभरं`
`सेवे श्रीनिधियोगिवर्यमनघं निर्बाधबोधोदयम्॥`

**37. Śrī Vīrarāghava Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in Piḷḷaippākkam near Śrīperumbūdūr in the year Krodhi in the month of Māśi (March 1845) under star Pūṣya. His father's name was Vīrarāghavācārya Svāmī, belonging to the famous Komāṇḍūr Iḷayavalli family. His *pūrvāśrama* name was Gopālācārya and he learnt the *ubhayavedānta* at the feet of his father. He had his *pañcasaṁskāra* done by the famous Tirupputkuḻi Svāmī (Mahāmahopādhyāya Kṛṣṇa Tātācārya). Completing *Adhyātma śāstra* first under the 33rd Jīyar, he studied next under
[]
the 34th Jīyar. Recognising his erudition, the 34th Jīyar (Attipaṭṭu Aḻagiasiṅgar) appointed him as the *Śrīkāryam* of the Ahobila Maṭha which post he continued under the 35th Jīyar also. He had his *prapatti* done by the 34th Jīyar. He learnt *Divyaprabandham* from a *Paramaikāntin* Śrī Śaṭhakopācārya of Kāyār.

Then he proceeded to the *divyadeśas* of the South doing *maṅgalāśāsana* to the Āḻvārs en route. He participated in the Brahmotsava at Āḻvār Tirunagarī during the month of Māsi. He developed *vairāgya* and distaste for worldly life and had his *āpatsaṁnyāsa* (immediate asceticism) done by his Bhagavadviṣaya Ācārya Pūvirundavalli Śrīnivāsarāghavācārya Svāmī. He had his *preṣamantropadeśa* from Teṅkanikoṭṭai Svāmī at Tiruvaḷḷūr in the year Heviḷambi in the month of Āḍi on pūrṇimā tithi under star Uttarāṣāḍhā and was conferred the name of *Śrī Vīrarāghava Śaṭhakopa*. After the *Saṅkalpamahotsava*, the Svāmī proceeded to Kāñcī. He came to know that the 36th Jīyar had attained *paramapada* and complying to the request of his disciples he became the pontifical head in the year Viḷambi in the month of Thai (31.1.1899).

The Jīyar proceeded to Tiruvahindrapuram where he restored the *utsavas* in the temple after settling the dispute among the Śrīvaiṣṇavas there.[^163]

[^163]: *Śrī Nṛsiṁha Priyā*, Twelfth Annual Number, English edition, p. 35.
[]
He remained there to supervise the Brahmotsava in the temple and has documented his experiences in a beautiful record named *Vedāntadeśikotsava Vaibhavam* for the sake of posterity. Later, he proceeded to Śrī Nṛsiṁhapuram where he took ill suddenly and attained *paramapada* in the year Vikārī in the month of Mārgaḻi on pūrṇimā tithi (16.12.1899). This Svāmī did not nominate his successor and hence there was an interregnum for about five and a half years between 1899-1905. The Jīyar's Bṛndāvanam is at Śrī Nṛsiṁhapuram. He ruled over the pontificate for eleven months.

His Taniyan reads as under:

`अस्त्यत्रैव विशेषो बुध इति शठजित्सूनुहृन्मान्या मुनिभ्या`
`मेकीभूयोदितस्यामिह निरुपाधिकं प्रेषितं सद्गुरुभ्याम्।`
`वेदान्तद्वन्द्वमन्त्रप्रविविदिषुमुखैः शिक्षितं शान्तिगुप्त्यैः`
`आदर्शं श्रीवीरराघवशठमथनगुरुं संयमीन्द्रं भजामि॥`

**38. Śrī Śrīnivāsa Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in the year Siddhārthi in the month of Thai on Śukla dvādaśī under star Tiruvādirai (Janurary 1860) at Kumbhakoṇam. His *pūrvāśrama* name was Tirukkuḍantai Ilanagar Gadādharapuram Śrīvatsāṅka Vidvān Cakravarthi Veṅkaṭācārya Svāmī. He was well-versed in *Tarkaśāstra* and had the good fortune of delivering lectures on Vedānta in the immediate presence of the 37th Jīyar and won accolades from him. As there was an interregnum of five and half years between the previous Jīyar and this Jīyar, the daily rituals of the Maṭha were carried out by the Śrīkāryam svāmī.
[]
The disciples appealed to the Government to appoint a head to the Ahobila Maṭha. The British Governor ordered the preparation of electoral rolls of the Maṭha's disciples and after the casting of votes, it was found that the majority favoured the Gadādharapuram Svāmī to be the head of the Maṭha.

The Maṭha rose once again to become the centre of influence and revered seat of learning. The Jīyar became the pontifical head in the year Viśvāvasu in the month of Āḍi in pūrṇimā tithi under star Uttarāḍham (17.7.1905) at Nṛsiṁhapuram. He stayed for sometime there enlightening his disciples on *Granthacatuṣṭaya* and doing *pañcasaṁskāra* and *prapatti* to his devotees. He proceeded on *sañcāra* to Pullambūtaṅguḍi, Ādanūr, Kumbhakoṇam, Tiruvinnagar, Teralundūr, Tiruviṇḍalūr, Tirukkaṇḍiyūr, Tanjore, Appakūḍathān, Anbil, Vaḍuvūr, Tiruppuliyūr and Tirukkaṇṇapuram.

A devotee from north named Bālamukundācārya became his disciple and it was with his help that the Uttara Ahobila Maṭha was established at Puṣkaram. He also renovated a number of Maṭha-buildings and Bṛndāvanams of previous Jīyars. Knowing that his end was nearing, he appointed a learned *Vyākaraṇa* Vidvān Raṅgācārya Svāmī as his successor. He attained *paramapada* in the year Saumya, in the month of Citra, on Kṛṣṇapakṣa aṣṭamī tithi (12.5.1909). His Bṛndāvanam is at Śrī Nṛsiṁhapuram. His idol was installed by the 40th Jīyar later. There are two available works about this Jīyar. They are []
Kārakkurichi Vaṅgīpuram Vidvān and *Vaibhava Prakāśikā* by Vaṅgīpuram Raṅgācārya Svāmī.

His Taniyan reads as under:

`श्रीमच्छठारिजिह्वर्यवीरराघवशठारियतिशेखरदेशिकेन्द्रः।`
`संप्रेक्षितं करुणया परिपूर्णबोधं श्रीश्रीनिवासशठकोपमुनिं भजामः॥`

**39. Śrī Parāṅkuśa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in Rājamannārkōil (Mannārguḍi) in Urupattūr Cakravartī family in the month of Viśākhā under star Bharaṇi. He became the pontifical head in the year Saumya, in the month of Viśākhā on Śuklapakṣa dvitīyā tithi (21.5.1909). He was known in his *pūrvāśrama* as Vyākaraṇa Raṅgācārya. He took to the ochre robes at the instance of the 38th Jīyar. He visited Pullambūtaṅguḍi Ādanūr, and Rājamannārkōil. He renovated the Maṭha at Mannārguḍi and was instrumental in making a silver *maṇḍapa* for Lord Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha. He also ordered the construction of the northern wall at the temple of Lord Vīrarāghava at Tiruvaḷḷūr. He performed *pañcasaṁskāra* and *bharanyāsa* to his devotees and gave lectures on philosophy and religion as propounded in the *granthacatuṣṭaya*.

Feeling that his health was failing, he called upon Kārakkuricci Vidvān Veṅkaṭakṛṣṇamācārya Svāmī to take to the ascetic order and succeed him. He named his successor Śrī Raṅganātha Śaṭhakopa. He attained *paramapada* in the year Rākṣasa in the month of Viśākhā in Śuklapakṣa pañcamī tithi

[]
(20.5.1915). His Bṛndāvanam is at Mannārguḍi. He ruled the pontificate for six years.

His Taniyan reads as under:

`श्रीवीरराघवयतीन्द्रपदाब्जभृङ्गं श्रीमच्छठारियतित्त्रयं कृपाप्तबोधम्।`
`श्री श्रीनिवासशठजिह्वलिपुर्यधीशान् पराङ्कुशयतीन्द्रगुरुं भजामः॥`

**40. Śrī Raṅganātha Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in Kārakkuricci Agrahāram on the banks of the river Tāmraparaṇī in the Vaṅgīpuram family in the year Virodhikṛt in the month of Mārgaḻi under star Viśākhā. He became the pontifical head in the year Pramādica in the month of Caitra under star Pūṣya (17.4.1913). After the 39th Jīyar attained *paramapada* in May 1915, this Svāmī proceeded on his *divyadeśasañcāra* to Śrīraṅgam, Āḻvār Tirunagari, Tirumāliruñjōlai and then proceeded to Hyderabad.

During that period, Ahobilam had become inaccessible because of the fear of dacoits and evil spirits. It should be said to the credit of this Svāmī that he was able to allay these fears of the devotees by his *mantric* powers. He visited Ahobilam and performed worship to the *Nava Nṛsiṁhas* there. Many devotees resorted to his holy feet for freedom from miseries of this world and bliss in the world thereafter. He ordered many gold and silver vessels to be made, which were utilised for the worship of the Lord. He built Maṭhas at many places and was instrumental in making the Maṭha rich and prosperous.

[]
He wrote the *Maṇipravāḷa Dīpikā* which elucidates in simple term, the philosophical truths found in the *Śrībhāṣya*. He also wrote the *Satsampradāya Prakāśikā* and *Śrībhāṣya dūṣaṇaparihāra*.[^164] He also established an Agrahāra called *Śrī Raṅganātha Śaṭhakopapuram*. Many treatises have been written extolling the Jīyar's erudition - *Yatīndra Guṇadarpaṇa, Śrī Raṅganātha Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika Śatakam* and *Paramācārya Navaka*. His devotion to Lord Nṛsiṁha earned accolades for him from his disciples who lovingly called him "*Śrī Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha Divya Pādukā Sevaka*."

He visited Tirumala, Tirunārāyaṇapuram, Madurai and Tuvarimān. Realising that his health was failing, he called upon one of his disciples, Śrī Gopāla Rāmabhadrācārya Svāmī to succeed him as the pontifical head. He attained *paramapada* in the year Dundubhi, in the month of Thai on Kṛṣṇapakṣa trayodaśī tithi (14.1.1923). His Bṛndāvanam is at Tuvarimān *agrahara*. He ruled the pontificate for 9 years and 9 months.

His Taniyan reads as under:

`श्रीमच्छठारियतिशेखरलब्धबोधं श्रीरङ्गनाथयतिपुर्यकृपेकपाम्।`
`श्रीमत्पराङ्कुशयतीन्द्रदयावलम्बं श्रीरङ्गनाथशठकोपमुनिं भजामः॥`

[^164]: All these works are published.

[]
**41. Śrī Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in Kārakkuricci agrahāram in Vādhūla gotra in the year Ānanda in the month of Mārgaḻi under Pūraṭṭādi star (Dec. 1854). His *pūrvāśrama* name was Taṭṭai Gopāla Rāmabhadrācārya Svāmī. He became the pontifical head in the year Dundubi in the month of Thai (17.1.1923). He was the oldest Jīyar to became the pontifical head of Ahobila Maṭha. It is to be noted that even at this advanced age, this Svāmī performed his daily duties (*nityakarmas*) to perfection. He gave religious discourses on the *granthacatuṣṭaya* as also on *Nyāyasiddhāñjana* and *Śatadūṣaṇī*. He travelled from Tuvarimān up to Rāmeśvaram in the South and Tirumala in the North. Taking into consideration his age and the prevailing mode of transport and poor road conditions, his *divyadeśa sañcāra* performing *maṅgalāśāsana* to the Lord and doing *pañcasaṁskāra* should be commended. He has authored the following works: *Śrī Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha Dhyānasopāna, Śrī Vedapādāśīstava, Daśāvatāra Vedapādastava, Nityaprārthanākārikāvalī, Ācāryadinacaryā* and *Śrī Mahāsvāmigadya* (on the 34th Jīyar).

The Jīyar was able to acquire nearly two and a half lakh Rupees worth of land for the Ahobila Maṭha. He ordered the construction of new buildings for Ahobila Maṭha at Tirumala, Tiruppullāṇi and Vaḍuvūr. He installed the idols of the 33rd and 34th Jīyars in the silver *maṇḍapa*. He also installed the idol of 40th Jīyar and also his own image at Tiruvaḷḷūr. He also made anew

[]
the Śrī Śaṭhāri in the silver *maṇṭapa*. Finding his health to be failing, he appointed Māḍabhūṣi Iñjimeḍu Vidvān Raṅganāthācārya as his successor after initiating him into the ascetic order with full honours. He was named Śrī Raṅga Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika. However, he recovered soon and for nearly 13 years both the Jīyars adorned the Ahobila Maṭha. He attained *paramapada* on Śuklapakṣa pañcamī tithi. His Bṛndāvanam is at *Daśāvatāra sannidhi* at Śrīraṅgam.

His Taniyan reads as under:

`श्रीमच्छठारिंशठकोपयतीन्द्ररङ्ग-कार्यात्मजातमुनिभ्यः गुरुसार्वभौमैः।`
`संप्रेक्षितं करुणया परिपूर्णबोधं लक्ष्मींनृसिंहशठकोपमुनिं भजामः॥`

**42. Śrī Śrīraṅga Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in Iñjimeḍu in Bhāradvāja Gotra in the year Bahudhānya in the month of Thai under star Uttarāṣāḍha (21.1.1879). He was known in his *pūrvāśrama* as Vidvān Iñjimeḍu Raṅganāthācārya. He had his Vedāntic teachings under Śrīmuṣṇam Svāmī (Svarṇam Kṛṣṇamācārya Svāmī) and had *bharanyāsa* done by him. In recognition of this Svāmī's erudition he was appointed as the *Āsthāna vidvān* by the 41st Jīyar. Under instructions from his *guru*, he wrote *sampradāya granthas* like *Uktiniṣṭhābharaṇam, Nyāsaniṣṭhāmīmāṁsā* and also *vyākhyāna* on the *Rahasyatrayasāra* called the *Sārabodhinī*. He also wrote *śrāddhamantrabhāṣyam, Upākarmanirṇaya, Kṛttikādīpanirṇaya, Śrīvaiṣṇavasadācāranirṇaya* and *Gītārthasaṅgra-

[]
*havyākhyāna*. He wrote a *bhūmikā* (Preface) for *Tattvatīkā* and *Viśiṣṭādvaita Kośa* (a dictionary of Viśiṣṭādvaita terms). He was initiated into asceticism in the year Śukla in the month of Caitra (April 1929). He became the pontifical head in the year Viṣu, in the month of Aippaśi (24.10.1941). He was instrumental in establishing a *Vedapāṭhaśālā* at Madhurāntakam and also bringing out a monthly journal of Ahobila Maṭha, *Śrī Nṛsiṁhapriyā* and in establishing a Maṭha at Bombay. The Veda Pāṭhaśālā has since developed into a famous centre of learning and is flourishing well in present day, and is sought after by young students eager to learn the Vedas. The Monthly Journal is having a wide circulation in the present day. The Chief Editor of the journal is the Ahobila Maṭha Jīyar and his editorial provides interesting reading to students of philosophy and religion and laymen alike. The Ahobila Maṭha at Bombay (Chembūr) is the centre of attraction to the Maṭha's devotees there, and is flourishing well under the patronage of Śrīvaiṣṇava *Śrīsannidhiśiṣyas*.

He travelled from Śrīraṅgam to Hyderabad and then to Tirunārāyaṇapuram, Kāñcī and Tiruvaḷḷūr. Finding that his health was failing, he appointed Paruthipaṭṭu Vaṅgīpuram Vidvān Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁhācārya Svāmī as his successor who was formally initiated into the ascetic fold in Vikṛti year in the month of Thai (7.2.1951). For two years both the Jīyars adorned the Ahobila Maṭha and enlightened the disciples in Śrīvaiṣṇava Sampradāya. The

[]
elder Jīyar attained *paramapada* in the year Nandana, in the month of Māsi in Kṛṣṇapakṣa prathamā tithi (1.3.1953). His Bṛndāvanam is at Tiruvaḷḷūr. He ruled the pontificate for twenty-four years and one month.

Śrī Pādūr Purāṇam Svāmī (Śrī Rāghavācārya) has written a work called *Vaibhava Sudhā* in 500 verses about this Svāmī.

His Taniyan reads as under:

`श्रीरङ्गेशयतीन्दुना करुणास्री स्रावितिं प्रेषितं`
`ख्यातश्रीरङ्गसिंहकारिमुनिनाऽऽबुद्धजेन्द्रिन्द्रम्।`
`दान्तिशान्तिदयादिभिः शुभगुणैर्भान्तं बुधाग्रेसरं`
`श्रीमद्रङ्गशठारियोगिनृपतिं श्रेयोनिधिं संश्रये॥`

**43. Śrī Vīrarāghava Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born to Devanārvilāham Vidvān Paruthipaṭṭu Vaṅgīpuram Tiruvenkaṭācārya Svāmī in the year Plava, in the month of Kṛttikā under star Pūrāḍa. His *pūrvāśrama* name was Vidvān Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁhācārya Svāmī. He graduated from Tiruvaiyāru College taking his degree in Tarka and was awarded the Tarka Śiromaṇi title. He was also the Principal of Madhurāntakam College. He was a *pañcakāla parāyaṇa* who considered his own house to be a temple. He took to asceticism in Vikṛti year in the month of Thai (9.2..1951). He travelled from Rāmeśvaram in the south to Himālayas in the north and performed one of his *cāturmāsyavratas* at Ṛṣīkeśa. He built *Vedapāṭhaśālās* at Madhurāntakam and Pādūr and renovated the Rājagopuram at Pullambūtaṅguḍi and Tiruvaḷḷūr. He renovated the

[]
Ahobila Maṭhas at Cuddappa, Vānamāmalai and Tirukkōṭṭiyūr. Many golden utensils were ordered to be made for the worship of Lord Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha. A golden palanquin was also made for the Lord.

The Jīyar contributed many articles to journals like *Vedāntadīpikā* and *Śrī Nṛsiṁhapriyā* and also published some works of Attipaṭṭu Jīyar. After finishing his *cāturmāsyavrata* at Ṛṣīkeśa, the Jīyar came to Delhi, where he stayed for sometime doing *pañcasaṁskāra* and *prapatti* to those who resorted to his holy feet.

While returning South from Delhi, the Jīyar fell ill and attained *paramapada* at Naimiśāraṇya in the year Hemalamba, in the month of Kṛttikā on Śuklapakṣa tṛtīya tithi (24.11.1957). His Bṛndāvanam is at Naimiśāraṇya. He was the only Jīyar to have travelled so far across the length and breadth of India. He ruled the pontificate for five years and ten months.

His Taniyan reads as under:

`श्रीमत् श्रीरङ्घपूणवीरराघवारिपुणा संयमीन्द्रेण दृब्`
`न्यस्तात्मानं नृसिंहं नृहरिश्ठजिह्वागिणेतुः प्रसादात्।`
`प्राज्ञ-श्रीरङ्गकारिप्रभवयतिपतिः प्रापितलक्ष्मींनृसिंहा-`
`स्थानं सेवे यतीन्द्रं सकलगुणनिधिं वीरराघ्वशठारिम्॥`

**44. Śrī Vedānta Deśika Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Jīyar was born in Mukkūr on the banks of the river Ceiyyār to Vidvān Raṅgācārya Svāmī and Raṅganāyakī, in the year Manmatha in the

[]
month of Āvaṇi under star Hastā (August 1895). His *pūrvāśrama* name was Mukkūr Rājagopālācārya Svāmī. He under_c_went his studies in the *Vedapāṭhaśālā* at Śrīmuṣṇam. He studied Śrīvaiṣṇava theology under renowned scholars like Taiyyār Māḍabhūṣi Śrīnivāsācārya, Śrīmuṣṇam Kṛṣṇamācārya and Naḍādūr Kṛṣṇamācārya. He also gained a strong foundation in *Tarka śāstra* from Śrī Cakravartyācārya Svāmī of Tillayāmbur. Śrī Kāśī Kuppusvāmī Aiyaṅgār taught him the *Divyaprabandham*. Soon he established himself as an able teacher and began to give religious and philosophical discourses which were appreciated by connossieur and common man alike.

However he was called upon by the 40th Jīyar to accompany him in his wide travels at the instance of the 41th Jīyar . He took charge of the affairs of the Ahobila Maṭha at Kāñcī. He became the Āsthāna Vidvān of the Ahobila Maṭha during the reign of the 42nd Jīyar.

During the brief period of the 43rd Jīyar's reign, Śrī Rājagopālācārya accompanied him in his sojourn to North India, and when the Jīyar left for his heavenly abode in the holy land of Naimiśāraṇya, he was called upon by his disciples to take over the leadership of the Maṭha. He was reluctant at first, but he found the call of duty to be irresistible and in the year Hemalamba in the month of Kṛthikā under Śravaṇa star, he donned the ochre robes and became the pontifical head on 27.11.1957 and settled down to purposive work. Before

[]
returning to the South, he visited Puṣkara where his lectures in Sanskrit and Hindi on *Śrīmad Rahasyatrayasāra* received wide acclaim. From Puṣkara he went to Tirumala and then to Tirukkaṇḍalam where he composed *Śrī Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha Karāvalamba Stotra*. During the first 25 years of his pontificate he travelled far and wide reaching upto Rāmeśvaram in the South, widening the circle of Śrīvaiṣṇavas and strengthening the base of Śrīvaiṣṇavism by training scholars in Śrīvaiṣṇava lore and renovating Vaiṣṇava temples.

The annual Mālola Vidvatsadas became a memorable event in his time, which attracted scholars from far and wide. He was also instrumental in setting to metre the *Śrībhāṣya* to make it easy for memorising. He was endowed with excellent communication skills and could put across his point to the layman and philosopher alike. He has authored the following works:-

*Śrī Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha Karāvalamba Stotra, Śārīraka Adhikaraṇakramabodhinī, Brahmasūtrārthapadyamālikā, Viśiṣṭādvaita-siddhāntatattvasaṅgraha, Lakṣmīnṛsiṁhaprapatti, Dayāsāgaraśataka, Pañcāmṛta stotra, Maṅgalamālikā* relating to all the Jīyars of Ahobila Maṭha and *Sadupadeśa*.

His *Dayāsāgaraśatakam* is in praise of Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha and the Jīyars of Ahobila Maṭha who have propagated the worship of the Lord Mālola Nṛsiṁha all over the country. Written in simple Sanskrit, the poem has universal appeal. The Lord is imagined as an ocean of compassion

[]
(*dayāsāgara*), a fire that burns the evil past of the devotees, a repository of good qualities mentioned in the *Tāpanīya Upaniṣad* and an all-encompassing companion who takes within his fold the prayers of Brahmins, Ceñchus the hunters, farmers and soldiers with equal pleasure. From the 53rd verse onwards Mālola journeys down the hierarchy of the Jīyars of Ahobila Maṭha. The 98th verse is autobiographical.

In keeping with the vision of the founder of Ahobila Maṭha, the Jīyar was a great builder. He established a Bṛndāvana at Naimiśāraṇya for the 43rd Jīyar, built a temple at Mukkūr, Nammāḻvār's *sannidhi* at Kāñcī, established a Maṭha at Pullambūtaṅguḍi, built a *sannidhi* for Tāyār at Iñjimeḍu, a Rājagopuram at Ahobilam, a *maṇṭapa* for Citra-utsava at Tiruvaḷḷūr, a temple to Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha, Lakṣmī Nārāyaṇa and Lord Hayagrīva and a *Kalyāṇamaṇṭapa* at Bombay, the Hṛttāpanāśinī tank at Tiruvaḷḷūr, and established Ahobila Maṭhas at Tiruvahindrapuram, Hyderabad, Bangalore and Vānamāmalai, and a large building for the Sanskrit College at Madhurāntakam. When one lists all these intellectual and administrative achievements in a *saṁnyāsin*'s life, a good deal of which has to be spent in the ritural worship of the presiding deity Śrī Malola Nṛsiṁha, one will be struck with a sense of wonder.

All this work pales into insignificance beside the Jīyar's launching the construction of the Śrīraṅgam Rājagopuram when he entered his 84th year, in

[]
1979. When he intimated this idea (which was conveyed to him through a dream by Lord Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha) to his disciples, they were wonderstruck by the magnitude of the task as also the Jīyar's advanced age. But backed by immense reserves of will power, and armed with his engineering intuition and guided by child-like faith he went ahead with his task ordained by the Lord. Making arrangements for financial expenses which crossed the one crore mark, he personally supervised the construction work day in and day out. The residents of Śrīraṅgam will bear ample testimony to his untiring efforts which reached completion in 1985. With 13 tiers built at a cost of Rs.15 million, the Rājagopuram is the tallest tower in Asia, 165 feet in length and 150 feet in breadth and rising up to 226 feet in height.

An intellectual, a spiritual guide, a generous benefactor, a great builder, the Jīyar was also a great lover of art. Despite his tiring schedule, the Jīyar always had time to encourage artists who spread the message of *bhakti* (devotion). When he found that his health was failing, he called upon the *āsthāna Vidvān* Villivalam Kṛṣṇamācārya to take over the Maṭha affairs after granting him the ochre robes in the year Prajāpati, in the month of Aippasi (21.10.91). This Jīyar performed over 35 *cāturmāsyavratas* and attained heavenly abode in the year Aṅgirasa in the month of Āḍi (16.8.92). His Bṛndāvanam is at Śrīraṅgam.

[]
His Taniyan reads as under:

`श्रीरङ्गनाथशठकोपयतीन्द्रदृष्टं लक्ष्मींनृसिंहलज्जितकरुणैकपात्रम्।`
`श्रीवीरराघवशठकोपमुह्यम् वेदान्तदेशिकयतीन्द्रमहं प्रपद्ये॥`

**45. Śrī Nārāyaṇa Yatīndra Mahādeśika**

This Svāmī was born in Villivalam in North Arcot district in Akṣaya year in the month of Kārtikai under star Uttaraṭṭādi (December 12,1926) to Paḷaveri Cakravartī Nṛsiṁhācārya Svāmī and Raṅganāyakī. His *pūrvāśrama* name was Kṛṣṇamācārya Svāmī. He studied at the feet of his father, but after his father's demise at a very early age, he turned to his elder brother Nārāyaṇācārya Svāmī for guidance. He had his *upākarma* done by his elder brother at the appropriate time. The requisite basic education necessary for under - standing the Śrīvaiṣṇava philosophy was imparted by the Svāmī's elder brother who was conferred the title of *Vedāntavādavadūka* for his proficiency in philosophy.

Śrī Kṛṣṇamācārya was a student of the Madras University passing the Nyāya Śiromaṇi Certificate in 1949 with honours, from the Madurāntakam college. He received the first prize for general proficiency. Later, he had the good fortune of learning the *nyāya* and *mīmāṁsa śāstras* at the feet of the 42nd and 43rd Jīyars of Ahobila Maṭha. He had served as Tamil Pandit in the Ramakrishna Vidyalaya, Chingleput for four years from 1956 and later, as

[]
Nyāya Professor in the Śrī Ahobila Maṭha Sanskrit College, Madurāntakam till 1965. He was appointed as the *Āsthāna Vidvān* of the Maṭha by the 44th Jīyar in 1966 and he had been the joint-editor of the journal "*Śrī Nṛsiṁha Priyā*" (Tamil) since 1982.

Settling down at Madras Śrī Kṛṣṇamācārya had been regularly giving discourses in *Śrībhāṣya, Śrīmad Rahasyatrayasāra, Śrīmad Rāmāyaṇa, Śrīmad Bhāgavatam, Tiruppāvai* and *Bhagavad Gītā* at various places in the country for the past 30 years. His discourses delivered in the conventional style on the *granthacatuṣṭaya* were a source of perennial interest to his friends and disciples. He was a Board Member of the Ahobila Maṭha Sanskrit Vidyā Abhivardhinī Sabhā which manages the Maṭha's Oriental High Schools at Madurāntakam and West Mambalam, as also the Sanskrit College at Madurāntakam and in this capacity his contribution is significant. His scholarly commentaries on the *Upaniṣads* and *Viṣṇu Pūrāṇa* which are published serially in the "*Śrī Nṛsiṁha Priyā*" have now been compiled and published in book form by Śrī Viśiṣṭādvaita Research Centre, Madras.

The 44th Jīyar suddenly took ill in October 1991, and immediately sent for Śrī Kṛṣṇamācārya to take up the reins of the Maṭha. His formal induction into *saṁnyāsāśrama* amidst traditional rituals took place on October 21st 1991. It will be significant to note that Śrī Kṛṣṇamācārya had his *pañcasaṁskāra* from the 42nd Jīyar, *bharanyāsa* under 43rd Jīyar and

[]
*preṣamantropadeśa* from the 44th Jīyar at Śrī Ahobilam. He recalls to this day, with great veneration, his close association with these Ācāryas and mentions nostalgically many interesting ancedotes during the short period when he was called upon to attend to the personal needs of the 42nd Jīyar for sometime.[^165]

Once the formal *paṭṭābhiṣeka* cermony (24.8.1992) was over, His Holiness took the *āśrama* name of "*Śrī Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa Śrī Nārāyaṇa Yatīndra Mahādeśika*"[^166] and donned the *haṁsamudrā* (signet ring) to execute the administrative duties which invariably form part of the pontifical head's officaldom. He took to his task with seriousness, and the five years of his pontifical rule are enough testimony to his capacity as a good administrator. He was a scholar (*vidvān*) and a capable administrator (*samartha*).[^167] The *Śrīkāryam* of Ahobila Maṭha has listed four outstanding qualities of the present Jīyar. They are: *dātṛtva, priyavaktṛtva, dhīratva* and *ucitajñatā*.[^168] which qualities cannot be acquired, but are only natural to him. The Jīyar has stated in no uncertain terms after his assumption of the pontifical office that his duty was only to live up to the training, guidance and ideals of his *pūrvācāryas* and carry on the torch of their glorious tradition for the benefit

[^165]: *Śrī Nṛsiṁha Priyā*, part 2, Nov. 1994, p. 50. See also *Saptati Malar*, p. vii, 21st Nov. 1996.
[^166]: In respectful memory of his brother Śrī Nārāyaṇācārya.
[^167]: *Saptati Malar*, p. 59.
[^168]: Ibid. p. 58.

[]
of *śiṣyas* and aspirants. Adhering to the guidelines laid by Svāmī Deśika, His Holiness enlightens the masses by his discourses and interesting educative writings, and performs his daily and enjoined duties through his dedicated *ārādhanā* to Śrī Mālola Nṛsiṁha - "*Adhyātmagranthanirmāṇam, anekeṣāṁ ca bodhanam, arcāvatāra sevā ca*."

The Jīyar took upon himself the task of making the forest shrines of Ahobilam more accessible to the devotees, by taking Śrī Mālola Nṛsiṁha (*utsava* deity) to Ahobilam for eight times and providing the pleasure of having the *darśan* of the *mūla* and *utsava* idols in unison for five times starting from 26.11.1992, on 3.3.1993, 3.10.1993, 20.3.1994 and 8.10.1995. He was instrumental in constructing 32 steps leading to the Bhairava tank at Ahobilam at a cost of Rs.15,000. In March 1993, His Holiness bedecked Lord Prahlādavarada at Ahobilam with golden *śaṅkha, cakra* and *abhayahasta*, a golden crown and foot-rest and a golden *yajñopavīta* at a cost of Rs.17 lakhs. In October 1994, he renovated the holy tank in front of the Ahobilam temple. He performed the *abhigamana* and *ijyārādhana* for Śrī Mālola Nṛsiṁha in the *maṇṭhapa* adjoining the tank on 31.10.1996. A new chariot was ordered to be made for Lord Prahlādavarada at a cost of Rs.24 lakhs and this was presented on 5.3.1996 and on this occasion a new pathway leading to Śrī Chatravaṭa Nṛsiṁha *sannidhi* was laid.

[]
The Jīyar's contributions to the renovation of other *divyadeśa* temples are innumerable and his visit to Badrīkāśrama is a memorable one, as those who travelled in his entourage will vouchsafe. Suffice it to say, he has travelled across the length and breadth of India[^169] in his onerous task of carrying out the divine command of Lord Nṛsiṁha. His literary contribution is also very significant. Noteworthy among his works is the *Sudhīpriyā*, a *nithyagrantha* commentary on the *Śrīvaiṣṇavasadācāranirṇaya* of Śrī Raṅganātha Yatīndra, the 26th pontiff. It took nearly seven valuable years to compile this work and its speaks volumes for the Jīyar's *Ācārya bhakthi* because he had undertaken this work at the instance of the 42nd Jīyar. He has performed four *cāturmāsya vratas*. The establishment of several Trusts to take care of the various activities of the Maṭha is a signficant event during the Jīyar's pontifical rule. They are: the Save Trust, Smart Trust, Samrāṭ Trust, Viśiṣṭādvaita Research Centre and Śrī Nṛsiṁha Priyā Trust.[^170] In the midst of his very busy schedule the Jīyar is presently writing a commentary on *Śrīmad Rahasyatrayasāra* which is being published serially in the *Śrī Nṛsiṁha Priyā*.

Carrying the mantle of his forbears in propagating the Śrīvaiṣṇava religion and philosophy, His Holiness, the 45th Jīyar of Ahobila Maṭha

[^169]: For a detailed account of H.H. the Jīyar's sojourns, see *Saptati Malar*, pp. 32-38.
[^170]: For details see *Saptati Malar*, pp. 107 - 108.

[]
demonstrates how spirituality and monasticism can be effectively practised in a secular society.

His Taniyan reads as under:-

`श्रीमदूरङ्गशठारिसंयमिधुरन्धरलब्धधृगान्तसद्व्यं`
`श्रीमद्वीररघुद्वहस्ययमिहृब्जात्स्थायिपादार विन्दाश्रयम्।`
`श्रीमद्देवयदेशिकम्पतेः कारुण्यवीक्षास्पदं`
`सेवे रघुपरीणशासनवशं नारायण योगिनम्॥`

The above is a brief description of the lives of the saints of Śrī Ahobila Maṭha. The onerous task started by Śrī Ādi Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa is continuing into the future also.

---

[]
## SELECT WORKS
A STUDY OF SELECT WORKS OF THE JĪYARS OF ŚRĪ AHOBILA MAṬHA

An attempt is made in this chapter to present a brief study of some works of the Pontiffs of Śrī Ahobila Maṭha. The works are selected on the basis of their literary and philosophical importance. Smaller *stotras* like *daśakas, aṣṭottaraśatas* and *maṅgalāśāsanas* are not taken into consideration. Some of the works are highly scholarly disputations, some are elucidatory of important concepts like *puruṣakāra* and *rahasyas*, while some others are commentarial, expounding basic texts like the *Śrībhāṣya* and *Gītārthasaṅgraha*. As many as 25 works of the Pontiffs have been studied in this chapter. Some of the works are in the form of palm-leaf / paper manuscripts while a majority of them is available in print. The fact that the Pontiffs could find time to compose excellent treatises inspite of their busy schedule of ritual worship of the presiding deity Śrī Mālola Nṛsiṁha, temple renovations, periodical tours and so on, makes the study all the more inspiring and interesting.

[]
***Yajussandhyāvandanabhāṣya*[^171]**

The author, Śrī Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa Śrī Nārāyaṇa Yatīndra Mahādeśika, second Jīyar begins his *Bhāṣya* by paying his obeisance to Lord Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha the presiding deity at Ahobilam and then to his guru and predecessor, Śrī Ādi Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa Svāmī by whose grace, the import of *Vedas* was made as clear as the fruit in one's palm. This echoes the idea expressed in the *Śvetāśvataropaniṣad*[^172] which stresses the importance of *Bhagavad bhakti* and *Ācārya bhakti* in elucidating the inner meaning of the *mantras*.

The author declares at the outset that thousands of commentaries are available for the *Sandhyāvandana mantras* and states that the present work comments on these *mantras* from the Vedāntic point of view.[^173]

The author points out that the word *Devatā*, whenever it occurs in the *mantra* must be taken to refer to Lord Nārāyaṇa only, since the *Pāñcarātra* texts declare thus - "*Paramātmā devatā*", and the *paramātmā* is none other

[^171]: With *Maṇipravāḷa Vyākhyā* by Śrīvaṇśaṭhakopa Śrī Raṅgaśaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika, 42nd Jīyar, pub. by R. Krishnamachariar at Gopalakrishna Press, Madras on 2.4.1950.
[^172]: यस्य देवे परा भक्तिः यथा देवे तथा गुरौ। तस्यैते कथिता ह्यर्थाः प्रकाशन्ते महात्मनः॥ (VI. 23)
[^173]: Vide. p. 2: आपोहिष्ठादिमन्त्राणां व्याख्याः सन्ति सहस्रशः। ग्रन्थतात्पर्यानुसारेण व्याख्यास्यं क्रियते मया॥

[]
than Lord Nārāyaṇa Himself. Since the *upaniṣadic* passages have also been interpreted in the Śrīvaiṣṇava tradition as implying the supremacy and the causal character of Lord Nārāyaṇa, the present body of literature namely the *Sandhyāvandana mantra* should also be interpreted in the same light.

The author profusely quotes from the *Brahma Sūtras, Upaniṣads, Purāṇas* and *Bhagavad Gītā* to elucidate his interpretations. For example, the word *āpas* found in the portion of the *mantra* - *āpo janayathā ca naḥ* (p. 6) is interpreted by our author to mean Lord Viṣṇu who has the waters as His Body. The *nāmarūpavyākaraṇa Śruti* in Chāndogya (section vi) has been interpreted by Śrī Rāmānuja[^174] to mean that all words referring to living and non-living entities must imply only the Supreme Being, since all these form the body of the Lord, and since the Lord exists in all these entities as the inner soul (*antaryāmin*). Even holy rivers like the Ganges are adorable because of their association with the Lord and the very characteristic of sanctity has been imparted to them by the Lord Himself.[^175]

Likewise the word "*sūrya*" in the *mantra* starting, *sūryaśca mā manyuśca* ... is interpretated by Śrī Nārāyaṇa Yatīndra to mean Lord Nārāyaṇa

[^174]: *Śrībhāṣya* - *Jijñāsādhikaraṇa*.
[^175]: p. 8 - सर्वफलप्रदं भगवन्तं विना केवलस्य जलस्य ... इत्यप्रोक्तम्।

[]
only.[^176] This is in accordance with the *Śrībhāṣya* on the *Brahma Sūtra* (I, i, 21): *antastaddharmopadeśāt*.

On the same lines, the author proceeds to explain the term *Varuṇa* to mean Lord Nārāyaṇa (p-42). Finally the *mantra* hails *Varuṇa* and prays that all sins be destroyed:

`सर्वां तां विश्व जिधिवे देव! अथाते स्याम वरुण प्रियासः।`

and this destroyer of sin is none other than Śrīman Nārāyaṇa.

This has been rendered into *Maṇipravāḷa* by the 42nd Jīyar of Ahobila Maṭha. In the introduction, he summarises the necessity of performing *sandhyāvandana* by all people belonging to the three *Varṇas* namely Brāhmins, Kṣatriyas and Vaiśyas, and states that one who does not perform this *nityakarma* is not eligible to perform any *karma* at all. (*anarhaḥ sarvakarmasu*). He also states that he has written in *Maṇipravāḷa* style to enable laymen to understand the real import of the *mantras* which in turn will enable them to perform their daily duties. This *vyākhyā* makes easy reading and is quite useful for laymen of Sanskrit language.

[^176]: `सुष्ठु ईरयति प्रेरयतीति सूर्यः - परमात्मा`

[]
***Nyāsa-viṁśati Vyākhyā*** [^177]

The doctrine of *prapatti* as expounded in the Śrīvaiṣṇava system of philosophy, with its catholicity of approach is recommended to all irrespective of distinctions of caste; and this has taken the doctrine to the lowest of the low, to layman and woman alike. Vedānta Deśika's *Nyāsa-viṁśati* is a metrical composition in 22 verses dealing with this doctrine for which Deśika himself has written a commentary. However the author of this explanatory treatise, Śrī Nārāyaṇa Muni (2nd Jīyar) feels that Deśika's commentary is not simple enough and hence he has penned this work.

Beginning with the term *Sat-sampradāya*[^178] the author offers a couple of interpretations. It means the tradition as established by Yāmuna and other *ācāryas*; the secret teachings of the tradition imparted by *guru* to *śiṣya* (*rahasyajñāta*), it or may refer to noble descent (*satkulaprasūti*). The term *īpset* in the desiderative form suggests that the whole process is something obligatory (*niyogavidhi*).[^179] The characteristics of the *guru* and qualifications of the disciple are enumerated. The teacher imparts learning to the disciple which is in fact *vidyā-janma* and hence the disciple is born again.

[^177]: By Śrī Nārāyaṇa Muni (2nd Jīyar). See *Nyāsa Viṁśati* - A critical study - Dissertation submitted to University of Madras, for M. Phil degree by Mrs. G.Sakuntala (1986).
[^178]: *Nyāsa-viṁśati*, A critical study. p. 77.
[^179]: Ibid. p. 78.

[]
The term *mām* and *ekam* in the *Carama śloka* are important, according to the author. Explaining v.16 of the *Nyāsa Viṁśati*, the author feels that the word *ekam* in particular precludes *prapatti* from the scope of *upāya*; and exhibits the oneness (*aikya*) of *upāya* and *upeya*; it may be interpreted as referring to the Lord as the one who can confer all human ends, that He does not require anything else but *nyāsa* as a pretext (*vyājamātram*) to save the devotees; or it may be taken to mean the Lord as the most important means of *mokṣa*. Nārāyaṇa Muni makes an interesting observation as to whether *ekam* includes Śrī - His Consort or not. The answer is that Lord Viṣṇu in eternal association with Śrī forms a single unitary principle i.e. the supreme God-head. This has been indicated by Vedāntadeśika by the use of the term *Śrīsakha*.[^180] Explaining the *sādhyopāya*, the author states that *prapatti* is *śaraṇāgati* and quotes from the *Śrībhāṣya*[^181] where Rāmānuja uses the term *śaraṇāgati*.

Explaining v.19, the author states that one should give up *vidhi* and *niṣedha* types of acts and should perform only such acts by which one does not incur *anartha*. Now and then one has to do *prāyaścitta*. This itself is explained as *prapatti* by Śrī Deśika. The ultimate advice to *prapannas* is that *bhakti* etc., should be asked for only from the Lord or His associates

[^180]: *Nyāsa-viṁśati*, A critical study, p. 114.
[^181]: *Śrībhāṣya*, II, p. 101. - *Tasya vaśīkaraṇam taccaraṇāravinda śaraṇāgatireva*

[]
(*bhaktyādikam bhagavataḥ tadīyebhyo yācet*).[^182] Acts for peace, health and strength should be done invoking Lord Viṣṇu only, to the exclusion of other gods like Brahmā, Indra (*śāntipauṣṭikādikam ca bhagavantamuddhiśyaiva kuryāt, na brahmārudrāgnyādikam*)

The *ājñā* (compulsory) and *anujñā* (permitted) duties are discussed in the commentary of v. 20. The term *svābhiṣṭaphala* is explained by the author as accruing immediately after *prapatti* or at the fall of the present body or at any time a *prapanna* chooses[^183] (*prapattiyuṭtarākāle dehāvasāne vā yadā prāpriccha tasmin kāle*).

Thus the commentary of Nārāyaṇa Muni explains all the issues connected with *prapatti* as an independent means of *mokṣa*. The commentator has displayed his profound scholarship through various quotations from *Lakṣmī Tantra, Śrībhāṣya, Viṣṇupurāṇa, Viṣṇudharma* and so on. By his lucid exposition he has made it a veritable treat for those interested in this field.

[^182]: *Nyāsa-viṁśati*, A critical study,p. 120.
[^183]: Ibid. p. 126.

[]
***Rahasyatrayajīvātu***[^184]

Śrī Nārāyaṇa Muni pays his obeisance to the Lord and Śrī and says that the meanings he had learnt from his *ācāryas* have been condensed into this work for the easy comprehension of his disciples. From the colophon of the Manuscript we come to know that this work was also called *Rahasyatrayadīpa*. As the name suggests, this work is a veritable life-saving drug for suffering humanity. It is the beacon light that leads them to final beatitude i.e. *sāyujya*.

The author then goes on to speak of the three secrets viz., *Aṣṭākṣara, Dvaya* and *Carama śloka*. He goes into the genesis of the first *mantra*. Its greatness lies in the fact that it was imparted directly by Lord Nārāyaṇa to Nara who was infact, His own aspect, at Badrīkāśrama. The *Aṣṭākṣara* is called the *vyāpaka mantra*, as it is not only found in the *Viṣṇu Gāyatrī* starting with "*Nārāyaṇāya vidmahe*" but also in all the *Vedas*. The author corroborates this with the help of quotations from *Pañcarātra* texts. *Dvaya mantra* which follows, is called *Mantra Ratna*, the very gem among *mantras*. Both these can be called *Rahasyas* since they should not be heard by a third person (*aśatkarṇatayā*). Regarding the *Carama śloka* (*Gītā* xviii. 66) an

[^184]: By Śrī Nārāyaṇa Muni, 2nd Jīyar. Two manuscripts are available (a) GOML - Madras No: 5339, Palmleaf, Telugu characters. (b) Adyar D.X. 421, Palm leaf, Grantha characters. The above study is based on the latter manuscript.

[]
objection can be raised regarding its secret character (*rahasyatva*) since it can be learnt by all the four castes. The author replies that *Carama śloka* is still a *rahasya* is as much as it is in the form of an injunction (*vidhi*) ordained upon a *prapanna*; and it elucidates the import of the first two *mantras*. This point has been discussed at length.

Among these *mantras*, there is a sort of hierarchy. The meaning of the first *mantra* is explained by the second and the full implication of the second *mantra* is conveyed by the third, so that all these three form a composite whole known collectively as *Rahasyatraya*.

The author points out that the *Aṣṭākṣara* when repeated along with the *praṇava*, appropriate *svara* and various auxillaries, is called *vaidika* and without these special accessories it is *tāntrika* which is open to all castes. Several passages are quoted from *Purāṇas* and *Smṛtis* in support of this. The author also takes occassion to explain certain Vedic *mantras* where the word *Maheśvara* is used. The term *Maheśvara* according to the author (folio-4) refers only to the Supreme Brahman, Lord Nārāyaṇa. He goes on to give the grammatical interpretation regarding the syllable '*om*' where *a* stands for Viṣṇu in the Dative sense. The point that Viṣṇu alone is the protector has been proved at length. That the *jīva* is connoted by the syllable *ma*, that he exists only for the sake of the Lord (*Tādarthya*), that for this reason, *jīva* is

[]
known as *śeṣa* has been explained at length by the author in a masterly way. The Lord is the *Śeṣin* in eternal association with Śrī. This point has been corroborated by a number of quotation from *Pāñcarātra* texts and Yāmuna's *Catuślokī*.

The author goes on to explain *śeṣatva* and *dāsatva* as mutually complementary in character (*śeṣatva jñānarhatvam hi dāsatvam*) (Folio 6a). He explains the definitions of the term *śarīra* as given by Rāmānuja in his *Śrībhāṣya*.

The middle syllable in *om* is *u* and is explained as conveying emphasis (*avadhāraṇa*), so that all the three put together explain the irrevokable relationship that all *jīvas* are subservient to the Lord in association with Śrī. He explains the character of *jīva* as conveyed by *ma* from various viewpoints based on different verbal roots- "*mana jñāne, man avabodhane, māñ māne, masi parimāṇe*", so that a full picture of the *jīva* would emerge as knower, as atomic in character and as distinct from the body, senses and so on.

The *śeṣatvajñāna* is more important than the knowledge that *ātmā* and *śarīra* are different. He is *jīva* only because he is essentially a *śeṣa* to the Lord. He quotes from the *Viṣṇu purāṇa* to prove this point. The Lord is the inner controller (*yamasyāpi yamaḥ*) and he enters the *jīvātmā* (*anupraveśa*) and rules from within (*sarvaniyantā, antaḥpraviṣṭaśśāstā janānām*) and hence

[]
, he is *sarvātmā*. The relevant verse from the *Prapanna Pārijāta* (Folio 9) is quoted to elucidate this point. This knowledge of one's *śeṣatva* itself is a *yāga*. He quotes from Vedāntadeśika to explain that *pratyagātmā* is the oblation, *ātmasamarpaṇa* is the sacrifice and the *praṇava* is the *karaṇamantra*, and the fruit is *mokṣa* (Folio 9a).

The author goes on to explain the meaning of the *praṇavavākya*. It makes one bow down in all humility (*prakarṣena nāmayati*). He quotes *Atharvaśiras* as authority and states that the *jīva* is possessor of vital breath (*prāṇān prāṇinaḥ*) and the Lord is the inner controller (*śeṣatvena niyacchati*). The word *a* is *Viṣṇuvācaka* because it is *cit svarūpa*; and *ukāra* is Śrī and *makāra* is the *jīva* who is the servant of both Lord and Śrī. He thus establishes the *śeṣatva* and *pāratantrya* of the *jīva* in the *praṇava mantra*.

Next, the author goes on to elucidate the *namaḥ śabda*. Only the Lord is *śeṣabhūta* and the *jīvas* add excellence to the Lord through subordination to Him. (*atiśayādhāyako hi śeṣa iti vyapadiśyate*) (Folio 10). He says that by the term *namaḥ, ahaṅkāra* and *mamakāra* are rooted out totally. He defines *ahaṅkāra* as (*ahameva mama nirvāhakaḥ*) pride in feeling that "I can take care of myself". *Mamakāra* is defined as (*idam mameti*) "feeling of being the possessor of objects that do not really belong to one" (Folio 10 a).

[]
A valid point is then taken up for discussion - whether there is any *kartṛtva* for a *jīva* and whether *jīva* has any independence during *prathamapravṛtti*. According to Svāmī Deśika, the question of *prathamapravṛtti* does not arise because *jīvas* are beginningless and *karma* is also beginningless. The author states that to a person who is favourably disposed towards God, (*atimātra bhagavadānukūlya vyasthita*) (Folio 11a) a desire to seek salvation is generated by the Lord Himself (*rucim janayati*); and in the case of the person who is not favourably disposed towards Him, God allows him to proceed in those lines that do not lead him to God. He quotes from the *Bhagavad Gītā* to substantiate his point. He acknowledges that Rāmānuja has explained this point in the *Śrībhāṣya* (*parāyattādhikaraṇam*).

Hence by the *praṇava* both *śeṣatva* and *pāratantrya* are fully established. He then goes on to explain the difference between the two: *yatheṣṭa viniyogārhatvam* is *śeṣatvam* i.e., fitness to be utilised as one desires and *yatheṣṭa viniyujyamānatvam* is *pāratantryam* i.e. capacity to be utilised as one desires.

The *jīva* has the capacity to do things by himself to a certain extent, like worshipping the Lord etc., *jīvasya kartṛtvam vyāpārāśrayamātram*. Sometimes *acetana* can be the cause of activity, like mud being used for producing pots. But this is meant as an *upacāra* only. So, the Lord accords His permission by inducing action and remains a silent witness (*sākṣī*) because

[]
the *jīva* is only experiencing the fruits of his own *karma*. The Lord becomes the *sahakārikāraṇa* (co-operative cause) because He is the indweller in all and He is the granter of fruits as explained in *Śrībhāṣya* (*phalmata upapatteḥ*) (Folio 12). He stresses the importance of devotion to God and quotes *Śruti* texts in his favour and says that all acts are in vain without devotion to the Lord. He speaks very highly of *Viṣṇubhaktas*. He quotes *Viṣṇupurāṇa* to substantiate the innate greatness of *Bhāgavatas*.

He raises a question in (Folio 14 a) as to whether servitude to *Bhāgavatas* does not mean disrespect (*droha*) to the Lord. He denies this and states that it is only through God's *saṅkalpa* that one becomes a *dāsa* of a *dāsa*. In fact *Bhāgavata śeṣatva* is more pleassing than *Bhagavat śeṣatva* and this is obtained only through God's Grace. Only *aniṣṭa* (dislike) has to avoided. So, there is mutual interdependence between devotees. There is no mutual contradiction if one is a master and the other is a servant and yet both are servants of God. The author then speaks of how the Ācārya imparts *sadupadeśa* according to *śiṣya's* wish and eligibility (*yathāhṛdayam yathārham ca*) (Folio 15 a). He quotes the first verse of the *Rahasyatraya-sāra-śiṣyakṛtyādhikaraṇa* to substantiate his point. The *anyonyapārārthyam* is the *śeṣaśeṣibhāva* between an *ācārya* and his disciple; but as far as the Lord is concerned, both are equal (*sāmya*) in their being the servants of the Lord.

[]
Here, *Bhāgavata* means a *paramaikāntin*. He quotes the relevant *Viṣṇupurāṇa* verse:

`एकान्तिनः सदा ब्रह्मध्यायिनो योगिनो हि ये।`
`तेषां तत्परमं स्थानं यद्वै पश्यन्ति सूरयः॥`

These *Bhāgavatas* are devoted to Viṣṇu to the exclusion of other gods. He goes on to quote extensively from the *Vāmanapurāṇa* to elucidate the fact that *Viṣṇubhaktas* are superior to other devotees because of Lord Viṣṇu's Supremacy and this *Bhāgavata* enjoys being the servant of the Lord. The *Bhaviṣyat Purāṇa* is quoted, where Rudra himself speaks of the impermanent fruits for the followers of *Pāśupataśāstra* and he goes on to condemn non-Vedic religions and describes the fate of those who follow these religions. Hence, the author concludes that Lord Viṣṇu alone is the one to be resorted to by performing *śaraṇāgati*.

Next, the term *namaḥ* of the *Aṣṭākṣara* is taken up for discussion. *Namaḥ* according to the author is *śaraṇāgati vācaka śabda* and he corroborate this from the *Ahirbudhnya saṁhitā* (52-31 & 32)

`पञ्चा न्कार उद्दिष्टो मः प्रधान उदीर्यते।`
`विसर्गः परमेशस्तु त्रयार्थोऽयं निरूप्यते॥`
`...`
`तत्प्राप्तये प्रधानीऽयं पञ्चा न्मन - नापवान्॥`

Here *na* denotes *upāya* the path, *ma* denotes its importance and the *visarga* denotes the Lord and hence the term *namaḥ* means only *śaraṇāgati*.

[]
Three types of interpretation are possible here. In the subtle (*sūkṣma*) sense, this denotes *bhagavatpāratantrya*; in the gross (*sthūla*) sense, it means *śaraṇāgati* or *prapatti*; and in the ultimate (*para*) sense, it refers to the *siddhopāya* i.e. *puruṣottama*.

The third word of the *Aṣṭākṣara*, namely *Nārāyaṇa*, is then taken up for study. The *akāra* and *makāra* in the *Praṇava* are explained by this term *Nārāyaṇa* i.e. the all -controlling power of the Lord denoted by *akāra* and the eternality of the *jīvas* by the *makāra*. The *caturthī vibhakti* denotes the fruit of *śaraṇāgati*. The two different compounds, *Tatpuruṣa* and *Bahuvrīhi* are exhaustively detailed out. He speaks of the distinctions between *cit, acit* and *Īśvara*; and the distinction among *jīvas* themselves. *Jīva* is called *nara* because he does not undergo modification like *acit*. Lord is the *ayana* or abode and He is the *upāya* and leads them to Himself. The author declares that *ayanaśabdasya ādhārārthatve sakalacetana - acetana ādhāratvam bhagvataḥ siddhyati* (Folio 18 a). He defends the viewpoint that there is no mutual contradiction involved in the Lord being both *upāya* and *upeya*. He states that the natural compassion (*svābhāvika dayā*) and Grace (*prasāda*) of the Lord are the two qualities that make Him the *upāya*; and because the Lord is the cause of the Universe, He is the *upeya* (Folio 18 a) as well (*sarvakāra-ṇatva viśiṣṭatayā sarvadā anubhāvyatva viśeṣeṇa prāpyatvam*). The author

[]
draws a distinction between *bhakti* and *prapatti* and states that *prapatti* will result ultimately in *bhakti* to the Lord.

He goes on to refute the view of *Mīmāṁsakas* that Vāyu and other gods grant fruits and declares that it is the Lord as *antaryāmin* in all these gods who ultimately bestows the fruits by corroborating from the *Śrībhāṣya*. So, all *Vedāntavākyas* declare the Lord to be the possessor of all good qualities by His own nature, prescribe the code of propitiating Him through *yāga, dāna, homa, stuti, namaskāra* and so on, and promise the fruit of this worship namely *bhoga* and *mokṣa*. For the Lord this *śaraṇāgati* is a mere pretext (*vyājamātra*) for final liberation. He is indeed the *kāraṇa* for all *cetanas*.

Quoting profusely from *Śruti* texts, the author declares that there was only Nārāyaṇa in the beginning and that Śiva and Brahmā are lesser in status to Nārāyaṇa. The Lord's *janma* and *karma* are both divine and He incarnates only for the protection of the virtuous. In the beginning of every *yuga*, Brahmā, Indra and other gods propitiate Viṣṇu in order to obtain and retain their positions. Thus the *jagatkāraṇatva*, the *mokṣa pradānatva* and the *jagad ādhāratva* of the Lord are established in no uncertain terms.

By the *Bahuvrīhi* interpretation of the term *nārāyaṇa* the *antaryāmitva* and by the *Tatpuruṣa* interpretation the *bahirvyāptitva* of the Lord are then

[]
proved. The innumerable auspicious perfections of the Lord are extolled citing Parāśara Bhaṭṭa and Rāmānuja. The author quotes from *Viṣṇupurāṇa* and *Viṣṇusūkta* in *Ṛg Veda* and drives home the point that even in His incaranations, the Lord's body is *aprākṛta* and is not the result of any *karma* at all (*na karma-nimittajātam*).

The author then speaks of the Lord's *nityayogatva* with Śrī and His permanent abode *Vaikuṇṭha*:

`वैकुण्ठे तु परे लोके श्रिया सार्धं जगत्पतिः।`
`आस्ते विष्णुरचिन्त्यात्मा भक्तैर्भागवतैः सह॥`

He cites the *Vaikhānasa Āgama* to state the pluarity of *viṣṇulokas-āmoda, pramoda sammoda* and *vaikuṇṭha*. The *Mokṣadharma* describes the location of *vaikuṇṭha* above all the other worlds. The Lord is untouched by the *rajas* and *tamo guṇa* of *prakṛti* and yet His external pervasion is such that there is no place untouched by Him (*aspaṣṭapradeśavaidhurya*). He is *avāptasamastakāmaḥ* and is always happy; the sportive creation of the world is by His own *saṅkalpa* and He is the granter of *mokṣa*.

The author then expatiates on the *caturthī vibhakti* of the term *Nārāyaṇāya* and says that it refers to the fruit of *kaiṅkarya*. Each *jīva* has a different *puruṣārtha* according to his body; for the cattle it is grass, for man it is rice, for gods it is *amṛta* and so on. This gradation in life is seen in hell also. The author declares that the fruit of the *karaṇakalebarayoga* is only

[]
*Bhagavatsevā*. He discusses about the difference between *kaiṅkarya* and *anubhava* in the state of liberation. In this process, the author speaks of *viṣṇuloka* and draw a distinction between *viṣṇuloka* and *paramapada* and says that the former is located in *prakṛtimaṇḍala*. It seems to be a lower kind of heaven, because he mentions that people return to earth after sometime (*kālaviśeṣa*) but once a *jīva* reaches *paramapada* there is no coming back to earth certainly. This can be reached through *bhakti* and *prapatti* and in the *paramapada* there is *paripūrṇa bhagavadanubhavaprāpti*. The *muktas* are always possessed with *kaiṅkarya śakti*. The author then states that *sāyujya* is the final beatitude - *sāyujyameva sākṣānmokṣaḥ*. Etymologically, *sāyujya* means *sayujoḥ bhāvaḥ* and hence there is extreme similarity in enjoyment (*bhogasāmyam*). There is *paramasāmyam* only and not *aikyam* and hence there is *bheda*.[^185]

Śrī Nārāyaṇa Muni then goes on to explain *kaivalya* which is different from *mokṣa* because in the former there is no *bhagavadanubhava*. Only *bhagavatkaiṅkarya* is *mokṣa*. He quotes Yāmuna's *Gītārthasaṅgraha* to show that *kaivalya* is *mokṣa* and *kevalas* can reach God through *arcirādi mārga*.

[^185]: Cf. *Śrībhāṣya*, "*bhogamātrasāmyaliṅgācca*" (IV. iv. 21).

[]
Finally the author explains the suffix *āya* and states that it implies eternal servitude to the Lord. Hence in the *Aṣṭākṣara* '*om*' refers to *svarūpa*, '*namaḥ*' refers to *upāya* and *Nārāyaṇa* is the *puruṣārtha*.

In the second section the author takes up the *Dvayamantra* for discussion. He says that it is called *Dvaya* because it has two parts - *khaṇḍadvaya*. The author states that because it is a *mantra* that connotes *śaraṇāgati*, it has to be received from one's *ācārya* who acts as the mediator for the soul desirous of liberation. Hence it is all the more necessary to have an *ācārya* and follow the *satsampradāya* as laid down by the *ācāryas*. He goes on to explain the *ācāryalakṣaṇa* as detailed out in the first verse of Svāmī Deśika's *Nyāsaviṁśati*[^186] word by word. It is interesting to note that this *vyākhyā* is similar to the *Nyāsaviṁśati-vyākhyā* by the same author. All the points are incorporated here. He dwells at length on the miseries of worldly existence to highlight the necessity of liberation. For this, one should resort to a good *ācārya* with whose grace, one can perform *śaraṇāgati*.

After this lengthy prelude, the author goes on to explain the meaning of this *mantraratna*, the very germ among *mantras* - its essential nature (*svarūpa*) and its meaning (*arthasvarūpa*). He quotes the *Śvetasvara upaniṣad* - "*mumukṣur vai śaraṇamaham prapadye*" and from the *Padmapurāṇa* to

[^186]: `तत्त्वप्राप्ती प्रभवति तथा देशिको मे दययालुः॥`

[]
stress the greatness of this *mantra*. Here *Śrī* denotes *Lakṣmī* just as *akāra* denotes Lord Viṣṇu in a special way. *Śrī-sevāyām* is the verbal root which denotes the subject and object etymologically i.e. She does service to the Lord and She is served by all the *cetanas* (Folio 40). The root *Śru-śravaṇe* indicates that *Śṛṇoti* and *śrāvayati* are both possible in Her case. She listens to the prayers of the devotees and then pleads to the Lord on their behalf. *Śrū-hiṁsāyām* and *Śrū-vistāre* are the roots which means that She removes the sins of the devotees and develops in them the desire for doing service to the Lord. Through this, *Śrī's puruṣakāratva* is also established. He quotes from the *Pāñcarātra Āgama* to substantiate this. But an objection may be raised here that the Lord is naturally the protector of all, and so He does not stand in need of a mediator to perform this duty-

`स्वाभाविकसर्वज्ञत्वेन परमकारुणिकस्य भगवतः कथमिव`
`पुरुषकारसापेक्षम्` (Folio 40 a)

He replies that this necessity of a *puruṣakāra* is only through *Bhagavatsaṅkalpa*. The *Daṇḍadharatva* of the Lord, and the *Puruṣakāratva* of Śrī complement each other says the author and quotes from Parāśara's *Śrīguṇaratnakośa "*yuvarājau*" (v.34) to substantiate his point. He answers another objection as to how the term *puruṣakāra* can be used in relation to a *cetana* like Śrī and concludes that Lakṣmī is the *śakti* of the Lord and is also His consort and hence She has equal powers in creation and other activities: *sṛṣṭyādi vyāpāreṣu samānalīlayā* (Folio 41). She induces the Lord to act by

[]
Her powers and hence is *sahakāriṇī*. He quotes from *Lakṣmī Tantra* to enumerate the three qualities that go to make up *śakti - icchā, saṁvit* and *ahantā*.

Compared to the other consorts of the Lord, Bhū and Nīḷa, Śrī occupies a pre-eminent place according to the author - *ataḥ bhagavataḥ upāyatve bhūminīḷācāryebhyo api utkṛṣṭapuruṣakārabhūtā śrīreva bhavati* (Folio 41 a). Since Śrī is the *viśeṣaṇa* of the Lord, Her *patnīguṇa* acts as *viśeṣaṇa* to the Lord and there is no contradiction because there is unity in the goal and the way (*upāya upeya aikyam*). If we accept duality in *upāya* then we have to accept duality in *guṇa* and *vigraha* and there will be *vaiṣamya*. The term *māmekam* in the *carama śloka* refers to *Śrīmat śabda* only which in turn means "*lakṣmyā saha hṛṣīkeśaḥ*". The Lord is *cetanācetanātmaka kṛtsnaprapañcaviśiṣṭa* and is ever in association with Śrī. According to our Ācārya the *svara* clinches the issue.

The Lord needs Śrī as His *sahadharmacāriṇī* who is always favourable to the Lord's actions (*svakāryānukūlā*) and this does not detract the Lord's all-powerful nature. Hence the Lord Śrīman Nārāyaṇa alone is the protector of all and He alone is to be resorted to by all. *Aniṣṭanivāraṇa* is the special quality of Śrī as *vātsalya* and *vāllabhya* are quite natural to Her. She tempers Lord's justice by her unique quality of *dayā*. When the ever-just Lord desires

[]
to punish the erring souls (*kṣipāmyajasram and na kṣamāmī*). Śrī enters the Lord's heart and kindles the quality of *karuṇā* in Him and thus revives the *jīvas* and makes them survive: *kṛpāviṣayatvamujjīvanam ca* (Folio 43 a).

Hence the author states that it is absolutely essential that Śrī should be present when *śaraṇāgati* is performed to the Lord. (*Bhagavataḥ samāśrayane śriyassannidhānam avaśyāpekṣitam iti siddham*). Certainly, Śrī neither deprives nor infringes upon the Lord's independence. *Śriyaḥpatitva* is the special quality of the Lord and hence the Lord does not have any *vastutva* without Her (*anayā vinā na vastu siddhiḥ*). The Lord's independence is not impaired. He quotes the relevant verse from *Śrīguṇaratnakośa, "svayā dīptyā ratnam bhavadapi mahārgham"*. In reality independence implies only mutual dependence.

The author then goes on to explain the term *nara*. It means *nara sambandhi* and *nara rakṣaṇa upayogiguṇajātam* i.e. *samāśrita* and *saṁrakṣaṇaguṇas* such as *kārunya, svāmitva, sauśīlya, vātsalya, saulabhya, jñāna, śakti* and so on, and explains each quality in detail .

All these qualities instil a sense of great confidence in the devotees who resort to His feet. The author now takes up the term *Nārāyaṇa* of the *Dvayamantra* for discussion. Here the term is capable of bringing to light all the qualities mentioned above, and the Lord alone is the repository of all these

[]
qualities. The term *caraṇau* indicates that as far as the devotees are concerned it is absolutely essential to resort to the Holy Feet of the Lord for protection and liberation and the Holy Feet themselves are capable of granting the desired result as they are an integral part of the Lord.

A question is raised as to why the Lord's *caraṇa* is *upāya*. The feet of the Lord should be resorted by the servant (*jīva*) and hence it is appropriate says the author. He opines that the *arcāvatāra* is ideally suited for *dvayānusandhāna* and this *caraṇagrahaṇa* cannot be overlooked (*anatikramaṇīyam*). If we take the term *śaraṇam* to mean house or protection then, too *caraṇau* becomes an *upāya*. So, the term *śrīmat* means, the goal to be achieved and the way to achieve it also. So, there is *prāpyaprāpaka aikyam*, according to *ācāryas*.

Then the verb *prapadye* is taken up for elucidation by the author. It is taken first in the sense of *gati* i.e 'to reach', through *manas, vāk* and *kāya*. Each act has its own result, but when the three are combined together in one single act, then the effect becomes very significant too.
