But, through the rule of "*jñānān mokṣa*", *manas* is of greater importance than *vāk* or *kāya*. *Prapatti* is possible only when we realise our total helplessness and know that the Lord alone is the *upāya* and *upeya*.

[]
Secondly the term *prapadye* means "moving towards God". But by the rule – *gatyarthā dhātavaḥ buddhyarthāḥ*, physical movement means mental approach towards God. A question is raised as to whether *prapatti* and *bharanyāsa* are different. The author states that the mental approach leads to *mahāviśvāsa* and hence it includes *bharanyāsa* also (Folio 48 a) - *bhara-nyāsātmakam prapadanameva anuṣṭheyamiti nirṇītam*.[^187] But this *prapatti* should be requested; for, without prayerful attitude (*prārthanāmatik*), *prapatti* is meaningless. He quotes from the *Ahirbudhnya saṁhitā*[^188] starting with *ānukūlyasya saṅkalpaḥ*... and discusses about the *ṣaḍvidha prapatti* where five are *aṅgas* and *ātmanikṣepa* is *aṅgin* similar to *aṣṭāṅgayoga* and says that *nikṣepa, nyāsa, saṁnyāsa, tyāga* and *śaraṇāgati* are all synonymous. It does not stand in need of any other accessories, except of course the *prārthanā*.

The author then discusses the use of the present tense in the verb *prapadye*. He opines that because of this usage doubts may arise about the permanent nature of the result of *prapatti* because it is done only once as contrasted with *bhakti yoga* which one can perform till death, any number of times. He refers to *Brahma sūtra* 4.1.1: *Āvṛttirasakṛdupadeśāt*. But, he concludes that since *Śruti* and *Smṛti* refer to "*sakṛdeva*" etc., *prapatti* should

[^187]: *Rahasyatrayasāram*, p. 600.
[^188]: 2 37 - 28 & 29.

[]
be done only once and defines *prapatti* as *bhagavatpravṛtti-virodhi svapravṛtti nivṛttiḥ*.

The second sentence explains that *sādhana* is twofold: *siddha* and *sādhya* and the *phala* is twofold: *bhagvat prāpati* and *kaiṅkarya prāpti*. Only the highest *puruṣārtha* should be aspired for namely *paramapada*. Ācāryas are of the opinion that the Lord grants this *paramapada* out of His own will – *sarveśvaraḥ svayameva paramampadam prayacchati* (Folio 52).

Explaining the term *Śrīmat* in the first sentence of the *Dvaya mantra*, the author states that the Lord who is ever-just (*daṇḍadhara*) and wants to punish the erring soul, is tempered by Śrī who revives the soul and pleads for its redemption. So, the *nityayogitva* of Śrī is implied. The term *namaḥ* represents a prayerful attitude (*baddhāñjalipuṭaḥ, hṛṣṭaḥ*). The agency and the claim for the fruits of action should be given up totally. The only aim of *kaiṅkarya* should be *bhagavanmukhollāsa*.

The third section is devoted to the discussion of the *Caramaśloka*. This brings out in full the meaning of the *Dvayamantra*. It is called *carama* because it speaks of the fourth or last *upāya*, the other three being *karma, jñāna* and *bhakti yogas*.

The first term of the *carma śloka* is *sarvadharmān*. By the term *dharma* is implied the means for *bhoga* and *mokṣa* in conformity with the

[]
*śāstras*. The plural usage is indicative of the plurality of the means viz *karma, jñāna* and *bhakti*. He quotes from the *Bhagavad Gītā* to prove the efficacy of performing *karma yoga*. By *karma* is meant *nitya* and *naimittika karmas* i.e. daily and enjoined duties. In *jñāna yoga* too there is plurality viz., *sad, dahara, śāṇḍilya, madhu, upakośala, paryaṅka*, and so on. As far as *bhakti yoga* is concerned, *dhyāna, arcana, praṇāma* etc., are the various methods of propitiating the Lord.

The author enumerates the different ways in which the Lord can be served – by washing the temples (whereby the Lord washes away the devotees' sins); by lighting lamps of oil or ghee for the Lord, the devotee is taken through the path of light in a well-lit *vimāna*; by propitating the idol of Lord Nṛsiṁha, duly installed, a devotee attains *mokṣa*; by repeating the Holy names of the Lord, the devotee attains *paramapada* (*yāti brahma sanātanam*) and so on.

The author then speaks of the glory that a devotee gets by propitiating the Lord with *ūrdhvapuṇḍra* by quoting from *Smṛti* texts. All *karmas* are not meant to be given up because we have the scripture *yajñena dānena tapasā anāśakena brahmaṇo vividiṣanti*. *Smṛtis* too declare that *karmas* (duties) are a means for liberation. By the term *śaraṇam vraja, śaraṇāgati* is implied. Different castes have different duties and the duties enjoined upon one according to one's *varṇa* and *āśrama* should not be given up at any point of

[]
time by one desirous of liberation. Hence the author states: *sarva dharma tyāgapūrvakaśaraṇa-varaṇakaraṇam ramaṇīyam*.

*Prapatti* is independent (*nirapekṣā*) and the *viśiṣṭa vidhi* viz. *śaraṇam vraja* does not depend on any other *upāya* for its completion. It cannot brook the idea of introducing any other *upāya* like, the *Brahmāstra*. So in the first *pāda*, the author states the essential nature of that which should be given up; in the second *pāda*, he speaks of the *tyāgaprakāra*-the way of giving up and in the third *pāda, 'mām'* he speaks of the *upāya* that should be chosen; and here all the qualities of *vātsalya* etc. which go to make up a *śaraṇya* should qualify the term '*mām*'. By the term *ekam*, Lord Hari who is the *ādipuruṣa* is meant and this should be used in the sense of *eva* only i.e. stressing the independent nature of the *upāya*; and *prapatti* itself is only a mere pretext (*vyājamātra*) and is not dependent on *bhakti yoga*. *Ekam* is used in the sense of *vilakṣaṇa* or uniqueness. The term *śaraṇam vraja* implies *manasā cintaya* according to the rule - *garyarthāḥ dhātavaḥ buddhyarthāḥ*. Realising that the Lord is the *antaryāmin* of all living things, one should be in consonance with them.

The author points out that *antimasmaraṇa* is not a necessity for a *prapanna*. The author quotes in support, the *Varāhacaramaśloka* viz.,

`स्थिते मनसि सुस्वस्थे शरीरे सति यो नरः।`
`धातु साम्ये स्थिते स्मर्ता विश्वरूपं च मामजम्॥`
`ततस्तं म्रियमाणं तु काष्ठपाषाणसन्निभम्।`
`अहं स्मरामि मद्भक्तं नयामि परमां गतिम्॥`

[]
The author explains each word of the *śloka* in minute detail. He now goes back to the term *māmekam* in *caramaśloka* and states that the Lord has all the six qualities: *jñāna, bala, śakti, tejas, vīrya* and *aiśvarya* in full, and hence is capable of granting the fruit of liberation. For a *prapanna* all *prārabdha karmas* are wiped out. Then takes place a discussion on the subdivision of the *pāpas*. It is not a hard and fast rule that all *prārabdha karmas* are exhausted by one's birth and death and hence the necessity of *prapatti*. Future sins done involuntarily will be removed by *yajña, dāna, tapas* and *anāśaka* (fasting). The involuntary sins of a *prapanna* are destroyed by the Lord by giving him some *alpadanḍas*.

Once the *śeṣatva jñāna* has dawned, now it is the Lord's responsibility to take care of the *prapanna*. *Bhagavat prāpti* is the only desire and just as a gem shines forth in all its brilliance after it is well-cleaned, so too, the *pratibandhas* having been removed, the *prapanna jīva* shines forth in full effulgence ready and fit to receive God's Grace by attaining *Sāyujya*. For such a *prapanna* there is no return to *saṁsāradaśā* as the last *Brahma sūtra* states - *anāvṛttiśśabdādanāvṛttiśśabdāt* (IV,iv,22).

A study of this text indicates the author's profound scholarship, his clear understanding of the three secrets imparted by his *ācāryas* and his ability to quote at will from *Śruti* and *Smṛti* texts. He refers to the *Prapanna Pārijāta*

[]
of Naḍādūr. Ammāḷ and quotes from *Tattvasāra, Rahasya Trayasāra, Gadyas, Stotraratna, Pāñcarātra* texts like *Ahirbudnya saṁhitā* and *Lakṣmī Tantra*. His language is simple and there is clarity of thought and expression.

***Rahasyatrayārthavicāra***[^188]

This work is a metrical composition in 22 verses that explains the three *rahasyas* viz. the *aṣṭākṣara*, the *dvaya mantra* and the *carama śloka*, very briefly. The first seven verses deal with the first secret. The teacher imparts these secrets to the disciple who is desirous of liberation. The Lord is the *jagatkāraṇa* and He is the protector. Lord Hari is of the nature of *jñāna* and *ānanda* and He has them as His qualities also. Explaining the word *Nārāyaṇa* the author states that He is the abode of all beings of the universe and He resides in all of them as their inner self (*antaryāmin*). The *jīvas* are eternally subservient to Him. The relationship between the *jīva* and the Lord, the way to reach Him and the prayer for this is the meaning of the first secret.

`जीवेशयोश्च सम्बन्धः सम्बन्धानुगुणाक्रिया।`
`तत्फलप्राप्तयेऽर्थना चेति मन्त्रार्थमनुसन्दधे॥`

The author then goes on to explain the *Dvayamantra* in the next seven verses. Here, the Lord's eternal association with Śrī who is the abode of all good qualities like *sauśīlya, saulabhya, vātsalya*, and *sārvajñatā* and Her

[^188]: By Śrī Nārāyaṇa Muni. Palm leaf Manuscript deposited with GOML, Madras, folio 185 of R 3671 (f).

[]
*puruṣakāra* (mediation) are mentioned. Śrī purifies all the *jīvas* and leads them to the Lord. The author prays to the Lord to obliterate all his bad deeds as he has performed *bharanyāsa* (surrender) with *mahāviśvāsa* by the grace of his *ācārya* and hence does not stand in need of *antimaśmṛti*.

The last seven verses deal with the *carama śloka*.The author, incapable of performing *jñāna, bhakti* and *karma yogas* has resorted to the feet of the Lord which is only a mere pretext for the Lord to extend His Grace. He alone is the bestroyer of all fruits. He is the way and He is the goal to be achieved. With this, the author rests assured and is free from worries.

This small metrical piece is written on the lines of Vedāntadeśika's *Nyāsadaśaka*. The author's ability to condense into simple verse form the quintessence of the *Rahasyatraya* is evident.

***Vāsantikāpariṇayam***[^189]

In literature, drama is said to be the most beautiful medium of expression -

`काव्येषु नाटकं रम्यम्।`

[^189]: by Śrī Śaṭhakopa Yati, 7th Jīyar of Śrī Ahobila Maṭha, Ed. by Narasirhhasastri; published in Vidyatarangini press, Mysore, 1912, (Telugu). The editor of this book has mistakenly mentioned the author as the 1st Jīyar in the title page.

[]
True to this statement, the author of the above work, Śrī Śaṭhakopa Svāmī, the 7th Pontiff of Ahobila Maṭha (Vaṁśaṭhārī III - 1513-1522) has presented in lucid style, the wedding of the Divine couple viz. Lord Nṛsiṁha and Ceñcu Lakṣmī called Vāsantikā, the daughter of a local hunter chieftain Śūrasena. The setting is at Ahobilapura and Prahalāda is also one of the characters in this five-act drama. It begins like all other Sanskrit dramas, with an invocatory verse called Nāndī –

`पारावारसुताप्रमोदघटटंकीकृतो समालम्बते`
`स श्रेयांसि चतुर्भुजो रचयताल्लक्ष्मीनृकण्ठीरवः`। etc.
`अकुण्ठोद्भवादिभाविभ्या यस्य हेषया।`
`अस्तु मे वस्तु मेधायै कन्धरौपरि सैन्धवम्॥`

Then the Sūtradhāra and Māriṣa enter the stage and through their dialogue we come to know that the vernal festival (*Vasantotsava*) of Lord Narasiṁha was being celebrated and this drama was to be staged on that occasion.

***Act I***

The verses 1-18 are introductory in character. Lord Nṛsiṁha was spending his time dressed like a hunter along with Gālava (a *vidūṣaka*) in a forest near Garuḍācala, Ahobila. Indra and Mātali pay their respects to Him. According to Indra's statement to Mātali, Lakṣmī cursed a *gandharva* princess to be born in a hunter's tribe. The story goes that Lakṣmī pleased by the princess' music offered her a boon by which the *gandharva* princess wanted

[]
Ahobileśvara Himself as her husband. This enraged Lakṣmī and she cursed the princess thus:

`मुग्धमदीयदयितं दयितं तवापि सम्पृच्छ्य साहसवती यदवक्ष्यं माम्।`
`आसाद्यवञ्चककिरातकुलेऽवतारं काङ्क्षां भज त्वमिति तां कमला शशाप॥`[^190]

The *Kirāta* girl Vāsantikā (daughter of Śūrasena) came to the same forest along with her friend to worship the Vanadevatā. As the Lord saw her, He fell in love with her. On seeing Him, Vāsantikā's friends leave the place. The Lord and Vāsantikā also leave for Garuḍācala.

***Act II***

The scene is located at Śūrasena's harem. Kādambaka, a chamberlain, was asked by the *Kirāta* chief to verify the veracity of the statement that his daughter was blessed by the forest deity to have a suitable husband in the immediate future.

Madhurikā, attendant of Vāsantikā confirms the news and informs the chamberlain that ever since Vāsantikā saw the Lord of Ahobila she was in deep love with Him. Vāsantikā tells her friends—

`सकलहृदयान्तार्यामी स्वामी मम भावमवगत्य स्वरूपं दर्शितवा-नासीत्।`(p.18)

[^190]: I l, 19.

[]
A sooth-sayer Vijñānavatī was also sent for, to predict if the Lord of Ahobila would marry Vāsantikā. The sooth-sayer confirmed it and said that even the Lord was love-sick ever since He saw her in the forest.

***Act III***

Māyāmaya and Śaṅkarī enter the stage and talk about the Lord's love-sickness. Māyāmaya was sent by the Lord Himself on the mission of bringing Vāsantikā out of her harem under some pretext, to the garden.

The Lord and Gālava (*vidūṣaka*) roam about in the garden situated between the slopes of the Vedagiri and Garuḍācala, and on the bank of the river Bhavanāśinī. Gālava fails in his effort to divert the mind of the Lord.

Through the Lord's own Yogamāyā, they both enter the garden in the outskirts of the hunter's village, towards the north of Garuḍācala. Māyāmaya sent earlier by the Lord becomes a beautiful parrot and entices Vāsantikā into the garden. The Lord and Vāsantikā meet each other, and the parrot vanishes. As Vāsantikā's mother arrives there, the Lord and Vāsantikā had to part hurriedly.

[]
***Act IV***

Two bees enter the stage and reveal that Gandharvarāja and his wife came to the earth and tried to pacify Lakṣmī who had earlier cursed their daughter to be born as Vāsantikā.

The Lord and Vanadevatā enter the stage and she tried to divert the mind of the love-sick Lord. Gālava brings information that Vāsantikā's marrriage is near at hand. Vanadevatā goes to Garuḍācala to make arrangements for the wedding. Gālava informs the Lord that all the efforts of Vāsantikā's friends to relieve her of the love-fever proved futile. He also informed the Lord that he met Lakṣmī on his way who enquired about the love-affair of the Lord and the hunter girl.

Both the Lord and Gālava then reach the garden of Vanadevatā, by Yogamāyā. Vāsantikā who came there to worship Manmatha, met the Lord there. They exchange compliments but had to part hurriedly because the girl's parents had finished the vernal festival and were leaving for their home-town. Vidūṣaka and the Lord also exit, hoping for an early marrige.

***Act V***

Prahlāda enters the stage. He had spent sleepless nights worried by the Lord's love-sickness. Nārada enters the stage and informs that Lakṣmī Herself had agreed to the marriage of the Lord and Vāsantikā.

[]
The *Vidūṣaka* says that the *Smṛti* texts point out that some *pativratā* ladies are also known to marry their husbands to girls of their husbands' choice, for the continuity of their *māṅgalya*.

`अस्ति सत्येवं सुभगेलीवत्कल्पः -`
`माङ्गल्यसूत्रस्त्वास्त्वं काङ्क्षमाणाः पतिव्रताः।`
`काम्यभूमिगता भर्त्रा द्रष्टुमिति स्मृतिः॥`(V. 10)

All the gods arrive on the scene. Brahmā becomes the priest and the marriage of the Lord and Vāsantikā takes place with great pomp and eclat.

The author's style is very simple and lucid. There is alliteration too, in the description of Vāsantikā by Lord Narasimha.

`गुस्तारकुचकुम्भी कोरके कोरकेऽस्याः`
`पद्मक्वनित्राणां पल्लवे पल्लवे च।`
`प्रभुतमिथुनानां पञ्चमे पञ्चमेऽहं`
`वचनमपि हहाहातुस्मरामि प्रभामि॥`(III. 9)

`मन्दा गतिः मदवदसि कुची च`
`कुम्भी दन्ती कपोलफलकौ करसम्प्रद्रू।`
`त्वं हस्तिनी तदपि किं वकितासि`
`गन्तुं हं हन्त हन्त विद्धि हरिम्बद्योगीगात्॥`(III. 20)

Lord Narasimha's love-sick condition is described below –

`चन्दनं विरहिणी विनिन्दन् वन्दिका कदनवीततन्द्रिका।`
`मन्मथो भवति हन्त हन्मथो मालिका विरहाताप्रभूूलिका॥`(IV, p. 45)

We have the beautiful description of Vāsantikā at first sight by the Lord.

[]
`अहो! प्राक्तनपुण्यतन्त्रमनगोरायुष्यसिद्धिदृषं`
`शृङ्गारायतनं विधेः वरतनुसृष्टिक्रियामातृका।`
`रागोद्दीपनकेलिसिद्धघटिका लावण्यधारस्थली`
`कैषा शैशवयौवनान्तरचरी योषा दरिदृश्यते॥`(I. 28)

and

`कविता वनिता चैव स्वयमेवागता वरा।`
`बलादाकृष्यमाणा चेत् सरसा विरसा भवेत्॥`(I. 38)

In conclusion it may be said that this drama provides the genealogy of the first seven Jīyars of Ahobila Maṭha. It gives the title of the seventh Jīyar as *sarvatantra svatantra* and *kavitārkika kaṇṭhīrava*. The author of this drama was probably the guru of Allasāni Peddana the Telugu poet of Kṛṣṇa Deva Rāya of Vijayanagar and he received the ochre robes from Parāṅkuśa Muni, the 6th Jīyar of Ahobila Maṭha who was honoured by Mukunda Deva Rāya of Orissa and the King of Karṇāṭaka.

An extract from the introductory portion of the drama is furnished below as it provides the genealogy of the first seven Jīyars of Śrī Ahobila Maṭha:

v.5. आसीत् व्यासस्य वीप्सा शुकमुनियमकं पुण्डरीकदृग्लप्तिः
प्रह्लादस्याऽनुवादः प्रभृतिमतिकुलप्राणनिर्वाणलाभिः।
प्राज्ञानां यस्य राढां पदविनतिकृतामर्हणार्थोपदेशात्
अहॆय्याहॊभगनिगदित समधिकामदिक्स्यातातां च॥
नाटर्चं किल निश्कुलबलवर्धयताम् ...
चतुस्सप्ततिसंख्यानिनाथातवेष्णवकुले भद्रास
नाधिपत्यं पुराविद उदाहरन्ति।

[]
v.7. `नारायणो मुनिरथॊऽथ पराङ्कुशार्यः`
`श्रीश्रीनिवासमुनिरप्यथ वण्शठारिः।`
`पञ्चात् पराङ्कुशहामुनिरविरासीत्`
`इत्थं जना जगति हन्त न जानते किम्॥`

v.10. `तस्मात्लब्धया तृतीयग्रन्थसमसमुद्भविष्यल्लाभात्स्वराभिः`
`प्रादुर्भूतप्रबोधाभृतकरमुषिताशेषमोहान्धकारः।`
`गाढध्यानावधानप्रमदवहश्शयप्रीतिदेवप्रसादो-`
`दञ्चत् साहित्यमार्गा जगति विजयते वण्शठारियतीन्द्रः॥`

The Genealogical Table as construed from the *Vāsantikāpariṇaya* is as follows:

- Ādi Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa I (1379-1458)
- Nārāyaṇamuṉi I (1458-73)
- Parāṅkuśārya I (1473-85)
- Śrīnivāsamuni I (1485 -93)
- Vaṇ Śaṭhāri II (1493 -98)
- Ṣaṣṭha Parāṅkuśamuni II (1499 -1513)
- Vaṇ Śaṭhāri III (1513 - 22)

The author was the son of Śrīnivāsa, son of Cāruvācālaya, son of Tiruvanantārya of Bharadvāja gotra, native of Bālavana agrahāra of Tuṇḍīramaṇḍala. He was praised by Vāhinipati, a great poet. His original name was stated to be Tirumala and he had the title of *Kavitārkika Kaṇṭhīrava*.

[]
***Puruṣakāra Mīmāṁsā***[^191]

The *Puruṣakāra Mīmāṁsā* occupies an important place in the philosophical contribution of the Jīyars of Ahobila Maṭha. It consists of about 183 verses approximately, and deals with Śrī as the mediator (*puruṣakāra*) in great detail. Studied along with its lucid commentary *Maṇidīpikā* by Śrīśaileśa, it helps in understanding the intricacies of the concept of Śrī as *puruṣakāra*. Each and every word of the *śloka* of Nārāyaṇa Muni is explained, providing scriptural evidence from *Vedas, Upaniṣads*, the *Rāmāyaṇa, Mahābhārata, Viṣṇupurāṇa* etc. He quotes from the works of earlier *ācāryas* like Yāmuna, Rāmānuja, Kūreśvara, Parāśara Bhaṭṭa and Vedāntadeśika.

Nārāyaṇa Muni in the very opening verse of the work, has summarised the central theme of his work, thus :

`स्वतन्त्रः स्वेच्छया सृष्टिस्थितिसंहारमोक्षणे।`
`मत्समक्षं क्रीडतीतः तं भजे लोकमातरम्॥`

He states that creation, maintenance, dissolution and liberation of the universe are the functions of the Lord who is the only independent principle. All these activities take place due to His own free will. He performs the

[^191]: By Śrī Nārāyaṇa Muni (14th Jīyar), See *Concept of Śrī as Puruṣakāra according to the Puruṣakāra Mīmāṁsā of Nārāyaṇa Muni* - unpublished Ph.D. thesis submitted to the University of Madras by G. Sakuntala, July, 1992.

[]
activities in the presence of the Divine Mother Lakṣmī, which activity becomes their sport.

From this simple verse, we can conclude that Viṣṇu and Śrī form the Divine couple, and that Lord Viṣṇu alone has the full fledged responsibility of creation, dissolution etc. The role of Śrī can be appreciated as the Mother of the universe since she is the consort of the Lord. The subsequent verse –

`स्वयंव्यक्ते रङ्गधाम्नि तत्त्वे वात्सल्यतूलके।`
`निवसन्ती नमास्याबौ दम्पती जनको विधेः॥`

qualifies the meaning of the first verse by declaring that this divine couple (Lord Raṅganātha and Raṅganāyakī at Śrīraṅgam) form the parents of Brahmā, the four-faced god. These two verses taken together, mean that Śrī is ascribed the quality of *jagajjanakatva* along with the Lord. The aim of *Puruṣakāra Mīmāṁsā* is to decide beyond doubt, if Śrī the *patnī* of the Lord can lay claim to all the features of the Lord, in the manner He possesses them; *patnyāḥ pativadirktvam asti neti nirūpyate* (v. 4 a). According to Nārāyaṇa Muni, Lord alone is the direct means of salvation and Śrī's *upāyatva* is explained through her status as an attribute of the Lord and never as the substantive i.e. the Lord.[^192] Regarding *nigraha* also, since Śrī is purely of the nature of *anugraha* also She is not directly connected with it and She never desires to display it (*śaktiḥ śrīyosti neccheti*).

[^192]: See G. Sakuntala's Thesis, p. 91.

[]
For Nārāyaṇa Muni the *viśeṣaṇatva* of Śrī generates her *kāraṇatva, upāsyatva* and *prāpyatva*. Her creation is marked by pure unalloyed grace. Since the Lord is qualified eternally by Śrī, whatever qualities the Lord has, can also be shared by Śrī. One cannot imagine a substance without an attribute and all the features of the substantive can be ascribed to the attribute which is a part and parcel of the substantive. So, Śrī becomes the soul of the entire universe which forms Her body. She becomes a *Śeṣiṇī* and is coeval with the Lord in all His aspects except in *nigraha*. Whenever the Lord is mentioned as *kāraṇa, upāsya, upāya* and *prāpya* the presence of Śrī is also included. To comprehend the meaning of vv. 23, 24 Śrīśaileśa's commentary is very helpful. To resolve the apparent contradiction that *Brahmalakṣaṇa* cannot be applied to Śrī, according to *Tattva Ṭīkā* and that the divine couple constitute the cause of the universe according to *Nyāya siddhāñjana*, he says that the qualities of *mātṛtva* and *anugraha* of Śrī were not taken into consideration while speaking of *jagatkāraṇatva*.[^193] Absence of certain qualities in Śrī does not make Her the Brahman technically, but this does not deny Her the status of being equal to Him in other aspects.

Explaining why Śrī cannot be accepted to be the agent of all cosmic activities involving *nigraha* in v. 23. Śrīśaileśa points out that

[^193]: See *Maṇidīpikā*, G. Sakuntala's thesis, p.21.

[]
*samastakāryahetutvam*, agency regarding the individual destruction, creation of hell etc are unique to the Lord and are absent in Śrī.

`समस्तकार्यहेतुत्वमित्यत्र व्यष्टिसंहारनारकादिकार्यस्यापि प्रतिपत्तेः तदे-`
`तुत्वस्य निग्रहहिततयादेव्यसंभवेन समस्तकार्यहेतुत्वं पतिमात्र-`
`निष्ठमित्यभ्युपेयम्।`

Nārāyaṇa Muni's final verdict on Śrī's position is stated in vv. 47, 48 – the characteristic of Brahman namely causality regarding the universe applies only to the Lord and not to both. Creatorship means "being the agent of creation" i.e being the locus of volition which is favourable for creation, not merely being *vibhu* since in that sense, Time which is all-pervasive should also be accepted as creator. So *vibhu cetanatva* cannot be the qualification required of a creator. So the *sāmyatva* between the Lord and Śrī should be understood without infringing upon the characteristics of Brahman, mentioned in the *śrutis* and *sūtras*.

Verses 50, 52 mention the qualities common to Śrī and Viṣṇu which make their *dāmpatya* eternal. Hence there is no difficulty in explaining *sāmya* and *aikya* between them. *Sāmya* according to Nārāyaṇa Muni consists in their being the parents of the whole universe. The term *jagat* in *jagajjanakatva* (v. 53) should mean the world of living beings and this quality of parenthood is found in the Lord only and Śrī acquires this indirectly by virtue of her sharing the joy of creation along with the Lord. The *pati-patnībhāva* between the Lord

[]
and Śrī is taken up for discussion with reference to *sāmyatva* (vv. 56, 57). *Sāmya* is understood as *śeṣitva* which is twofold:
a. with reference to two *vibhūtis* and
b. with reference to one another in being *pati* and *patnī*. Normally this indicates *svāmitva* and so there is no question of one being subordinate or superior to the other.

Then Nārāyaṇa Muni speaks of *aikya* or oneness between Lord and Śrī. It can be – (a). *prakāraikya* (oneness of the mode) because of extreme similarity between husband and wife.
(b). *śeṣatva* of the entire creation including *nitya* and *līlāvibhūtis*.
(c). *ātmahavis* i.e., oneness with regard to being recipients of *havis* in the form of all the souls.

There are some critics who argue that it is cumbersome to accept the divine couple Lakṣmī Nārāyaṇa as two persons (v. 64) and as such it will be parsimonious to accept one single deity. Nārāyaṇa Muni argues that if parsimony is the only criterion then the pluarality of *jīvas* can be dismissed and only one *jīva* should be accepted, which is however rejected by Śrī Rāmānuja. Statements involving *abheda* between Lord and Śrī can be explained by *Rāmasugrīvayoraikyam* (v. 65) without undermining the essential difference between each other. In some passages where Śrī is stated to be the *śakti* of the Lord, it should be taken to mean *śakti* as the *viśeṣaṇa* of

[]
the Lord (v. 67). At the time of creation, this *śakti* is identified with Śrī and She can be taken as *sahakārikāraṇa*. The words *samānā niyatyā* do not mean that Śrī has all cosmic activities as her sport as he is incapable of *nigraha*. Hence, this expression means *sāmarasya*, as having identical taste - *bharturlīlāyāmaikarasyāt tadanuguṇatvopapattiriti bhāvaḥ* - Śrī induces the Lord to action only through *sāmarasya* as expressed in following–

`नाज्ञया न च दानेन प्रेरयत्यन्नं न प्राज्ञया` v. 68 a

In v. 74, Nārāyaṇa Muni observes that the Lord is referred to in some texts as *nārīmaya* because He is the *ādhāra* of Śrī who represents all womanhood; and Śrī is referred to as *Nārāyaṇātmikā* because she is the consort of the Lord. But there is no fear of *dvairājya* or dual rulership because of the special status of *Viṣṇupatnī* accorded to Śrī. The commentator Śrīśaileśa asserts that the definition of *Īśvara* given in *Nyāyasiddhāñjana* as *svajñānāsvetara-samastadravya-śarīratvam* is intended to exclude Brahmā, Rudra and other gods from the scope, but not Śrī.[^194]

Verse 80 is significant in that it declares that only the Supreme Brahman qualified by Śrī should be resorted to on the authority of the definition of *prapatti*, the *mantra* which speaks of it and the injunction which ordains it,

[^194]: See *Maṇidīpikā*, G. Sakuntala's thesis, p.124.

[]
`न्यासस्य लक्षणमन्त्रान् विविधेः व्याख्यान्तरादपि।`
`भाष्यद्भिः संपदायाच्च प्रपत्तव्यः परः पुमान्॥`

The definition of *prapatti* viz. *ananyasādhyā* is by one Bharata Muni. The *mantra* which ordains *prapatti* is *Dvaya* and the *vidhi* which ordains it is in the *Carama śloka - māmekaṁ śaraṇaṁ vraja* (*Bhagavad Gītā* , xvii, 66).

Verses 83 - 85 explain the exact role of 'Śrī' as a *viśeṣaṇa* of the Lord being ever associated with Him. Hence she becomes the recipient of the *bhara* of those who surrender to the Lord also. Even during the stage of *nyāsa*, She remains an attribute of the Lord, destroys the sins of the devotees, generates a taste in them for the Lord who forms the goal, produces a conviction that Lord alone is the *upāya* and ensures His grace for them.

`विशेषणतया न्यासदशायामपि तिष्ठति।`
`पापनाशं प्राप्यरुचिं प्रापकाध्यवसाविताम्॥`

In v. 91 the word *aikarasya* should be interpreted to mean *sāmarasya* according to Śrīśaileśa.

The Lord alone is *daṇḍadhara* and Śrī can never afford to get angry because she is free from *nigraha*. The *śeṣatva* of Śrī covers every living being other than the Lord. The chief criterion of the *upāyatva* of Śrī is the removal of the impediments i.e. *nigraha nivṛtti*. Śrīśaileśa quotes profusely from

[]
*Śrutis* and *Smṛtis* and Deśika's *Rahasyatrayasāra*, Rāmānuja's *Gadyas*, and *Vedārthasaṅgraha* in his commentary to illustrate this point.[^195]

The discussion then shifts to the status of Śrī as *viśeṣaṇa* of the Lord who is called *siddhopāya*. How can anyone state that Śrī becomes an *upalakṣaṇa* (indicator) in the first part of the *Dvayamantra* (v. 100)? The *Rahasyatrayasāra*, the *Gadyabhāṣya*, and the *Catuślokībhāṣya* of Deśika do not prove Śrī as either an *upalakṣaṇa* or an *upāya*. Their intention is only to show Her as a *viśeṣaṇa* of the Lord. Śrīśaileśa in his commentary justifies Nārāyaṇa Muni's stand and states that there is no question of duality of *upāyas*. The *upāyatva* of Śrī lies in Her conferring the experience of complete bliss whereas the *upāyatva* of the Lord lies in His conferring such an experience after shedding his wrath.[^196]

The *puruṣakāratva* and *nityayoga* of Śrī are acceptable on all hands but Śrī as an *upāya* is explained only through her status as *viśeṣaṇa* and not as the chief *upāya* like Her Lord as in Vedāntadeśika's *Rahasyatrayasāra* and *Nyāsatilaka*:

`लक्ष्माः पुरुषकारत्व-नित्ययोगी सतां सती।`
`विशेषणतया न्यासविष्यत्वमिहाधिकम्॥`

[^195]: See *Maṇidīpikā*, G. Sakuntala's thesis, pp. 174 - 201.
[^196]: Ibid. p. 222.

[]
In v. 107 Nārāyaṇa Muni states that the idea of Śrī's *viśeṣaṇatva* is reinforced by the *Brahmasūtra* (III.2.20) *vṛddhihrāsa* etc. All the illustrations given to support Śrī's *viśeṣaṇatva* become justified on the analogy of the *dṛṣṭāntas*. Śrīśaileśa's commentary is elaborate and he states that illustrations need not be taken to correspond to the illustrated in all aspects. The sun reflected in ponds, wells, rivers and vessels may have different shapes, but still the sun cannot be associated with those shapes.

`परमात्मनः चेतनाचेतनरूपनानावस्थानेऽपि चेतनाचेतनगतदोषाननुषङ्गेन`
`दाहॆन्तिक- दृष्टान्तयोः वैषम्यं नास्ति।`[^197]

The status of Śrī as *upāya* which prompts one to perform *bharanyāsa* to the Lord is the result of her being the attribute of the Lord. This idea is brought out in v.110.

`यद्वाप्यात महविर्ह्यते प्राधान्यम् उभयोरपि।`
`विश्लेषणं शरण्यस्य भरन्यासे तथापि सा॥`
`भरालम्न्यासधोर्धदादन्योन्मृतिवारतः॥`

The commentator quotes from the *Rāmāyaṇa, Sāttvatasaṁhitā* and *Viṣṇusahasranāma stotra*, Yāmuna and Parāśara to state that Śrī is an adjective of the Lord (*śaraṇya*) at the time of *śaraṇāgati*. He describes *nyāsa* to be of three kinds - *svarūpanyāsa* (offering one's essential nature), *bharanyāsa* (reposing one's burden) and *phalanyāsa* (offering the fruit of

[^197]: See *Maṇidīpikā*, G. Sakuntala's thesis, p. 246.

[]
one's endeavour). In all these, Śrī is only the *viśeṣaṇa* and never the *pradhāna* like the Lord.

In v.117 Nārāyaṇa Muni clearly declares that Lord Viṣṇu alone forms the cause of the universe, that He alone has to be resorted to for liberation and that He becomes the protector as well as the goal along with Śrī. Nārāyaṇa Muni is puzzled as to why critics do not relish the attribute and substantive principle of Śrī and Viṣṇu who form a single *śeṣī* principle with identity of taste (*aikarasya*) in all functions. In v. 135:

`यद्विच्छायैव यत्पीत्यै शासनं निग्रहादि च।`
`तत्र निग्राह्यजातीयविजातीयतामतिः॥`

the author declares that Śrī belongs to *Īśvarakoṭi* and not *jīvakoṭi* because the Lord commands and chastises all the beings only according to the wish and for the pleasure of Śrī and hence, it is logical to conclude that she belongs to a category different from *jīvas*. There is no problem of *dvairājya* because the relation between Lord and Śrī is similar to the relation between radiance (*prabhā*) and the Sun. Hence, one adds to the excellence of the other and there is no other entity which affects that excellence i.e. there is inseparable relationship (*apṛthaksiddhatva*) between them which only confirms the *viśeṣaṇatva* of Śrī.

In v.161 the author mentions Piḷḷai Lokācārya by name and tries to reconcile the differences between him and Vedāntadeśika. According to him

[]
both are *āptas* (v. 164) or benefactors to humanity and their works should not be subjected to narrow interpretations and declares that the works of Deśika and Piḷḷai Lokācārya should be considered in the light of their intentions and we should draw parallels rather than highlight the apparent differences. Even as the *Pūrvamīmāṁsā* of Jaimini and *Brahmasūtra* of Bādarāyaṇa are considered to be *ekaśāstra*, the work of Piḷḷai Lokācārya and Vedāntadeśika should constitute a single *śāstra* as far their intention and ultimate import is concerned.

`यथा च धर्ममीमांसा-ब्रह्ममीमांसयोर्द्वयोः।`
`अविरुद्धार्थतात्पर्यात् एकशास्त्र्यं समर्थितम्॥`(171)

In the succeeding two verses he pays glowing tributes to *Śrīvacana-bhūṣaṇam* and other works of Piḷḷai Lokācārya. In v.176, the author states that instead of indulging in useless discussions one should concentrate on the *upāya* and *phala* as suggested by these *ācāryas*.

The catholicity of approach in this work is to be commended. The author breathes the spirit of synthesis into his work and teaches the lesson of unity in diversity to the Śrīvaiṣṇava community as a whole. The author's scholarship and his thorough knowledge of not only Deśika's work but those of Piḷḷai Lokācārya as well, his ability to condense the essence of philosophy into verse form is all evident from this work. Śrīśaileśa's lengthy commentary elucidates this poetic work in prose form.

[]
***Bhagavadgītārthasaṅgraha vibhāga***[^198]

The *Bhagavadgītārthasaṅgrahavibhāga* is a commentary on the *Gītārthasaṅgraha* of Śrī Yāmunācārya. It is the first and perhaps only one of its kind in the post-Vedāntadeśika period to interpret the *Gītā* in the Viśiṣṭādvaita tradition.

The author of this prose commentary is Nārāyaṇa Muni and from the *maṅgala śloka* and colophon of the text, it is reasonable to infer that he is the 14th Pontiff of Śrī Ahobila Maṭha. The title *Vibhāga* is significant in that the term refers not only to the division of verses into *ṣaṭkas* as was done by Śrī Yāmuna, but also means an explanatory treatise or analysis of the contents of the *Gītārthasaṅgraha*.

Initially, the author pays his obeisance to Lord Hayagrīva and prays for His grace to elucidate the meanings contained in the treatises of Śrī Yāmuna, Śrī Rāmānuja and Svāmī Deśika - the *trayīmaulisūris*. Beginning with the first verse of Yāmuna which is *maṅgala śloka* as it opens directly with *vastunirdeśa*, the author defines *bhakti* on the lines of Śrī Rāmānuja as *mahaniyaviṣaye prītiḥ* i.e. love or devotion for the most worshipful being viz. Lord Nārāyaṇa. He terms the *Gītā* as *Upaniṣatsārasaṅkalanātmikā* i.e. as the

[^198]: By Śrī Nārāyaṇa Muni (14th Jīyar), See *Bhagavadgītārthasaṅgraha vibhāga* (an edition with English translation), unpublished M.Phil. Dissertation by K.N.C. Sumitra, Department of Sanskrit, University of Madras, 1995.

[]
epitome of the very essence of the Vedāntas which teaches us that Lord Nārāyaṇa who is the abode of innumerable auspicious qualities is the Supreme Reality who can be reached through *bhakti* and *prapatti*.

In the first six chapters the performance of *karmayoga* and *jñānayoga* are explained: The *nitya* and *naimittikakarmas* should be performed without any attachment to the fruits there of but only with the sole purpose of *paramātmaprīti*. These two courses of discipline aim at mental concentration and their main aim is *ātmānubhūti* or self-realisation.

The next six chapters deal elaborately with *bhaktiyoga* or path of devotion which fosters a realisation of the true nature of Bhagavān who is the repository of the six qualities of *jñāna, bala, śakti, vīrya, tejas* and *aiśvarya*.

The third *ṣaṭka* is again divided into two halves. The first deals with the three realities or *tattvatraya* and the second half deals with the performance of *nitya* and *naimittika* duties with loving devotion and without attachment to the fruits.

Commenting on v. 8 of the *Gītārthasaṅgraha*, the author states that the term *sva* refers to the Lord's incarnations as *matsya, kūrma*, etc., and goes on to explain that even in these *avatāras* His essential *svabhāva* is *asādhāraṇa* or unique i.e. it is untouched by *karma* or *prakṛti*. It is always *aprākṛta* only. Following the footsteps of Vedāntadeśika and Rāmānuja, Nārāyaṇa Muni

[]
states that *yoga-abhyāsa* is a necessary prelude to *bhakti-yoga* discussed in the succeeding *ṣaṭka*. In v.14, the author states that the divine qualities of the Lord are mentioned again with a view to intensity the *bhakti* aspect. That *viveka*, the discrimination between the body and the soul, and the realization that the individual soul is of the form of knowledge is discussed in v. 18. i.e., *kṣetrakṣetrajñaviveka, aiśvarya* and *bhagavatprāpti* are explained and the author states that all the three culminate ultimately in Bhagavān only.

Verse 22 is significant since the author discusses the point of *prathamapravṛtti* or the so-called initial effort. The author explains that for all actions there are five causes: a) the physical body or the substratum, b) the individual soul who is the agent, c) the different functions of the sense-organs and e) last but not the least, the divine will which is the underlying cause because the Lord dwells as *antaryāmin* in all beings. The injunction in the *śāstras* is for individual souls alone and since the Lord has granted the body with its ensuing sense organs and free will, the *jīvas* act according to their past *karma* and having the Lord as their indweller. This is similar to moving a rock or treee by many persons, all of whom are collectively and individually the agents of that act.

In v. 23, the author stresses the need for performing one's *karma* according to one's *varṇa* and *āśrama*. The author gives his own definition of *karmayoga* thus:

[]
`कर्मयोगस्तपस्तीर्थदानयज्ञाद्युत्तमाः।`
`वेदाभ्यासो ज्ञानयज्ञः शमहोमाद्यनानि च॥`

The author enumerates the ten different types of *tapas* - *tīrtha* is visiting sacred river and holy place; *yoga* is meditation, *dāna* is *dravya yajña* and it is that act by which one gives up one's ownership right; *yajña* is *yāga* or sacrifice to the gods; *homa* is sacrifice to gods other than Brahmā and Agni; *prāṇāyāma; vedābhyāsa* is individual prayer or meditation; *jñānayajña* is studying the inner meaning of the Vedas; *śama* is control of internal and external sense organs and *arcana*, worshipping the Lord. These *aupacārika karmas* lead one to devotion and finally to *śaraṇāgati* or *prapatti* which is the main teaching of the *Gītāśāstra*. Yāmuna defines *bhaktiyoga* as *Paraikāntaprītyā dhyānādiṣu sthitiḥ*. The performance of *nitya* and *naimittika* duties is stressed in all the three *yogas* and though other deities are propitiated it is the Lord who is the *antaryāmin* in all these deities, who is propitiated.

In v. 27, the author discusses *kaivalya* and says that this can be reached by all the three *yogas*. The author here refers to his own work *Gītāsārarakṣā*[^199] for a detailed description of *kaivalya*. In the commentary of v. 30 the *paramaikāntin* is described in great detail by the author. The term *nyasyet* in v. 32 indicates *prapatti* and *abhīḥ* denotes freedom from fear of one's sins (*svakṛta aparādhas*).

[^199]: p. 55.(which is not available now).

[]
Towards the end, the author summarises the entire *Gītāśāstra* in about seven verses[^200] as a sort of *maṅgala* and details out the *phalaśruti* also. He gives his own commentary for these seven verses. By the phrase *iti gītārthasaṅgravibhāgaḥ* all other rival schools of thought like Advaita stand rejected.

In this prose track, the author's strict adherence to the interpretations offered by *ācāryas* like Yāmuna, Rāmānuja and Svāmī Deśika is evident. It is written only as an elucidatory treatise to the great works of the *ācāryas*. His style is simple and each word is explained in detail. The author's comments provide interesting reading. Another significant point is that the author refers to his work other work *Gītāsārarakṣā*.

***Jijñāsāsūtrabhāṣya-Bhāva Prakāśikā*** [^201]

The author of this commentary is Nārāyaṇa Muni who in all probability, is the 14th Jīyar of Ahobila Maṭha since he has the title *Śrīvatsāṅka* as mentioned in the colophon.[^202] This is a metrical composition interspersed with verses in *sragdharā* and *anuṣṭubh* metres.

[^200]: See pp. 64-65.
[^201]: By Śrīvatsāṅka Śrīman Nārāyaṇa Muni (14th Jīyar), Adyar D.X. 213. Palm leaf manuscript (Grantha characters), pp. 260-262.
[^202]: `नारायणेन मुनिना श्रीवत्साङ्केन निर्मितः।`

[]
As the title *Bhāvaprakāśikā* suggests, this commentary on the first *Brahmasūtra-Athāto Brahmajijñāsā* (I,i,1), explains the import of the *sūtra*. The author also refers to it as *Bhāvapradīpikā*. At the very outset, the author states that the *Karmakāṇḍa* and the *Brahmakāṇḍa* portions should be taken together as a single unitary text because the subject dealt with in both is *vedārtha* and that the fruit is also the same viz., ascertainment of the import of the *Vedas* (*tannirṇayaḥ*). The import of the *Vedas* is Brahman only and the fruit is also Brahman though the *Karmakāṇḍa* and *Brahmakāṇḍa* portions may deal with different subsidiary topics. As the desired knowledge of Brahman depends on the interpretations of Vedic texts and as one who has studied the *Vedas* naturally takes to the study of the exposition of the *karma* first, therefore, an enquiry into *karma* must first be taken up. When from such an inquiry a person learns that the result of all *karma* is ephemeral and limited, while he finds that another part of the *Vedas* says that the knowledge of Brahman yields eternal and unlimited results, viz. liberation, a desire to know Brahman arises in him. So, the *nityānityaviveka* is a consequence of the complete understanding of the *Karmakāṇḍa* portion. *Adhyayana* should be the first step in this direction and *rāga* or desire to understand the import of Vedic injunctions will dawn at a latter date according to the eligibility of an individual.

[]
The author refutes the views held by different schools of Buddhism, namely Vaibhāṣikas and Sautrāntikas who declare the identity of body and soul (*nātmā dehātiriktaḥ*) and postulate the theory of *kṣaṇikatva*. The author is of the view that there is hardly any difference between the Śūnyavādin and the Advaitin, as the latter says that *jñātṛ* and *jñeya* are all *mithyā* and the former speaks of only *śūnya*. The concept of *Nirguṇa* Brahman is refuted and according to Rāmānuja, *Nirguṇa Śrutis* are actually in conformity with the auspicious qualities of the Lord (*kalyāṇa anuguṇā eva*)[^203].

`निर्गुणत्वेऽपि विद्वत्पन्नं सगुणध्यानचिन्तनां फलम्।`
`गुणानां पारमात्म्यं वौ हानिर्निर्गुणवादिनाम्॥`

The author states that the *Sadvidyā* section of the *Chāndogya* establishes only *Saguṇa Brahman*.

The author uses the term *Viśiṣṭādvaita* in the course of this work and defines it as *Viśiṣṭasya advaitam* i.e Brahman is one but qualified by attributes. Brahman has *cit* and *acit* as his body. The *muktas* also form the *prakāra* of the Lord, and as far as the eight *guṇas* are concerned there is *aikya* between *jīvas* and the Lord. The author states that three types of *advaita* are taught in the scripture-(1) between the liberated (*mukta*) and the Brahman (2) between Brahman on one hand and the *cit* and *acit* on the other, and (3) between one *jīva* and another *jīva*.

[^203]: Folio 2.

[]
So, the reason for the inquiry is the unsatisfactory character of the ends promised by the *karmakāṇḍa* portion of the *mīmāṁsā*. The inquiry is for the purpose of gaining knowledge of Brahman, which is the *summum bonum* of all existence. This knowledge is not mere intellectual understanding but a devout and intense meditation on Brahman viz. *bhakti* according to Rāmānuja. When viewed in this aspect, there is *sauhārda* between the *karmakāṇḍa* and *brahmakāṇḍa* portions.

Thus in this small metrical tract, the author has attempted to establish the oneness of the *karma mīmāṁsā* and *brahma mīmāṁsās* and in the process refutes the Śūnyavādins, Advaitins and Dvaitins. The author's clarity of understanding the ideas of Rāmānuja as expounded in the *Śrībhāṣya* is evident. His ability to condense his thoughts in simple verse form is quite clearly seen in this work.

***Śrīstava***[^204]

This is a hymn in praise of Goddess Śrī in 100 verses in *sragdharā* metre. A perusal of this hymn reveals the influence of earlier *ācāryas* like Yāmuna, Śrīvatsāṅka, Parāśara and Vedāntadeśika on the author, not only on the ideas expressed regarding Śrī, but also in the expressions employed.

[^204]: By Śrī Parāṅkuśa Rāmānuja Yatīndra Mahā Deśika (24th Jīyar), pub. by Śrī Kalyāṇapuram Cakravarthi at Kumbhakoṇam in Śrī Komalamba Press, 1939 (Grantha characters).

[]
To cite a few examples: (v. 3)

`या श्रीरित्येव नामा श्रुति-तदनुगुणस्मृत्युपात्ताखिलानाम्`
`भूतानामीश्वरी या निखिलचिदचितां जन्मरक्षादिहेतुः।`
`भोगाभोगो यदीक्षाविशिखविनिहता विध्युती विश्वनेतृ-`
`र्वा चाऽवज्ञविशं जननि कथमहो वीक्ष्यसे मादृशस्त्वम्॥`

Terms like *khādyam hṛdyānavadyam* (v. 6), *nityā siṁānukampā* (v. 9), *pūrṇam tejaḥ* (v. 16) *nityāmoda* (v. 20) are reminiscent of the terms used by Vedāntadeśika in his *Śrīstuti*.

For the author, Śrī is the consort of Lord Nṛsiṁha the presiding deity of Ahobilam, *yatsthānānko nṛsiṁhaḥ* (v. 1). She is *nṛhareḥ praṇayinī* (vv. 8, 11, 17), *śrīmannṛsiṁhapraguṇabhagavatī* (v. 10), *nṛhareḥ vallabhā* (v. 62). She has *aprākṛtadehā* (divine body) like the Lord Himself (v. 29). In v. 7 the author prays that his art of poesy be blessed by Śrī's benevolent glances.

The idea of *śrīvatsāṅka* in his *Śrīstava*, that when a dog drinks the water of the Ganges, its innate purity is not lost, is echoed in v. 11:

`हन्त श्वा किं तृषार्तः प्रपततु बिभेत्यामलिन्यन्निवृत्तम्।`

In v. 14, the coronation (*paṭṭābhiṣeka*) of Śrī is described on the lines of Vedāntadeśika. Verse 22 describes etymologically the function of Śrī: *Śṛṇati, Śṛṇoti, Śrāvayati, Śrayate* and *Śrīyate*. Verse 35 states that according to one's *karma*, one attains the body of god, man, animal or plant. As the author proceeds, he addresses Śrī as Maithilī on the lines of Parāśara

[]
Bhaṭṭa in his *Śrīguṇaratnakośa* (v. 41). He enumerates the qualities of Śrī in v. 48.

`ज्ञान शक्तिबलं ते जननि मम कृते ज्योतिरैश्वर्यवीर्यं`
`प्राथम्येन प्रतीता महितबहुगुणास्तद्विशेषाश्च सर्वे।`
`वात्सल्यौदार्यवीर्यं श्रियमतुलप्रथाप्रेमशीलव्यदान्ति-`
`क्षान्तिस्वादुत्वतान्त्यार्जवमधुरकृतज्ञत्वसत्पूर्णताद्याः॥`

In v. 36, the author states that Śrī makes Nṛhari forget the sins of His devotees – *doṣān vismārayitrī*. In v. 49 the author performs *prapatti* to Śrī on the lines of Yāmuna. In v. 50, the author states that it is Śrī's duty to pacify the Lord – *doṣān sarvāneidānapohya*.

In v. 51 the author does *prapatti* at Lord's and Śrī's feet –

`देवि श्रीमन्नृ लक्ष्मींनृसिंहचरणयोरर्पयामीहभार्यं-`
`रुद्वेषाम्भ्यां पितृष्यामनवधिकृपया रक्षणीयः कटाक्षैः।`

thus stressing the unity of the Godhead. In v. 64 the author states that this *līlāvibhūti* subject to creation, maintenance and destruction, is a game of dice for the divine couple:

`प्रियतमभगवत्खेलनं द्यूतमेतत्।`

In v. 65, the author states that the difference in status of lives of people are due to Śrī's benevolent glances:

`श्रीमदभिक्षते कटाक्षेनेहरिदपिते तारतम्याद्युपैतैः`

on the lines of Śrīvatsāṅka's *Śrīstava* (v.9): *loke vanaspatibṛhas-patitāratamyam* ...

[]
Śrī is quick to grant boons (v. 80): *Kṣipraprasādinī*. In v. 84, the author speaks of his own lack of devotion to Lord Nṛsiṁha, to his own *guru* and his incapacity to grasp the meaning of the *mantras*. Only through Śrī's grace his doubts are cleared: *vitaśaṅkā-kalaṅkaḥ*. Then he declares that Śrī is capable of granting learning (*vidyā*) and not merely prosperity (*aiśvarya*). The author speaks of his own total incapability and his own worthlessness to receive Her Grace and yet he prays to Her (v. 29).

`भूयो भूयः पुनस्ते निखिलभुवनसम्प्राप्ति विज्ञापयामि`
`स्वाधोऽन्यो शृण्वतो गतिकरणकुण्ठोऽकिञ्चनोऽतीव मुग्धः।`
`दुष्टो शिक्षप्रविष्टश्चरणरहितो भीत एवाऽऽस्मिमात्रम्`
`त्वेतन्मात्रो हि पात्रं जननि निरवधेस्वर्वदाया दयायाः॥`

In v. 95, the author delineates Śrī as being served by Pārvatī, which indicates Her supreme status:

`त्वामासीनां सुधस्योपरि हिमधरणीभृत्सुता धातुपुत्री।`

Verse 96 is significant in that the author describes Śrī as the support of the whole universe - *sarvalokādhāratva*, and the whole universe is Her body - *etannikhilamapi jagatte śarīram*. She is also *upādānakāraṇa* like Her Lord, and she is free from all demerits. If that is the case, can the quality of *aṇutva* be associated with Goddess Śrī? It is a poignant question and shows that the author disagrees with the Teṅkalai view that Śrī is not *vibhu* (all-pervasive). Again in v. 97, he performs total surrender to the Lord and Śrī.

[]
`शृण्वन् जिह्विपशुपश्यन् जननि किमपि वा संस्पृशन् वा स्वदन्वा`
`गच्छन् गूह्णन् वदन् वाच्यमहमिह निमिषन्नुन्मिषन्वा नमस्यन्।`
`प्राणान् धार्याम्युपेयान् प्रणयिनि नृहरेः मत्कृपाधीनवृत्ति-`
`स्तत् च त्वां त्वत्पतिं चानुषधि परिचरन् सर्वतस्स्यां कृतार्थः॥`

In v. 98 the author prays that his composition should be accepted by Śrī:

`पद्ये पूर्णैः कटाक्षैः कुसुमफलवती संहितास्तु स्तुतिस्ते`
`कामनां कल्पवल्ली प्रभवतु कमले श्रेयसे भूयसे नः॥`

Finally the author mentions the *phalaśruti* and states that those who study this composition of Parāṅkuśa Muni with devotion, will be blessed by the Consort of Nṛhari.

The style of the author is lucid and makes for easy reading and comprehension. He follows faithfully the ideas of his *pūrvācāryas* in his elucidation of the concept of Śrī.

***Śrī-pañcāśat***

This work by the same author is again a hymn of 51 vv. in *sragdharā* on Goddess Śrī. The author here exhibits his poetic skill in the use of *śabdālaṅkāras* like alliteration and *yamaka*. The beauty of maintaining *prāsa* is to be appreciated.

The author begins with the consontant *ka* in *prāsasthāna* (second letter) from the first line of the first verse.

[]
`साकारोकारटङ्काप्रकटितविभवां ...`
`स्वीकारिकार्येकां ...`
`स्वाकारकारिणं कामपि ...`
`पाका मुका वराका ...`

The consonants *ka* to *kṣa* have been chosen as the second letter in each line of the verses, right upto v. 51:

`लक्ष्मीरसय्यलक्ष्मीधरस्तु ...`
`लक्ष्मीभृताक्षरेक्षो ...`
`यक्ष्मीभावक्षमेक्षा ...`
`क्षुब्धमीभृताक्षरादि ...`

In the v. 11, *yamaka* is used effectively.

`स्वच्छं स्वच्छायया वासि ...`

*Svaccha* is first used as meaning pure and *svaccha* in the sense of complexion (*in svacchāyayā*) is used next. In v. 12, the author enumerates some of Śrī's important qualities like compassion (*dayā*), patience (*kṣānti*) and parental affection (*vātsalya*) and states that Śrī rejuvenates the entire creation by her qualities.

`तेजोवाजीवपुर्ज्जगदवसि दयाक्षान्तिवात्सल्यमुख्यैः।`

In v. 25, the author pleads to Śrī to save him who is totally helpless and who has surrendered at Her feet.

`सत्यासत्या नियत्या कृपणमपि जडं मूढवृत्त्या प्रपत्या`
`कृत्वा सत्या महत्या स्वकमव कृपया वत्स मा मां प्रपत्या॥`

[]
The same idea is echoed in v. 33. She is the consort of Nṛsiṁha (*nṛhari sahacarī*) (v. 36) and the author stresses the unity of Godhead in (*Bhagavati Nṛharau*) in v. 43. She is the most beloved of Nṛhari (*nṛhareḥ jvāyasi preyasī śrīḥ*) and She has taken a vow to protect the universe in v. 51 (*jagatkṣemarakṣaikadīkṣā*). The last is the *phalaśruti* that ensues when this *pañcāśat* is read with devotion.

`लक्ष्मीरसय्यलक्ष्मीधरस्तु सरसिजाक्षाधिवक्षसुरक्षा`
`लक्ष्मीभृताक्षरेक्षित(मनोज्ञगम्भीरवीकदीक्षा।`
`यक्ष्मीभावक्षमेक्षणगुणाध्यक्षमायाक्षरक्षा`
`क्षुब्धमीभृताक्षरादिशर हृदि पतिवीक्षाक्षमत्ववीक्षा॥`

From the above avaiable two works of His Holiness the 24th Jīyar, we can appreciate the Svāmī's clarity of thought, his understanding of the *granthas* of Śrīvaiṣṇava preceptors, and his ability to adopt their ideas and convey them in his own style. The second work, also in praise of Śrī is not redundant but actually complements the former. At the same time, we are able to gauge the author's poetic skill and his command over the Sanskrit vocabulary and language. These two hymns make easy reading and can be memorised through repeated study.

[]
***Vaikuṇṭhavijaya-campū***[^191]

The *Vaikuṇṭhavijaya-campū* is a travelogue that details the visit of two imaginary characters Jaya and Vijaya in their aerial path to the temples of Śrīraṅgam, Mysore, Yadugiri, Ayodhyā, Kāśī and Dvārakā. The dialogue between Jaya and Vijaya is significant as it indicates the supremacy of Lord Viṣṇu over Lord Śiva, the necessity of an Ācārya for liberation and highlights the selfless devotion of the *ācāryas* for the propagation of Śrīvaiṣṇava religion and philosophy among the masses. The *Campū* is a form of literature that is interpersed with prose and poetry:-

`गद्यपद्यमयं काव्यं चम्पूरित्यभिधीयते।`

Here, the author employs terse prose (on the lines of Vedāntadeśika's *Raghuvīragadya*) and simple verse form. It is *sarasacārugadyapadyamiśraṇa*, according to the editor, K.E. Govindan. The author begins the work with a benedictory verse addressed to Śrī Lakṣmī Nārāyaṇa and then to Śrī Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha, Śrīkṛṣṇa, Śrī Rāma, Śrī Lakṣmī and then pays his obeisance to the lineage of his family and *ācāryas*. He mentions these in separate *ślokas*[^192] starting from Nāthamuni, Rāmānuja, Nigamānta Mahādeśika, Ādi Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa, Nārāyaṇa Yati, Śrīnivāsa Yati, and Raṅganātha Yati. He salutes

[^191]: By Śrī Vīrarāghava Vedānta Yatīndra Mahādeśika (27th Jīyar), Ganganath Jha Kendriya Samskrita Vidyapitha Granthamala, No:22, ed. K.E. Govindan, pub. by Rastriya Samskrit Sansthanam, New Delhi,1987.
[^192]: *Vaikuṇṭhavijaya-campū*, p. 4.

[]
his great-grandfather Śrīnivāsācārya, grandfather Veṅkaṭācārya and father Śrīnivāsācārya. The author is the disciple of Raṅganāthasvāmī and studied religious works under Śrīnivāsasvāmī. The author takes pride in saying that he was a great scholar in literature (*sāhitya*) and philosophy (*darśana*) and is also well-versed in poetic literature.

`काव्यशास्त्रालङ्कृतिष्वपि च परिख्यात्।`[^193]

He declares that his own poetic achievements are the result of his study of the works of earlier Śrīvaiṣṇava *ācāryas* like Yāmuna, Rāmānuja, and Deśika. In true humility he says that some people may censure his work, but the world is not small and his work will have its own appeal.[^194] Two characters Jaya and Vijaya are introduced who after visiting the three worlds are interested to travel to the earth. Hence they set out on their mission. Jaya is a devotee of Lord Śiva whereas Vijaya is a *viṣṇubhakta*. Hence their dialogue is significant and interesting. Vijaya speaks of the greatness of the Lotus feet of Lord Viṣṇu and waxes eloquent about the supremacy of Lord Viṣṇu and his imerrable auspicious qualities in 13 verses.[^195] To Jāya's query as to why he does not propitiate Śiva, Vijaya replies that Śiva, Brahmā and Indra carry out their duties only as ordained by Lord Viṣṇu.[^196] So he asks Jaya to cast off his

[^193]: *Vaikuṇṭhavijaya-campū*, v.18, p.5.
[^194]: Ibid. v.14, p.6.
[^195]: *Bhagavadpādācūḍābhivandana* similar to Vedātadeśika's *Bhagavad-dhyānasopānam*.
[^196]: *Vaikuṇṭhavijaya-campū*,v. 51, p.17.

[]
veil of ignorance and leave off the study of the *purāṇas* dealing with *tāmasic* qualities. He eulogises the *Bhāgavatapurāṇa, Śrī Viṣṇupurāṇa* and *Śrīmad Rāmāyaṇa* and asks him to develop devotion to Lord Hari as that alone will dispel fear of death –

`हरन्ती पापपाशानय परिहरन्ती यमभयम्।`[^197]

Vijaya again goes into rhapsodies when he speaks of the blissful qualities of Lord Hari in *Hariguṇānandalaharī* in 10 verses. He is not satisfied with this and again bursts out in his *Vedāntapādastava* in another 10 verses in which the last foot of each verse incorporates a Vedic statement. For instance, to quote the very first verse:[^198]

`आनन्दपूर्णं प्रतिमिन्द्रियाभाः भक्तोत्तमं भुवननाथगुप्त्यै।`
`स्वतोऽवतीर्णं दयया भजेयं आदित्त्ववर्णं तमसः परस्तात्॥`

Turning the aerial chariot towards Śrīraṅgam, he pays his obeisance to Lord Raṅganātha and gives a graphic description of the town in 3 verses resounding in alliterations.

`रङ्गं भवभङ्गं भज तुङ्गं तद्वन्दैः स्फीतं भुवि भातं नमदात्मनिर्हान्तम्।`
`श्रीमद् गतमत्सरधीभजनसेव्यं सेवाधिकभागवातदेवालिसान्द्रम्॥`

Here Jaya intervenes and in eight verses casts aspersions on Śrīvaiṣṇava ascetics who pretend to be *saṁnyāsins* (v. 101 *vairāgyam*

[^197]: *Vaikuṇṭhavijaya-campū*, v. 79, p.17.
[^198]: Ibid. v. 88, p. 19.

[]
*bhāvayantaḥ*), but are really attached to worldly dersires (v. 106 *baddha spṛhāḥ*). To this Vijaya, praises the Śrīvaiṣṇava ascetics in two verses and goes a step further to extol the Ācāryapuruṣas:

`आचार्यपुरुषा एते महावचसमुद्गवाः।`
`शिष्यैर्दत्तेन वित्तेन विततेषामवन्द्यते॥`[^199]

These preceptors are munificient and with the wealth acquired through acts of charity, they look after the welfare of their devotees. Vijaya states that there may be defects in an Ācārya, but their unique good qualities overshadow any defect.

`दोषाः सन्तु सहस्रशोऽप्यवितथरामेषां विशेषान् गुणान्`
`दोषपाक्कृत्प्रतिहतान् गुण्तरां लब्धावधानः सखे।`

He goes on to elucidate the story of the sinful Kṣatrabandhu and the virtuous Puṇḍarīkākṣa, both of whom attained liberation only through the grace of an Ācārya (v. 122). The *guru* is the *Parabrahman* and he is the ultimate goal (*parā gatiḥ*) (v. 124). The greatness of *bhakti* is highlighted and this devotion to Lord Hari finally grants liberation (v. 127). He defends the use of Tamil *Divyaprabandhams* (*Dramiḍasaṁhitā*) in temples. Tamil was a great language revered by Agastya (*Kumbhisambhavanāmaka* v. 130), and Nammāḻvār used it to perfection in his *Prabandham*.

[^199]: l p. 23, v. 111.

[]
As they survey Śrīraṅgam, they admire the devotion of the Bhāgavatās who, as they pay their obeisance to the Lord, fall flatly on the ground - *sāṣṭāṅga-namaskāra*. Then follows the description of Candrapuṣkariṇī tank and here *śleṣa alaṅkāra* is employed by the author.[^200]

Then diverting the aerial chariot, they bow down and pay their respects to Lord Raṅganātha in 12 verses. Jaya extols the Lord as the fragrance of fragrances, the essence of all essences and the final abode of all as desires described in the *Śrutis*.

`स सर्वकामः किं सर्वगन्धो विभात्यहो! सर्वर्सो रसत्मा॥` (v. 147)

Vijaya goes on to describe Śrī Raṅganāyikā, who is the consort (*aṅganā*) of Lord Raṅganātha. Jaya intervenes and wants to know why Śrī who is fickle-minded (*capalābhikhyā*) is propitiated. In reply to this Vijaya speaks out the excellence of Śrī in six verses. She is the dispeller of the sins of the universe (*viśvapāpaughamoṣā*) and *viṣṇuśuddhāntayoṣā* and is the granter of all wishes. Then, they pray to Garutmān, the holy vehicle of Lord Viṣṇu.

The description of Garuḍa in 13 verses that follow is on the lines of Vedāntadeśika's *Garuḍapañcāśat*. Then follows the description of *Daśāvatārasannidhi* which grants liberation (*vimuktipradam*). The ten

[^200]: *Vaikuṇṭhavijayacampū*, pp. 28,29.

[]
incarnations of Lord Viṣṇu are described on the lines of the *Daśāvatāra Stotra* of Vedāntadeśika and the author states that these forms were incarnated by the Lord only for the redemption of mankind. The description of river Kāverī follows wherein the sound of waters is echoed in the words used to describe it. *phulladhallakatallajollalalanavat* (v. 162). Then they proceed to Śirocala and Mahiśūrapura (modern Mysore).[^201] Reference is made to King Kṛṣṇa Deva Rāya,[^202] the glory and prosperity of his kingdom and the respect the king had for Śrīvaiṣṇavas - *tārāgaṇavat viṣṇupadasamāśrayasālibiḥ meghairiva vidyutbhāsitaiḥ dvārakāvāsibhirivakṛṣṇarājadayotkarṣasobhanaiḥ*.

The Yadugiri mountain in Melkote is sighted later; then homage is paid to Śrī Rāmānuja referred to as *Yadugiriśekhara*, whose favourite haunt was this hillock. Reference is made to his *Śrībhāṣya* and the profound scholarship with which he defeated rival schools of thought, with the commentaries of *Taṅka, Dramiḍa, Guhadeva*[^203] and he was well known by the term *Śrībhāṣyakāra*. Thousands of devotees entered into his fold and he allowed the entry of *mlecchas*[^204] into the temple of Lord Tirunārāyaṇa who is

[^201]: *Vaikuṇṭhavijayacampū*, p. 44.
[^202]: Ibid. p. 46.
[^203]: Ibid. p. 51.
[^204]: Ibid. p. 57.

[]
described as *yadugiriśikharaśekhara*.[^205] In this description, the author displays his mastery of Sanskrit vocabulary and the ease with which he is able to play on words using *yamaka* and *anuprāsa alaṅkāras*.

Then, Vijaya turns to Kalyāṇī Puṣkaraṇī and pays his obeisance to the holy tank in v. 106. Jaya intervenes and questions as to how a person who worships the tank called Kalyāṇī will achieve all auscipiousness. To this query, Vijaya on the lines of the poet Veṅkaṭādhvarin[^206] takes recourse to *tatkratunyāya*[^207] and states in v. 211 thus:

`कल्याणीभजनात्तु मर्त्यः कल्याणी भवति ध्रुवम्।`
`तत्क्रतुन्याययाथात्म्यं अत्रैव प्रकटीकृतम्॥`

In another ten *ślokas*, Vijaya again eulogises Yadugiri and he concludes in v. 221 with *Nārāyaṇa stuti*.

The aerial chariot then takes a different route and proceeds to Sahyādri, which is described to be the abode of rare and fragrant herbs and trees (v .222) capable of rejuvenating human life and hence the mountain is always flocked by practitioners of Siddha medicine (v. 223), delighted by the fragrance of sandal wood and the beautiful foliage all around.

[^205]: Reference is also made to the 74 *siṁhāsanādhipatis* nominated by Śrī Rāmānuja.
[^206]: Author of the *Viśvaguṇādarśa campū*.
[^207]: The relevant text of the *Chāndogya Upaniṣad* (III, 14, 1) is `यथाक्रतुरस्मिन् लोके पुरुषो भवति तथेतः प्रेत्य भवति।`

[]
The sight of Ayodhyā towards the North, sends Vijaya into raptures and he declares that this town has gained in sanctity because Lord Rāma ruled over it (v. 229) and He is verily Lord Nārāyaṇa, Śrīpatiḥ who has the whole world as His body (v. 234). Then Jaya intervenes to enquire whether Rāma was an incarnation of Śiva (v. 235). Vijaya speaks of the greatness of the Epic *Rāmāyaṇa* in (v. 236) and points out that Rāma should not be taken to mean Śiva, because the very terms *Viṣṇu* and *Nārāyaṇa* are used in relation to Rāma at the beginning, middle and end of the Epic; and by applying the rule of *upakrama* and *upasaṁhāra* in *tātparyanirṇaya*, these names are synonymous and mean only Lord Nārāyaṇa.

In the following five verses he speaks of the glory of Rāmāvatāra and refers to the story wherein Śiva was petrified through the *huṅkāra* of Lord Viṣṇu (v. 241). Reference is also made to Lord's Śiva's reply[^208] to Pārvatī who wanted to know the easy way to recite the thousand names of Lord Viṣṇu:

`केनोपायेन विष्णोरपि खलु लधुना नामसहस्रपाठौ`
`मर्त्यानां बोधवीति प्रिय वद तदिति प्रष्टुमुद्यामुयाम्।`
`तत्पुत्थं रामनामग्रहणामिति हस्योक्तिन्नेषा धुनीते`
`त्वच्छुद्धाशृङ्गं तस्मात् रघुपतिरनघो विष्णुपूर्णवतारः॥` (v. 244)

Vijaya glorifies the potency of reciting the *Rāmanāma* (v. 247) with beautiful alliteration. In a string of 8 verses (*Rāmāṣṭakam*) the author with his mastery of the Sankrit vocabulary extols the greatness of *Kosalendra Rāma*.

[^208]: *Śrī Viṣṇu Sahasranāma*, v.134.

[]
He is the supporter of the universe (*dhātā lokasya*) always the winner in battles (v. 248 *jetā raṇabhuvi*) and he is the source of innuverble auscipious qualities. The *phalaśruti* for reciting the *Rāmāṣṭakam* is also stated. It confers always auspiciousness and long life and removes the greatest of sins. Jaya is puzzled as to how Lord Rāmā is thus praised, though he was the cause of destruction of innumerable *rākṣasas*. Vijaya brushes aside this query and says that the wicked should be punished at all costs and Lord Rāmā is the destroyer of enemies (*virāmāḥ śatrūṇām*). Reference is made to the term *śaraṇāgati* as *bharanyāsa* (v. 255) when Sugrīva resorted to Lord Rāmā's feet seeking for protection from Vāli's attack.

From Ayodhyā they proceed northwards and the River Gaṅgā is described in all its splendour in 10 verses. The sanctifying powers of the river is highlighted and it is mentioned that Lord Śiva's greatness is enhanced because of his association with this river

`बर्हेन्द्रद्राघीयमान् भवति पशुपतिः सर्वविद्द्वत्समीड्यः।`
`नूनं त्वत्सङ्गमामात् ...` (v. 269.)

In v. 271, the author states that those who resort to the Lord for freedom from *bhavabhāva* (worldly existence) attain *Bhavabhāva* (become Śiva). This is an example of *virodhābhāsa alaṅkāra*.

`भवाभावमम्ब परिहर्तुमादरात् भवमुपेत्य भवभावमिच्छति।`

[]
The holy city of Kāśī is described in 4 verses. When Jaya enquires that it is Lord Śiva's abode (*śiva kṣetram iyaṁ kāśī*) Vijaya categorically states that it is because of the intense associations of Lord Viṣṇu with this place that it is the cause of liberation and it is in this vey place that Lord Śiva was conferred boons by Lord Rāma. In the *phalaśruti* it is stated that this *Upaniṣadic* secret meaning when heard by people, will purify them through the grace of Lord Rāmabhadra.

The holy city of Dvārakā is described next, in 4 verses. They pay their obeisance to Lord Kṛṣṇa (*Dvārakāpurīśa*):

`कृष्णाकृतेः भगवतः चरणारविन्दं`
`वृष्णा शिवेन विधिनापि समर्च्यमानम्।`
`तृष्णापहं जनिपथम्रपिणां नराणां`
`मुष्णातु मामकमुदं हृदयान्धकारम्॥` (v. 280)

With this Jaya and Vijaya return to their heavenly abode. The colophon of the text states that the author Vātsya Vīrarāghava has written this *Vaikuṇṭhavijayacampū* which is a precious gem among *campūs* to please Lord Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha.

It is stated in the preface to this book that this *campū* is modelled on the lines of *Viśvaguṇādarśacampū* by Veṅkaṭādhvarin and many points of similarity are brought out. Similarity with Vedāntadeśika's *Daśāvatāra stotra* and *Raghuvīragadya* is also discernible. The author's scholarship and literary and poetic skill in the use of *yamaka* and *anuprāsa* is seen throughout the

[]
work. Later, *ācāryas*[^209] opine that this work is a fitting reply to Nīlakaṇṭha Dīkṣita's *Nīlakaṇṭha Vijaya Campū*. The supremacy of Lord Viṣṇu, the philosophy of Viśiṣṭādvaita wherein the whole universe forms the body of the Lord, the efficacy of *śaraṇāgati*, the necessity of performing *kaiṅkarya* and loving devotion to the Lord and His devotees, the greatness of *ācāryas* and their duties as also those of pontifical heads are all presented through this medium of *campū* with its beautiful admixture of terse prose and simple verse form. To a student of literature, the graphic descriptions of many holy places of worship are a source of sustaining interest. Poetry and prose, religion and philosophy are all brought together in an enjoyable confluence in this work.

***Adhikaraṇakalpataru*** [^210] or ***Padayojanā***

The *Padayojanā* is an explanatory treatise on Śrī Vedāntadeśika *Adikaraṇasārāvalī*. The author has taken into consideration the commentary *Cintāmaṇi* of Śrī Kumāra Varadācārya on *Adhikaraṇasārāvalī*; but feels that this was not an exhaustive explanation. So, the *Padayojanā* has been written to elucidate the meanings so that even a layman who is interested to know about the *adhyātma śāstra*, will be able to grasp its import. The title

[^209]: Preface to *Viśiṣṭādvaitakośa*, p. 15.
[^210]: By Śrī Śaṭhakopa Rāmānuja Yatīndra (34th Jīyar),Vedāntadeśika's *Adhikaraṇasārāvalī*, pub. by Kurucci Lakṣmīnṛsiṁhācārya, Ahobila Maṭha, Śrīraṅgam, 1940.

[]
*Padayojanā* is quite fitting in the sense that each *pada* has been clearly explained with the *padaccheda, padārthokti* and *padāśo'rthaprakāśana*.

In the invocatory verse, the author pays homage to the Lord of Ahobilam and then to his *ācārya* and then to Vedāntadeśika and his son Kumāra Varadācārya. He calls himself Rāmāvāsarāghavācārya as his *pūrvāśrama* name was Śrīnivāsa Rāghavācārya Svāmī.

In the preface the 41st Jīyar (under whose auspices this book was published) opines that the two commentaries *Cintāmaṇi* and *Padayojanā* should be read along with Vedānta deśika's *Adhikaraṇasārāvalī* as they form the conch (*śaṅkha*) and discus (*cakra*) of Deśika's poetic piece that is Brahman.[^211] The preface is significant in that it includes a brief sketch of Ādi Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa's life as also that of the author of *Padayojanā* (Attipaṭṭu Jīyar as he was popularly called), the basic texts of the Viśiṣṭādvaita philosophy and a list of the works of the Jīyar.

Explaining the first word *svasti* of the benedictory verse of the *Adhikaraṇasārāvalī*, the author states that it is *āśīḥ kṣemaṅkara śāsanaviśeṣam* and quotes the lexicon - *āśīḥ kṣemapuṇyādau*. For the term

[^211]: p. xv of the preface. `सारावलीभूषणः सुदर्शन्पाञ्चजन्यवत्। इदुमुभयमपि धार्यमाचार्यवद्भिः॥`

[]
*śāśvat* (which was not explained by Kumāra Varadācārya) our author explains - *punaḥ punaḥ, triṁśadvāram śrāvitāśarīrakabhāṣyaḥ ityādyukta-rityā bahuvāramityarthaḥ*. An interesting explanation is offered for the term *sragdharā-dugdharāśiḥ* i.e. *divya gavya navya dugdhadhārā paramparā*. The *sragdharā* metre employed is a continous stream of fresh milk from the divine cow Kāmadhenu.

As far as the explanation of the verses dealing with *Jijñāsādhikaraṇa* is concerned, since the *Ciñtāmaṇi* is quite elucidative our author confines himself to explaining it in the barest terms without being redundant.

The discussion on the *parāyanādhikaraṇa* affords interesting reading. There are two types of *kartṛtva*[^212] - *prayojaka* and *prayojya*. For the Lord, *śaraṇāgati* is only a mere pretext (*vyājamātra*) and this according to the author may be even a simple act of folding hands (*añjalyādyalpa-vyājam*). Only the Lord who rules from within as the *antaryāmin* of all has *sarvaprayojakakartṛtva*. But since the *jīva* has received the power of discrimination from the Lord, he has *prayojyakartṛtva*, but there is no contradiction between the two. In the *Cintāmaṇi* it is stated that at all times and places the Lord is the motivating factor, but He does this according to one's past *karma*. Hence there is no room for any partiality (*vaiṣamya*) or

[^212]: See *Adhikaraṇasārāvalī*, pp. 387, 388, 389.

[]
cruelty (*nairghṛṇya*) on the part of the Lord toward the *jīvas*. In the *Padayojanā* our author declares that the Lord is the witness of the whole universe (*sarvalokasākṣī*) with its beginningless stream of *karma* and hence the question of original *pravṛtti* does not arise (*mūlakāraṇa praśnasya nāvakāśaḥ*). Towards the end, the author pays his homage to his *ācārya* and says that he has written this treatise on the lines of *Cintāmaṇi* (*cintāmaṇim anubhāvya*).

This is a fairly popular work among the present day scholars. The author supplements and complements the *Cintāmaṇi* of Śrī Kumāra Varadācārya. The original ideas of Vedāntadeśika are brought out clearly without any ambiguity.

***Vādataraṅgiṇī and Other Works***[^213]

This book which is taken up for study, contains the biographical details of the Jīyar rendered in English in about eleven pages followed by its Tamil version which was published earlier in the *Śrī Nṛsiṁha Priyā* monthly journal. In pages X and XI, a list of twentysix known works of the Jīyar is given. Of these, only thirteen are available and published in this edition.

[^213]: By Piḷḷaippākkam Śrī Vīrarāghava Śaṭhakopa (37th Jīyar), Ed. V. Śrīvatsaṅkacharya. pub. by P.N. Krishnaswamy and P.N. Parthasarathi, Madras 1984.

[]
Another work, *Tatkratunyāyasāra*[^214] is available in Manuscript form. This is also taken up for study, in the following pages.

The works studied here are (1) *Śrutigītā Vyākhyā* (2) *Śārīraka Suprabhātam* (3) *Vādataraṅgiṇī* (4) *Tārārthasāra* (5) *Tārārtha-prabhā* (6) *Tatkratunyāyasāra* (7) *Sthuṇā-liṅganirṇaya* (8) *Nyāyasiddhāñjana-kārikā-vimarśanam* (9) *Ādeśamaṇi* (10) *Ādeśamaṇi vyākhyā kaustubha* (11) *Dāsadāsīsamarthanī* (12) *Makārarakṣā* and (13) *Sthemadarpaṇa*.

According to the editor (p.34) there are still 15 works of the Jīyar which are not available now. They are:- (1) *Argalapañcakam* (2) *Ācārya saptati* on his own guru Paruttipaṭṭu Aḻagiya- siṅgar (3) *Śrī Ādi Van Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Vaibhava Candrikā* (4) *Śrī Raṅganātha Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśikastava* (5) *Āṣāḍhyupākarma-abhyanujñā* (6) *Gomālā* (7) *Goṣṭhīnāthastava* (8) *Yan-prakāśa* (9) *Yan-prakāśa Vyākhyāna* (10) *Yatirājabhoga* (11) *Vedāntakaustubhasāra* (12) *Vedāntadeśikastavamālikā* (13) *Raṇapuṅgavastava* (14) *Śrībhāṣyakāra suprabhātam* (15) A few *muktaka ślokas*.

[^214]: Adyar D. X. 223.

[]
***Śrutigītāvyākhyā***

It is a commentary on the 51 verses forming what is called the *Śrutigītā* in the *Bhāgavatapurāṇa*, Skandha 10, Chapter 87. This is also known as *Vedastuti* or *Śrīstuti*. The *mūlaśloka* is given first accompanied by a word for word meaning and relevant explanations in prose followed by the author's *śloka* that sums up the meaning.

For instance, when explaining *śloka* 36 (p.41) the author states that the Ācārya is the very incarnation of the Lord and explains the word *purupuṇya* used in it.

*Ācārya-avatara-lakṣaṇa* is actually *Ācārya-āśrama-viśeṣaṇa-parigrahaṇimittam*. In the ensuing *śloka*, the Lord is addressed as Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha (p.42):

`लक्ष्मींनृसिंह तव पादसरोजचिताः`
`पापापहाद्रिसलिला विमदा महान्तः।`
`न्यस्यन्ति ये सकृदिह त्वयि मोक्षकाङ्क्षा-`
`स्ते तीर्थतां दधति गेहसुबल्यजश्च॥` (22)

Towards the end of the commentary, the author states that he had written this work at the behest of the scholars (*budhavara*) of Tiruvaḷḷūr who were interested to know the Vedic truths contained in the *Śruti Gītā*.

[]
***Śārīraka Suprabhātam***

This is a hymn in 32 verses addressed to Lord Devarāja of Kāñcī who is conceived to be (i) reclining on the milky ocean of the wise sayings of teachers like Rāmānuja, and (ii) the Vedic passages explained in the various *Adhikaraṇas* of the *Brahma-sūtras*. On the lines of Vedāntadeśika's *Adhikaraṇasārāvalī*, the author employs the *sragdharā* metre and awakens the Lord of Kāñcī.

`श्रीरामानुजसूक्तिरुद्धजलधेरूहल्लिं! सुबुद्धितम्।`(1)

In v. 20, the author states that the *paramapuruṣa* is the indweller (*antaryāmin*) of the whole universe –

`तिष्ठत्युञ्चमात्रः पुरुषः इह तथाऽऽङ्गुष्ठमात्रोऽन्तरात्मा`
`लोकानां सन्निविष्टो हृद्य इह सदा भूतभव्येऽशितंति॥`(v.20)[^215]

Towards the concluding part of the work the author mentions the year and month in which he composed this *stotra* –

`उदबुद्धा वीरलक्ष्मीशठरिपुणा भिक्षुणा हेमलंम्बि-`
`न्यब्देऽस्मिन् चापमासे दिनगणणगिताः सप्धराः सर्वधार्योः॥` (v. 31)[^216]

***Vādataraṅgiṇī***

This is a work of grammatical interest in which the author justifies the use of feminine gender in expressions like *bhavatīpādalākṣārāsāṅkam*

[^215]: l p. 59.
[^216]: 2 p. 61.

[]
(Vedāntadeśika's *Śrīstuti*, 4) and *bhavati- bhāgadheyena jīvan* (Vedāntadeśika's *Haṁsasandeśa*, II, 31) where apparently according to Kātyāyana's *Vārtika* (V. 3, 28) *sarvanāmno vṛttimātre puṁvadbhāvaḥ*, the masculine gender has to be used. So, the first example should read as *bhavatpādalākṣā* etc. As the title suggests, the author advances the arguments and counter arguments in the forms of waves, and concludes that this rule does not apply to the term *bhavatī*. This work is also mentioned and discussed in another work titled *Śiṣṭaprayoga-samīkṣā*.[^217] The author concludes with his salutations to his *guru* who had blessed him with the philosophical knowledge–

`इत्थं पुत्स्वं ब्रुवाणः समिधमसदसोदितस्वादुवादो`
`योऽदाद् वेदान्तविद्बागुरुहृदयसमुल्लासिधीलासिकं मे॥`[^218]

***Tārārtha Sāra*** and its commentary ***prabhā; Tatkratunyāyasāra:***[^219]

The *Tārārtha Sāra* is in eight verses and aims to explain the usage of the term *eva* (एव) in the *Śruti* text –

`तं यथा यथोपासते तथैव भवति।`[^220]

[^217]: See editor's note, p. 17.
[^218]: 2 p. 109.
[^219]: Not included in the above text, but available in Manuscript in Adyar D. X. 223.
[^220]: Mudgala. p. 3.

[]
The author states that the term should be taken to mean *ayogavyavaccheda* and not *anyayogavyavaccheda*. This seems to have been a much debated point in scholarly circles during the author's time. Scholars like Śrī Kṛṣṇa Tātārya Svāmī (better known as Tirupputkuḻi Svāmī), Śrī Kapiṣṭhalam Deśikācārya and Śrīraṅgam Śrīmad Āṇḍavan Svāmī seem to have concurred with the author in this regard; but some of his Tennācārya colleagues disagreed with this viewpoint. Hence the author penned the work *Tatkratunyāyasāra*, which is an epilogue to his *Tārārthasāra* and *Prabhā*.

The *Tatkratunyāyasāra* is a metrical composition in fifty verses in *sragdharā* metre similar to the *Adhikaraṇasārāvalī* of Vedāntadeśika. The style, however, is not as simple as Deśika's. In this later work, the author sets at rest the opinion of his scholarly colleague who feels that Rāmānuja in his *Śrībhāṣya*, *śarīre bhāvādhikaraṇa* (III. 3, 52), meant only the *upāsyaguṇa*.[^221] But Vedāntadeśika states in his *Rahasyatrayasāra*[^222] that *evakāra* should be taken to mean the *upāsita-guṇas* viz. *apahatapāpmā, vijara, vimṛtyu, viśoka, vijighatsa, apipāsa, satyakāma* and *satyasaṅkalpa*. The *Chāndogya* text (III,14,7) reads as follows:

`यथाक्रतुरस्मिन् लोके पुरुषो भवति तथेतः प्रेत्य भवति।`

[^221]: See *Śrībhāṣya*. vol. II. p. 523– `तस्मात् प्रत्यगात्मा प्राप्यकार एव अनुसन्धेयः।`
[^222]: 2 See p. 153.

[]
The *pratyagātmā* is *upāsyabhūta parabrahma śarīra* and hence the qualities that are meditated upon will be acquired later, but not to the exclusion of the other qualities that are natural to the *jīva*.

`उपासितानां गुणादेर्यां प्राप्तावप्यबहिष्क्रिया।`
`सा तत्क्रतुनयग्राह्या नाकारान्तवर्जनम्॥`[^223]

The author refers to his work *Tārārthasāra* in vv. 2, 17, 30, 46 and 50.

The following *śloka* v. 11 elucidates the author's stand:

`मुक्ते नभस्युदस्तात् क्रतुनयबलातोऽपि युदस्तान् बभाषे`
`तस्मिद्भिः तत्क्रतुर्केरितानिरवनाथत्यपादात्र साध्या।`
`उक्ता योग्यामुदासे प्रकृतिरहितचिन्मात्रमुख्यत्वभाजे`
`प्राप्तौ ब्रह्मानवाप्यं क्रतुनयनिमाज्जिह्वलेप्यत्वभङ्गात्॥`
...
`एवं श्रुत्या तु या या फलति परमृतिः साऽपरोपास्यनूना-`
`कारित्वेत्यथसिद्धिः क्वचिदसति परोपासने न्यूनता का॥` (12)

Hence only the *śuddharūpāṣṭaka jīva* has to be contemplated upon. The eight qualities of the *jīva* are contextual and are neither redundant nor synonymous. There is variety of choice in the qualities to be contemplated depending on the desire of the devotee (*upāsaka*). The author quotes time and again from the *Śrībhāṣya* and Vedāntadeśika's *Tattvatīkā* to prove his point that the *jīva* has to be contemplated only as *phalagavisayātirūpa*. i.e., as pure (*amala*). He refutes the views of Naiyāyikas (vv. 36 and 39 - *pāṣāṇakalpa mokṣa*). According to one alternative, is *jñātṛtva* natural to the *jīva*, or is it

[^223]: *Rahasyatrayasāra*, p. 153.

[]
what one experiences like *prāṇa* (v. 38)? But this *jñātṛtva* is the result of *indriyas* (v. 43) and hence this alternative has to be rejected. In v. 39 the author states that *pūrvapakṣins* have only gained in unnecessarily creating an apparent discord between Rāmānuja and Vedāntadeśika (*muniyugakalaha*). So, the author categorically states in v. 42 :

`तस्मा ज्ज्वरीभावधिकाणफलितं निर्मलात्मरूपे`
`ध्येयत्वं नो विशिष्यापहतदुरितलादिरूपे तथालम्।`

In vv. 44,45 and 46 he again states that the interpretation of *anyayogavyavaccheda* ascribed to Rāmānuja is not correct. He states in v. 48 that those who meditate on the *pañcāgni-vidyā* also attain liberation even like those who perform any other *upāsanā* and become equal in all respects to the Lord with the exception of *lokavyāpāra*.
