He raises a pertinent question as to whether after attaining liberation, *upāsanā* comes to an end, but answers immediately that *upāsanā* continues even in the state of *mokṣa* in the form of *kaiṅkarya* to Bhagavān and Bhāgavatas. In the concluding verse, the author states that he has written this work in Śrīperumbūdūr having sipped (mastered) the essence of *Tatkratunyāyasāra* from his earlier *ācāryas* (*cuḷukitam*).

The verse numbers given here are in accordance with the numbers given in the available manuscript. However the first three verses and the last two verses are not numbered in the manuscript. This work brings to light the

[]
great veneration the author had for his *ācāryas* and his incapacity to bear any misinterpretations of their works or any divergence in their views.

***Sthūṇāliṅgavinirṇayaḥ***

This is a poetical piece in 16 verses justifying the usuage of the word *sthūṇā* in feminine gender by Vedāntadeśika in his *Daśāvatārastotra* (v.5).

`या काचित् सहसा महासुरगृहस्थूणा पितामह्यभूत्`

According to the critic, the word *sthūṇa* is only neuter in gender. But in the *Daśāvatāravyākhyāna*,[^224] two explanations are given:
(a) the word *sthūṇā* added to the single word *gṛha* becomes neuter by the *sūtra, gṛha-śaśābhyam klībe* (b) In the *sūtra* (I-22) *gṛha-śaśābhyam klībe* it is stated that though *gṛhasthūṇa* is *nityanapuṁsaka*, according to *śalākā strīyāṁ nityam* (I-34) the word *nithya* indicates optionality of the femine gender elsewhere. The relevant verse 10 reads as follows:[^225]

`यत्र स्थूणाया प्राग् गृहपदघटना स्यात् तदा क्लीबतैव`
`प्राग्न्नं स्वामिशब्दात्परपदघटितं प्राक्पुरं स्युपयोगि।`
`पश्चात् स्वाम्यन्वये तु प्रकृतगृहपदार्थान्वयः पारिषिकः स्यात्`
`स्थूणो साक्षाच्च पल्युं न स भवति ततः सुष्ठु नः सर्वसिद्धिः॥`

[^224]: 1 p. 21.
[^225]: 2 p. 130.

[]
Concluding the work he states that he has written `this` in Tiruvahindrapuram and pays his salutations to Vedāntadeśika –

`जयति निगमचूडार्यशिष्यदिव्यजनम्यनुतिः।`
`जयति रमानृगराड्यसुरगृहस्थूणायशस्स्तंजननीकः॥`

***Nyāyasiddhāñjanakārikāvimarsanam***

This work in 19 verses elucidates the meaning contained in the following *śloka* occuring in the *Jīvapariccheda* of Vedānta Deśika's *Nyāyasiddhāñjana*:

`इयं केवललक्ष्मीशोपायत्वप्रख्यातिरूपिका।`
`स्वहेतुत्वधियं रुन्धे किं पुनः सहकारिणाम्॥`

In this track, the author criticises the interpretation offered to this *kārikā* by some, to the effect that surrender (*śaraṇāgati*) cannot be the bestower of all the desired fruits. Referring to Kūreśa's *Varadarājastava* (v. 88) he explains that the term *sva* in the *kārikā* should be taken to mean *prapannāya* and not *prapattaye*. The relevant verse in the Jīyar's *vimarśanam* reads as under:-

`इत्थं चात्र स्वशब्दः परिमृशति पराधीनकर्तृप्रपन्नं`
`स्वाधीनश्रीशताम्प्राप्त्यहमवधरणं तुल्यमेवोपहन्यात्।`
`वैधी न्यासात्मधीस्तु स्वयतनविघिप्राप्तिकेत्युक्तवत् यत्`
`तद्रूपस्वोपरोधं वदति रुधिरय ज्रीर्हि सङ्कल्पगर्भा॥`

[]
That *prapatti* cannot be the bestower of fruits is negated by the author in v. 19, wherein he states that the very act of surrender is not merely the surrender of body and soul, but the surrender of even one's knowledge that one is the agent of any action. So, this total self-effacement itself is capable of generating all fruits (*akhilaphala*).

The author concludes by stating that he has written this commentary in Śrīperumbūdūr and prays that Lord Nṛsiṁha be pleased with his work.

***Ādeśamaṇi with commentary Kaustubha***

This work in 38 *sragdharā* verses explains the formation of the word *ādeśa* found in the *Chāndogya* passage *uta tamādeśamaprākṣayaḥ*. Advaitins derive the word *ādeśa* by adding the suffix *ghañ* to the root *diś* in the sense of the object (*karmaṇi*) or the instrument (*karaṇa*). Thus according to them *ādeśaḥ* means that which is arrived at through instruction (*upadeśagamyaḥ*) or a sentence which conveys an instruction (*upadeśātmakam vākyam*).

But, Śrī Rāmānuja takes this word in the sense of 'one who commands' in the lines of the *Śruti* sentences - *antaḥ praviṣṭaḥ śāsthā janānām*[^226] and *praśāsitāram sarveṣām*[^227]. It follows that the word *ādeśaḥ* according to Rāmānuja is derived from the root *diś* by adding the suffix *ghañ* in the sense

[^226]: *Kaivalya*. v. 10.
[^227]: *Manu*. xii. 212.

[]
of agent (*kartari*) by applying the rule, *padarujaviśaspṛśo ghañ* etc., through *yogavibhāga*.

The present work *Ādeśamaṇi* along with its commentary *Kaustubha* was written to refute the derivations given to the word *ādeśa* by one Bhāradvāja Raṅgācārya in his work *Ādeśakaumudī*.[^228] The author had earlier written a work *Gomālā* (which is not extant now) to refute the work *Ādeśakaumudī*. But, later because it was rather difficult to be comprehended by the less learned, the author took upon himself the task of writing the above work with its commentary. The author's scholarship and erudition are well reflected in this presentation. His mastery of Sanskrit grammar is also well marked. His interest to interpret the correct meanings intended by earlier *ācāryas* and his large-heartedness in writing in simpler language so as to cover larger audience is certainly to be commended.

***Dāsadāsīsamarthanī***

This work is in 10 verses, justifying the expression *tvaddāsadāsīgaṇaḥ* found in v. 1 of Yāmuna's *Catuślokī*. A few objections were raised by the critics to the effect that –
a) there should be *ekaśeṣa* compound according to Pāṇini's rule. *pumān striyā* (I-2-67) and

[^228]: 1 p. 29.

[]
b) the usage should be *dāsīdāsam* according to *gaṇapāṭha* of the *sūtra "gavāśvaprabhṛtīni"*(II.4-11). The author justifies the usuage of the compound *dāsadāsī* according to Pāṇini's grammatical rules to the effect that *ekaśeṣa* is not compulsory. The relevant v. 6 is quoted below.

`किञ्चाश्रेयत्यधीतत्वन्नियमव्यावर्त्यरूपं गणे`
`दासीदासपदेऽपि तुल्यनयतो वाच्यं हि तस्सिद्धये।`
`इन्द्रादिं प्रतिलोमरूपमतुलन्यायाश्रयेद् अन्यथा`
`सद्बोधो नियमस्य वाच्य इति तद् द्वन्द्वोऽत्र भाष्यज्ञपः॥`

The author refers to the *Śrībhāṣya* and *Catuślokī Vyākhyāna* of Śrī Vedāntadeśika to prove his point. The author's mastery of Sanskrit grammar and his interest to convey the correct meaning intended by Rāmānuja and Yāmuna is perceptible. The author concludes by paying his obeisance to Yāmunayogivarya and Rāmānuja.

***Makārarakṣā***

This work is also in 10 verses, and explains the last syllable *m* of the *praṇava "*om*" which according to the Śrīvaiṣṇava Ācāryas refers to the individual soul (*jīva*). In the *Mūlamantrādhikāra* of *Śrīmad Rahasya-trayasāra*, Vedāntadeśika explains that the term "*ma*" is derived from the root "*man*" in the sense of "to know"- *mana jñāne: mān māne* (to measure) *māsi parimāṇe* (to measure) *manu avabodhane* (to understand). In all these instances, *m* alone remains after effecting the *tilopa*.

[]
Now the objection is to the usage of *makāra* at the end of the word instead of *nakāra* by the grammatical rule *mo no dhātoḥ* (VIII.2. 64). The present track tries to answer the objections by resorting to the rule *uṇādayo bahulam* (III. 3. 1). The author states that this objection can be refuted even by resorting to the rule - *chandasi dṛṣṭānuvidhiḥ* and objection can be brushed aside by saying that it is *cāndhasaprayoga*. But the author's intention was to answer the objection in the traditional manner, grammatically, and hence the necessity of writing this piece. Once again, the author's proficiency in Sanskrit grammar is well-established.

***Sthemadarpaṇaḥ***

This work in prose is devoted to justify the usuage of the word *sthema* found in the opening verse of the *Śrībhāṣya* –

`अखिलभुवनजन्मस्थेमभङ्गादिलिेले`

According to some critics *sthema* is ungrammatical. As a matter of fact, the word *sthema* was used by Vācaspatimiśra in his commentary *Vidhiviveka* on *Nyāyakaṇikā* thus - *bhuvanabhavanasthemadhvaṁsa* etc. Murāri in his *Anargharāghava* (VI. 36) also used it *niḥsthemāno daśānanakīrtayaḥ* in the sense of 'maintenance'.

But the author takes recourse to grammar, and justifies the usage of the word *sthema*

[]
by
a) deriving it from the word *sthira*,
b) resorting to the word *sthāma* to which a suffix is added and
c) by adding the suffix *imanic* to the verb *sthā* under the rule *uṇādayo bahulam*.

The author concludes this treatise by paying his homage to Rāmānuja, Patañjali and Vedāntadeśika using alluring alliterative style.

`पतञ्जली नित्यकृताञ्जलिः स्यामपाकृतक्वान्तवाचोदोषि।`
`योगेन शब्देन च वैष्णकेन प्रेम्णा भुवि स्थेमकृति द्विजिह्वै॥`
- - -
`जयति निगमान्तधूरिर्वतिपतिवाणी सुधोरणी जयति।`
`जयति फणितिः पुराणी सर्वमस्येमधारीणी जयति॥`

The concluding verse reads as under –

`गोपालसूर्यशिष्यसोभानमेधापरिखराद्विराजिताम्।`
`स्थेमाधिवादपदमर्पणेन जीवाचिरं श्रीनृहरेः पदाब्जे॥`

In the appendix, the Svāmī's *vaibhava* containing biographical details and his composition is presented in 30 *ślokas*.

In the foregoing pages, a brief analysis has been attempted of the work of Piḷḷaippākkam Svāmī, His Holiness the 37th pontiff of the Śrī Ahobila Maṭha. The depth of meaning enshrined in his works, his mastery over the Sanskrit grammar, his well-grounded erudition and scholarship and his devotion to *ācārya sūktis* are evident in his compositions.

[]
The above study affords a glimpse into the philosophical and literary contributions of the Jīyars of Śrī Ahobila Maṭha to the cause of Śrīvaiṣṇavism. This selective study, it is hoped, will generate an interest into making an indepth study of the several individual works of the Jīyars.

---

[]
## CONCLUSION


In the foregoing chapters, the contribution of the Jīyars of Śrī Ahobila Maṭha has been studied from the view-points of philosophy, religion, literature and society. In fact all these constitute different facets of an integral whole. To the man of intellect, the philosophical interpretations and the commentaries on the *grantha-catuṣṭaya* afford food for thought; to the man of religion, the *arcā* worship of Śrī Mālola Nṛsiṁha, the *dolotsavas* of Lord Kṛṣṇa conducted at various individual residences and the daily religious schedule of the pontifical head, afford a veritable feast to the eyes and heart alike; to the man of letters, the "*Mālola Vidvat Sadas*" (scholarly assemblies) conducted annually, as also during special occasions, the arguments and counter-arguments put forth by erudite scholars and the Jīyar 's *samādhānams* are a treat to the ears and mind alike: and, to the society at large, the head of the Ahobila monastic order is not a total recluse, but very much a society-personage, involved in the rejuvenation of society. The Jīyar 's heart goes out to the suffering humanity and he is ever ready, like the Lord Himself, to alleviate their suffering by teaching them the easiest way to salvation viz., surrender (*śaraṇāgati*) which requires the mammoth mental attitude viz., supreme confidence (*mahāviśvāsa*) in the salvic power of the Lord.

The Jīyar is also well aware of the current affairs of the state and the country as is evidenced by his grant of Rs. 50,000 to the Andhra Pradesh

[]
Chief Minister's Cyclone Relief Fund on November 20th 1996.[^229] Further, the Jīyar has aslo asked all the branches of the Ahobila Maṭha in the country and also his disciples to provide succour to the suffering. This indeed is the very spirit of Śrīvaiṣṇavism namely, the inability to bear the suffering of others (*paraduḥkha asahiṣṇutva*).

By leading an exemplary life of detatched attachment, performing his daily and ordained duties, the pontifical head is setting standards to humanity and is showing the way in which to lead one's life according to one's *varṇa* and *āśrama*. By performing *pañcasaṁskāras* and accepting *bharanyāsa*, he is discharging his duty ordained by Lord Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha Himself and is thus, carrying on the six-century old tradition commencing from Śrī Ādi Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa, the first Jīyar.

The Jīyar lends a helping hand in the renovation of old and dilapidated temples (*punaruddhāraṇa*) seeing to it that there is no cessation of daily worship to the *arcā* idols in these temples. Donations in the form of valuable ornaments to the presiding deities in many temples are also made. To cite a recent instance, on the eve of the Jīyar 's 70th birthday (November 22, 1996), a diamond studded "Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha Padakam" costing about

[^229]: To quote from the Indian daily "The Hindu" dated 21st November 1996. p.4. The Jīyar appealed that "every citizen of India, irrespective of caste, creed and religion, should come forward for the rescue of the people who are badly affected and have lost everything that belonged to them, including their kith and kin in the tragic devastation that shook the entire nation".

[]
Rs. 2 lakhs was donated to the temple authorities at Tirumala to adorn the presiding deity, Lord Śrīnivāsa.

Further, the Maṭha plays an important role in the training of the temple priests (*arcakas*) and in educating them to be cultured and devoted in their service to the Lord. Vedic knowledge must be made available to the young and love for the highest moral virtues must be cultivated. From this view-point, the contribution of the Jīyar of Iñjimeḍu in setting up a *Vedapāṭhaśālā* at Madhurāntakam is very significant; and up to this day, it is fulfilling the purpose creditably. Students are enrolled at a very tender age and are imparted the study of *Vedas* and *Divyaprabandham* alike. This is how the *Ubhayavedānta* tradition is carried down the centuries.

The Maṭha provides *sat-saṅga*, i.e. company of practising spiritual personalities who have perfected their lives in the light of the Divine inflow and persence. To be in their company is to undergo a transformation as it were. Thus, the Maṭha offers opportunities for the making of the saints through *sat-sampradāya* i.e. holy presence and worship and caters to the demands of all persons who are anxious to have the blessings of a spiritual life and opportunities of receiving the love of God in abundance.

As a matter of fact, the basic priniciples of one's religion should not be surrendered but should be restated, with a special reference to the needs of a more complex and changing social order. It is in this context that the Maṭha is

[]
becoming more and more relevant to modern times. Religion is often misunderstood to be the outer practices, routine rituals and creeds unique to a particular culture. Even those who attempt to understand and follow their religion often get confused because they find it difficult to rationalise the beliefs and practices. Religious plurality is an undeniable fact and harmony should be the goal of all religions. Mankind today stands at the cross-roads of civilization, where on the one hand man is reaping the fruits of science and technology ushered in by the Industrial Revolution and on the other, he is searching for inner peace by tracing his cultural roots through religion. India has had a long cultural tradition and perhaps one of the earliest civilizations, the Vedic had integrated science and religion with success. In this mobile social order when there is inter-cultural rapport between continents, it is imperative that the enlightened pontifical heads initiate measures to educate the masses by creating awareness about the time-tested Vedic injunctious such as *satyam vada, dharmam cara* and so on, and focus on the grave consequences of neglecting these values which are essential for the very survival of mankind. The younger generation has to be taught that there is an inextricable connection between science and religion, though their methods are antithetical i.e. reason versus revelation.

All our Vedānta schools accept logic and their philosophies are substantiated and tempered by reason. It has now become imperative that the subtle concepts of Vedānta be communicated in a way relevant to the modern

[]
generation. Our concept of *Sanātana Dharma* is scientific and has withstood the test of time. Though the need for religious harmony has been proclaimed by the enlightened in every generation, religious differences continue to create discord within society and between nations. To root out this problem and foster religious tolerence, fanaticism should be eradicated. The world would lose its vitality if one creed absorbed another. Variety is the spice of life and hence a rich harmony and not colourless uniformity is the ideal to be aimed for. Intellectualism has a tendency to separate the dissimilar and shut them up in different compartments, but , higher intuition takes note of the natural differences in all spheres and seeks to combine them into an integrated whole. S. Radhakrishnan[^230] states "The half-religious and the irreligious fight about dogmas and not the truly religious.... and the more religious we grow, the more tolerant of diversity shall we become". Hence it is that a pontifical head is ideally suited to achieve this spirit of unity in diversity (each fulfilling its function and all directed by the force of the Divine to achieve the most exquisite harmony). It is indeed by performing this duty that a *Maṭhādhipati* can fulfill the heartfelt desire of Vedāntadeśika –

`परस्परहितैषिणां परिसरेषु मां वर्तय।`[^231]
"Let me reside in the vicinity of those who desire mutual welfare".

[^230]: *Hindu View of Life*, George Allen and Unwin, London, 1960, p. 44.
[^231]: *Abhītistava*, v. 28.

[]
Any research is not an end in itself. Infact it should be a beginning and should open up new *vistas* for further research and study. In this aspect, the present study, it is hoped, can encourage comparative study of the other Śrīvaiṣṇava Maṭhas, a study of the contribution of Piḷḷaippākkam Jīyar (37th Pontiff) to Śrīvaiṣṇavism and the preparation of a Critical Edition of Śrī Nārāyaṇa Muni's *Rahasyatrayajīvātu*. Efforts should also be made by aspiring young scholars to trace some of the valuable works of the Pontiffs which are mere names to us.

--- , ---

[]
